Body `{"text":"<message>"}`; validates `{windowId}` (`parseWindowID`, `400`) + non-empty/decodable text (`400`), then re-resolves the target pane server-side (extended `resolveWindowChat` ‚Üí `sessions.ResolveChatPane` also returns the `PaneID` ‚Äî active-pane-first rollup, client supplies no pane/ref; `FetchSessions` fail ‚Üí `500`, no-chat ‚Üí `404`). Injection (discrete provider-agnostic `injectChatMessage` seam, v1 no provider branch): baseline `CapturePane` ‚Üí `set-buffer -b rk-chat-send -- <text>` ‚Üí `paste-buffer -d -p -t <paneID>` ‚Üí **NOVELTY echo probe** (needle occurrence count must strictly INCREASE vs the pre-paste baseline; multiline paste-collapse chip counted only for multiline; fails closed) ‚Üí `send-keys -t <paneID> Enter` ONLY on probe success. Probe failure ‚Üí structured `409` (Enter withheld, pasted text left recoverable in the composer, retry-hint against duplication); tmux subprocess fail ‚Üí `500`; success `200 {"ok":true}`. Busy policy Allow + probe (NO `agentState` gate, NO queue ‚Äî Constitution II). Concurrency: per-`(server,paneID)` whole-sequence mutex + a nested global set‚Üípaste mutex for the shared named buffer; ONE shared context deadline (`chatSendTotalBudget` 4s) threads all subprocesses (route under the 5s rule). The generic `POST /api/windows/{windowId}/keys` is left untouched. See [chat](chat.md) ¬ß Send Path |
| `/api/directories` | GET | Server-side directory listing for autocomplete ‚Äî `?prefix=~/code/wvr` returns matching dirs under `$HOME` |
| `/api/sessions/:session/upload` | POST | File upload ‚Äî session from URL path (not form field). Multipart with `file` field, optional `window` field (defaults to `"0"`). Resolves project root via `ListWindows`, writes to `.uploads/{timestamp}-{name}`, auto-manages `.gitignore`. 50MB limit. Returns `200 {"ok":true,"path":"..."}` |
| `/ws/state` | GET (WS) | **State socket** ‚Äî one `gorilla/websocket` connection per browser tab multiplexes ALL session-state + host-metrics streams that previously rode per-server + `?metrics=1` SSE connections (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`, replacing the retired `GET /api/sessions/stream`). JSON text-frame envelope protocol, `serverFromRequest`-agnostic (no `?server=` ‚Äî the socket carries no server in the URL; subscriptions name servers in-band). `handleStateWS` (`api/state_ws.go`) upgrades via the shared `upgrader`, reads a mandatory first `hello` frame, replays the six cached global slots, then a read loop dispatching `subscribe`/`unsubscribe`/`preview-scope` while a per-connection writer pump drains the send channel. The whole event catalogue, cached-slot replay, per-server poll-set membership, metrics-only cadence, and the `gone` reap live under ¬ß State Socket below (the former ¬ß SSE Hub, refactored to the socket edge ‚Äî the producer machinery is untouched). **Why WS not muxed SSE**: an established WebSocket holds NO slot in the browser's 6-per-origin HTTP/1.1 pool in any engine (spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`), so consolidating state streams onto it clears the pool starvation that blocked terminal-relay handshakes on Firefox/WebKit for plaintext origins; in-band subscribe frames are also totally ordered with the events they gate, structurally killing the POST-vs-stream race class and the `attachServer`‚ÜíSSE race. GET/read-only (¬ßIX) |
| `/ws/terminals` | GET (WS) | **Terminals socket** ‚Äî one `gorilla/websocket` connection per browser tab muxing ALL pane relay streams that previously rode per-pane `/relay/{windowId}` connections (`260717-803u-relay-mux`, replacing the retired `GET /relay/{windowId}` + `handleRelay`). `handleTerminalsWS` (`api/terminals_ws.go`) upgrades via the shared `upgrader`, then runs a read loop dispatching binary `[u32 BE streamId][payload]` data frames (routed to the addressed stream's PTY) and JSON control ops (`open`/`resize`/`close`) while a single writer goroutine schedules every stream's output ‚Äî control/short frames ahead of bulk, round-robin across streams ‚Äî through the per-stream bounded queues. Each stream reproduces the retired `handleRelay` (validate ‚Üí `ResolveWindowSession` ‚Üí session-scoped `SelectWindowInSession` ‚Üí `forceTERM` + best-effort `ReloadConfig` ‚Üí `pty.StartWithSize` at the open op's cols/rows); a stream-level failure emits a `closed` control event (4004/4001) WITHOUT closing the socket. No `?server=` in the URL (the server rides each `open` op). GET/read-only (¬ßIX). Full protocol + write-path scheduler live under ¬ß Terminal Relay below |
| `/api/preview-scope` | POST | Declare a state-socket connection's expanded-session set for tile-grid pane previews (`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`). `handlePreviewScope` (`api/preview.go`) decodes `{conn, expanded[]}` (body bounded at 64 KiB via `io.LimitReader`; malformed ‚áí `400`, empty `conn` ‚áí `400`), resolves the server via `serverFromRequest`, calls `s.initSSEHub()` (a scope POST may race ahead of the first subscribe on a fresh server) then `s.sseHub.setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)`, returns `200 {"ok":true}`. A `conn` matching no live connection is a silent no-op `200`. **RETAINED alongside an in-band twin** (`260716-qf3j-state-socket`, decision D4): the state socket's own `preview-scope` op (see ¬ß State Socket) addresses the SAME connection by its own `hello` conn id via the same `normalizeConnID` semantics and calls the SAME `setPreviewScope`, so the HTTP endpoint stays zero-regression while the frontend now sends preview-scope in-band (no POST-races-the-stream window). The set is per-connection, in-memory only (Constitution II ‚Äî dropped on disconnect), and bounds which windows the poll captures. POST per Constitution ¬ßIX; CORS `AllowedMethods` stays `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]`. See ¬ß Session-Tile Previews |
| `/api/tmux/reload-config` | POST | Reload tmux config ‚Äî server from `?server=` param (default `"default"`). Runs `source-file` on the specified server. Returns `200 {"status":"ok"}` |
| `/api/status/refresh` | POST | **Composing on-demand refresh of BOTH PR pollers** (`260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`; superseded `POST /api/pr-status/refresh` ‚Äî a single-poller synchronous handler whose sole frontend consumer, `PrStatusLine`, had zero live sites). `handleStatusRefresh` (`api/status_refresh.go`) kicks the viewer-wide collector (`prstatus.Collector.RefreshNow` ‚Äî supplies the merged state via its URL-keyed join) AND the branch refresher (`prstatus.DefaultBranchRefresher.RefreshNow` ‚Äî covers the sibling case: a just-opened PR appearing on a window, a 30s wait today). **Naming is "status", not "pane"**: "pane" collides with the tmux-pane meaning in this codebase; "status" matches the established vocabulary (status pyramid, StatusDot). **Non-blocking `202` via a DETACHED goroutine**: the two refreshes run on a `context.WithTimeout(context.Background(), statusRefreshTimeout=60s)` context (NOT `r.Context()`, which dies the moment the handler returns) ‚Äî the branch pass is one `gh pr list` per registered pair and can exceed the 5s handler-blocking cap (`code-review.md`), so the 202-then-detach shape keeps the handler well under it (the exact detached pattern mirrors `api/waiting_push.go`). **Single frequency choke point** (so ANY trigger ‚Äî button-mashing, multiple tabs, future auto-triggers ‚Äî is safe to over-fire): (a) **coalescing** ‚Äî if a forced refresh is in flight, no second refresh starts; (b) **min-interval throttle** ‚Äî a call arriving within `statusRefreshMinInterval=10s` of the last refresh starts nothing. **Tri-state 202 body (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`)**: started, coalesced, AND throttled calls ALL still return `202` and are all still fire-and-forget (the body is NEVER the completion signal ‚Äî fresh data and completion both arrive over SSE, see below), but the body now REPORTS which fate applied so the client can give honest per-status feedback ‚Äî `202 {"status":"started"}` (a new pass began; a `status-refresh` completion event will follow), `202 {"status":"coalesced"}` (a pass is already in flight; ITS completion event will follow), or `202 {"status":"throttled"}` (nothing started; NO event will come). `startStatusRefresh()` returns a small named `refreshOutcome` string type (`refreshStarted`/`refreshCoalesced`/`refreshThrottled`) instead of the former `bool` ‚Äî the started/coalesced/throttled distinction was already computed internally under the mutex and is now surfaced rather than collapsed; `handleStatusRefresh` launches the detached goroutine ONLY on `refreshStarted` and writes `{"status": string(outcome)}`. **Completion broadcast**: `finishStatusRefresh()` (which runs exactly once per completed pass, at the end of the detached goroutine, after clearing the in-flight flag) calls `s.sseHub.broadcastStatusRefresh(s.now())` guarded by `if s.sseHub != nil` (the hub is lazy-initialized on the first SSE connection and absent in the direct-`&Server{}` handler tests, so the nil-guard is required) ‚Äî this is the once-per-pass structural guarantee that a coalesced/throttled POST (which starts no goroutine) emits no extra completion event. The two kicks are **injectable seams** on `api.Server` (`refreshCollectorFn`/`refreshBranchFn` function fields, defaulted in `NewRouterAndServer`, mirroring the collector-injection house pattern), and the coalesce/throttle state (`refreshStatusMu sync.Mutex`, `refreshStatusInFlight bool`, `refreshStatusLast time.Time`) plus a `nowFn func() time.Time` clock seam live per-server so handler tests assert both kicks fire ‚Äî and drive the started/coalesced/throttled paths deterministically ‚Äî without spawning `gh` or real sleeps (`startStatusRefresh`/`finishStatusRefresh` helpers; `s.now()` also stamps the broadcast `completedAt` so it is test-controllable). The collector kick nil-guards `s.prStatus` (a partially-wired test router has no collector ‚Äî no panic, branch kick still fires). Server-independent (both pollers are global, not per-`?server=`). POST per Constitution ¬ßIX (additive body + SSE event only ‚Äî no new endpoint, no new verb); the CORS `AllowedMethods` allowlist stays `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]` |
| `/api/riff` | POST | **Web-UI agent spawn** (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`; dialog-v2 fields `260714-q9cg-spawn-agent-dialog-mockup`) ‚Äî surfaces the extracted `internal/riff` engine (worktree + tmux window + agent launcher; full engine in [rk-riff](rk-riff.md)). `handleRiffSpawn` (`api/riff.go`): `?server=<name>`, JSON body `{task?, preset?, session, where?, worktreeName?, tier?}` (the last three are additive over the shipped body ‚Äî `where` ‚àà `""`/`worktree`/`checkout` (default `worktree`), `worktreeName` names the worktree in worktree mode, `tier` picks the fab agent tier). Validates `session` via `validate.ValidateName`, then the **v2 fields BEFORE deriving the repo root / touching any subprocess** (constitution ¬ßI ‚Äî nothing created on a 400): an unknown `where` ‚Üí `400`; a non-empty `worktreeName` **with `where="checkout"`** ‚Üí `400` (it has no meaning); a non-empty `worktreeName` ‚Üí `validate.ValidateWorktreeName` (`400`); a non-empty `tier` ‚Üí `validate.ValidateTier` (`400`). It then **derives the repo root** from the target session's active-pane cwd (see ¬ß Riff Repo-Root Derivation below), returning `400` (nothing created) on a non-repo/empty cwd or a session-read failure. On a valid repo it calls `s.riff.Spawn(ctx, riff.Options{server, session, repoRoot, task, preset, where, worktreeName, tier})` (count fixed at 1) and returns `200 {"server","session","window","windowId"}` ‚Äî enough for the client to navigate to `/$server/$window` (the sidebar row arrives via the existing SSE stream; no new SSE work). An unknown-preset engine error (`riff.ExitCodeError{Code: ExitValidation}`) maps to `400`; any other engine failure maps to `500`. **Synchronous handler with a documented 5s-rule exception** ‚Äî the aggregate `wt create` (30s build-class) + tmux (‚â§10s each) + `fab agent [tier] --print` (10s) MAY exceed the 5s tmux-blocking review rule; each individual subprocess keeps its own bound, and the exception is documented in a comment at the handler. Task text reaches tmux only through the engine's escaped `buildSkillShellString` seam (Constitution ¬ßI). Uses a dedicated `context.Background()`-derived timeout for both the repo-root `ListWindows` (`riffRepoRootTimeout = 5s`) and the engine spawn (`riffSpawnTimeout = 90s`) ‚Äî NOT `r.Context()` ‚Äî so a client disconnect never truncates a half-created worktree. POST per Constitution ¬ßIX |
| `/api/riff/presets` | GET | **Riff preset + tier preflight** (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`; `tiers` added `260714-q9cg-spawn-agent-dialog-mockup`; `tiers` fab-gated `260714-gsmu-spawn-dialog-tier-gate-sidebar-entry`) ‚Äî `handleRiffPresets` (`api/riff.go`): `?server=&session=`, validates `session` (`400`), derives the repo root exactly as `POST /api/riff` does, reads `fabconfig.ReadPresetsOrdered(repoRoot)` and returns `200 {"presets":[{name, layout, paneCount}], "tiers":[...]}`. `presets` is in YAML source order (`layout` empty-string when unset; `paneCount` = number of preset panes; `[]` when none). **`tiers` is GATED on `fabconfig.IsFabProject(repoRoot)` (since `gsmu`)**: a fab project (`fab/project/config.yaml` present) gets `fabconfig.ReadTiers(repoRoot)` ‚Äî the union of fab-kit built-ins (`default, doing, fast, operator, review`, `default` first) and the repo's `agent.tiers` keys; a repo with **no** config is NOT a fab project and gets `tiers: []` (a non-nil empty slice so the JSON key stays `[]`, response shape additive per ¬ßIX). The rationale is honesty: in a non-fab repo every tier resolves to the same `DefaultLauncher`, so tiers would be inert noise ‚Äî the empty list drives the dialog to HIDE the Agent Tier field entirely. The **absent-vs-malformed split** is deliberate: an absent config = `[]`; a malformed-but-present config is still a fab project (`IsFabProject` true) whose `ReadTiers` falls back to the built-ins (`ReadTiers`'s own contract unchanged). The dialog still populates **both** its preset and Agent dropdowns from this **one** preflight fetch (no second endpoint, constitution ¬ßIV). A non-repo cwd / session-read failure ‚Üí `400`. Read-only GET (¬ßIX) |

| `/api/notify` | POST | Fans out a Web Push to ALL stored subscriptions. Body `{title?, body}` (empty `body` ‚Üí `400`, no send); builds the `{title, body, icon}` payload and sends each subscription via `webpush.SendNotificationWithContext` under a bounded context, pruning any subscription the push service answers `404`/`410`. | `/api/update` | POST | One-click daemon self-upgrade (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`; force flag + shared spawn seam `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `handleUpdate` (`api/update.go`). **Tolerant body parse (since `260714-3law`)**: `{"force": bool}` ‚Äî an absent body, empty body, `{}`, or even a *malformed* body all decode to `force=false` (existing clients POST `{}` and MUST keep working byte-for-byte; a decode error is swallowed, never a 400). Branches, in order: (1) resolve the daemon's own executable path via the `resolveSelfPathFn` seam (default `selfpath.Resolve` = `os.Executable`+`EvalSymlinks`) ‚Äî a resolve error is `500`; (2) `!selfpath.IsBrewInstalled(selfPath)` (no `/Cellar/run-kit/` marker) ‚Üí `409` JSON error pointing at the manual path (`update manually with `rk update`‚Ä¶ or `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit``) ‚Äî this brew 409 is **UNCONDITIONAL** (kept on the force path too, and it also covers dev builds server-side: a dev binary never lives under `/Cellar/run-kit/`); (3) **only when `!force`**: `s.updateChecker == nil || !s.updateChecker.Snapshot().Qualifies` ‚Üí `409 {"error":"no update available"}` (`force=true` SKIPS this qualify 409 ‚Äî the real "is there anything newer" decision is delegated to the idempotent `rk update`, which exits "already up to date" harmlessly when nothing newer exists, so a patch release ‚Äî which the checker never qualifies ‚Äî becomes installable from the web); (4) respond `202 {"status":"updating"}` **before** spawning, because the detached `rk update` restarts the daemon and kills THIS process; then `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, "update.log", "update")` (a spawn failure is logged only ‚Äî response already committed). **Force path is byte-identical to today except the qualify skip**; `force=false` is unchanged. The shared `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, logName, args...)` seam (see ¬ß API Server version/checker wiring ‚Üí shared spawn seam) defaults to a **detached** `exec.Command(selfPath, args...)` with `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` (own session/process group ‚Äî it must outlive the server) and stdout/stderr redirected to `~/.rk/<logName>` (via the generalized `openRkLog(logName)`, `O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` 0644, `~/.rk` mkdir'd). **Deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** ‚Äî the Constitution ¬ßI timeout rule exists to stop a hung subprocess *blocking* the server, and a detached child cannot block it; argument-slice construction + no user input still hold. **No in-flight lock** (R8): a second click while an update is in flight spawns another `rk update`, which exits harmlessly once brew reports "already up to date". POST per ¬ßIX; no `GET /api/version` (minimal surface ¬ßIV ‚Äî the running version reaches clients over the SSE `event: version` slot instead, see ¬ß SSE Hub) |
| `/api/restart` | POST | Bounce the run-kit daemon from the web (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `handleRestart` (`api/restart.go`), body ignored (client POSTs `{}`). Wraps the existing `rk daemon restart` CLI (Constitution III) so a routine restart / wedge recovery no longer needs SSH on the remote-first box. Branches: (1) **`409` when the running version is `"dev"`** (the `devVersion` sentinel, read from `s.version` ‚Äî see the restart dev guard note) ‚Äî under `just dev` the serve process is air-managed (not the daemon), so spawning `rk daemon restart` would bounce the *real* daemon out from under a dev tab; a defense-in-depth mirror of the palette-side dev gate that also stops a curl/stale-tab from doing it; (2) resolve the self path via the same `resolveSelfPathFn` seam ‚Äî resolve error is `500`; (3) respond `202 {"status":"restarting"}` **before** spawning (the detached `rk daemon restart` kills THIS process, so ‚Äî exactly like `handleUpdate` ‚Äî the client must get its response first); then `spawnSelfFn(selfPath, "restart.log", "daemon", "restart")` (spawn failure logged only ‚Äî response already committed). **NO brew requirement** (restart works for any install method) and no in-flight lock (a plain stop/start is idempotent; the daemon just released its own port). **Accepted caveat** (user-decided): if `daemon.Start()` fails after the stop, the web UI is down and SSH is needed ‚Äî a narrow accepted failure window; `~/.rk/restart.log` makes it diagnosable. POST per ¬ßIX |
| `/api/servers` | GET | List available tmux servers ‚Äî scans socket dir, returns JSON array of `{name, sessionCount, rank}` objects sorted alphabetically. Session counts AND the per-server rank (`@rk_server_rank`, `*int` ‚Üí JSON `rank: 3` / `rank: null` when unset, since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`) are computed together by the same concurrent fan-out (WaitGroup + mutex-protected results maps): each goroutine calls `tmux.ListSessions(ctx, server)` **and** `tmux.GetServerRank(ctx, server)` ‚Äî one extra tmux call per server, same concurrency pattern. Per-server `ListSessions` errors log at warn and yield `sessionCount: 0`; per-server rank-read errors log at warn and yield `rank: null` ‚Äî neither surfaces a 5xx. Empty discovery returns `[]` (not `null`). **The array order is unchanged ‚Äî still `sort.Slice` alphabetical** (an asserted API contract, `servers_test.go`); `rank` rides each entry but display ordering is composed frontend-side (see ¬ß Frontend API Client ‚Üí `compareServersRanked`) |
| `/api/servers` | POST | Create tmux server ‚Äî JSON body `{"name":"..."}`. Creates session "0" in `$HOME`. Returns `201 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/servers/order` | POST | Persist the user-defined server display order ‚Äî JSON body `{"order":["srv-a","srv-b",...]}` (since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`). `handleServerOrderPost` (`api/servers.go`) decodes with `DisallowUnknownFields` (`nil` order ‚Üí `[]`), validates EACH name via `validate.ValidateServerName` up front (`400` before any tmux write on malformed body or invalid name), then writes rank `i` to the i-th listed server via `tmux.SetServerRank` ‚Äî **best-effort per server**: one unreachable server (killed mid-reorder, momentary timeout) logs a warn and is skipped, never failing the whole request (the no-5xx fan-out stance of `handleServersList`; the next full write self-heals). On success `initSSEHub()` + `sseHub.broadcastServerOrder(order)` (server-global echo, see ¬ß SSE Hub) and returns `200 {"ok":true}`. POST per ¬ßIX; mirrors `handleSessionOrderPost` minus the GET twin (rank already rides `/api/servers`) |
| `/api/servers/kill` | POST | Kill tmux server ‚Äî JSON body `{"name":"..."}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}` |
| `/api/keybindings` | GET | Curated tmux keybindings ‚Äî runs `tmux list-keys` on `?server=`, filters through a whitelist map, returns JSON array `[{key, table, command, label}]`. Returns `[]` if server not running or on error |
| `/api/settings/theme` | GET | Returns `{"theme": "..."}` ‚Äî reads via `settings.Load()`. Returns `"system"` when no settings file exists. Not per-server (no `?server=` param) |
| `/api/settings/theme` | POST | Accepts `{"theme": "..."}` ‚Äî writes via `settings.Save()`. (Migrated PUT‚ÜíPOST by `260529-jad6` per ¬ßIX; body/response unchanged.) Returns `{"status": "ok"}` on success, `400` if theme is empty. Not per-server |
| `/api/settings/server-color` | GET/POST | Per-server color preference, stored in `~/.rk/settings.yaml` `server_colors:` (string descriptors, `internal/settings`). `GET ?server=x` ‚Üí `{"color": "1+3"\|null}`; bare `GET` ‚Üí `{"colors": {server: descriptor}}`. `POST` accepts `{"server":"...","color":"4"\|"1+3"\|null}` ‚Äî `handleSetServerColor` validates the descriptor via the shared `validate.ValidateColorValue` (`400` on malformed) then `settings.SetServerColor` (null clears). String descriptors since `260615-6rnr` (was an int `{"color":N}`; tolerant read keeps legacy int files working). Not per-`?server=` |
| `/api/boards` | GET | Lists pane boards summarized across every server returned by `tmux.ListServers(ctx)` (each board's pins are server-scoped; the list is the union of board names). Derived from `_rk-pin-*` session `@rk_board` vars (since `260602-qn62`). Returns `200 [{name, pinCount}]`; `[]` when empty (never `null`). Not per-server (no `?server=` query). **Rank-aware order (since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`)**: `tmux.ListBoards` still returns alphabetical, but `handleBoardsList` then applies the user-defined display order at the API layer via the pure `sortBoardsByStoredOrder(boards, settings.GetBoardOrder())` helper (`internal/tmux` stays settings-unaware) ‚Äî boards present in the stored order first, by their index in `~/.rk/settings.yaml` `board_order:`, then any board absent from it after them, alphabetically; stale names in the stored order (boards that no longer exist) match nothing and are ignored on read. **The response order IS the display order** for every consumer (sidebar BoardsSection, Host-page BOARDS zone, top-bar BoardSwitcher) ‚Äî there is one list source, so this is the single sort choke point: NO `rank` field is added to the summary and NO client comparator is introduced (unlike servers, which have two list sources ‚Äî see `/api/servers`). With no stored order the list stays alphabetical (unchanged behavior) |
| `/api/boards/order` | POST | Persist the user-defined board display order ‚Äî JSON body `{"order":["deploys","reviews",...]}` (the FULL ordered board-name list, since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`). `handleBoardOrderPost` (`api/boards.go`) decodes with `DisallowUnknownFields` (`nil` order ‚Üí `[]`), validates EACH name via `tmux.ValidBoardName` AND rejects a **duplicate** name ‚Äî a malformed body, an invalid name, or a duplicate is `400` before any write ‚Äî then persists the whole list via `settings.SetBoardOrder`. On success `initSSEHub()` + `sseHub.broadcastBoardOrder(order)` (server-global echo, see ¬ß SSE Hub) and returns `200 {"ok":true}`. POST per ¬ßIX; mirrors `handleServerOrderPost`. Every reorder replaces the full stored list, so stale names self-heal. Unlike `/api/boards/{name}/reorder` (a within-board PIN reorder via `@rk_board_order` fractional keys), this reorders the BOARDS THEMSELVES in the board list ‚Äî persisted host-globally in settings, scoped to no tmux server |
| `/api/boards/{name}` | GET | Returns the board's entries (one per `_rk-pin-*` session carrying this `@rk_board`) joined with live tmux window data: `[{server, windowId, session, windowIndex, windowName, orderKey, panes}]`, sorted by `orderKey`. **Response field shape unchanged** by `260602-qn62` ‚Äî `session` is now the `_rk-pin-*` pin-session, transparent to the frontend. `{name}` validated against `^[A-Za-z0-9_-]{1,32}$` (`400` on invalid). A killed pinned window's session just drops out of the live read (no stale write-back). `200 []` when no entries match the name |
| `/api/boards/{name}/pin` | POST | Pin a window to a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234"}`. Validates `name`, `server` (via `validate.ValidateName`), and `windowId` (`^@\d+$`). Returns `404` when the named window does not exist on the named server. Idempotent ‚Äî re-pinning the same window to the same board is a no-op. Returns `201 {"ok":true}` on success and broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "pin" }` on the source server's SSE stream |
| `/api/boards/{name}/unpin` | POST | Unpin a window from a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234"}`. Returns `200 {"ok":true}`. Tolerant of "entry not present" (also returns `200`). Empty board cannot exist ‚Äî when this removes the last entry, the board vanishes from `GET /api/boards`. Broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "unpin" }` |
| `/api/boards/{name}/reorder` | POST | Reorder a pin within a board. Body `{"server":"...","windowId":"@1234","before":"@5678"\|null,"after":"@9abc"\|null}`. The new `orderKey` is computed server-side via `tmux.ComputeOrderKey(beforeKey, afterKey)`; the frontend never generates keys. Returns `200 {"ok":true,"newOrderKey":"bm"}` and broadcasts `event: board-changed { change: "reorder", orderKey }` |
| `/proxy/{port}/*` | * | Reverse proxy ‚Äî forwards to `http://127.0.0.1:{port}/{path}`. Port validated (1-65535, `400` on invalid). Per-port `ReverseProxy` instances cached via `sync.Map`. Handles WebSocket upgrade transparently. `ModifyResponse` rewrites `localhost:{port}` and `127.0.0.1:{port}` references in HTML responses (`text/html` content-type) to `/proxy/{port}` paths; handles gzip-compressed responses. Non-HTML responses pass through unchanged |

**`broadcastServerOrder` ‚Äî server-global fan-out (vs. per-server `broadcastSessionOrder`)** (since `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastServerOrder(order []string)` (`api/sse.go`) alongside the existing `broadcastSessionOrder(server, order)`. The distinction is load-bearing and deliberate: **session** order is a per-server concern (which server's sidebar reorders), so `broadcastSessionOrder` fans only to that server's clients and caches per-server in `previousOrderJSON[server]`. **Server** rank order is a HOST-global concern ‚Äî a client viewing one server, or NONE (the bare `/` Host page on the `?metrics=1` sentinel stream), still needs to re-sort its whole server list ‚Äî so `broadcastServerOrder` fans to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key (exactly like the `metrics`/`services` broadcasts) and caches in a SINGLE `cachedServerOrderJSON` slot replayed to every new client in `addClient` (NOT gated on `c.server`). It normalizes a `nil` order to `[]` so the cached JSON is always `"[]"`, never `"null"`. This is why the design chose a fresh server-global event rather than reusing the per-server `session-order` shape ‚Äî the latter would neither reach `?metrics=1` clients nor fit a host-global cache.

**`broadcastBoardOrder` ‚Äî server-global fan-out (vs. per-server `broadcastBoardChanged`)** (since `260708-a2qd-board-list-reorder`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastBoardOrder(order []string)` (`api/sse.go`), a verbatim structural mirror of `broadcastServerOrder` ‚Äî a board is an emergent cross-server aggregate of `_rk-pin-*` sessions with no owning tmux server, so board **display order** is a HOST-global concern (exactly like server rank order, and unlike the per-server `board-changed` pin/unpin/reorder event which fans only to one server's clients). It fans `event: board-order` to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key (incl. the `?metrics=1` sentinel) and caches in a SINGLE `cachedBoardOrderJSON` slot replayed to every new client in `addClient` (NOT gated on `c.server`), normalizing a `nil` order to `[]` so the cached JSON is always `"[]"`, never `"null"`. Payload `{"order":[...]}`. Fired synchronously by `handleBoardOrderPost` after the `settings.SetBoardOrder` write; it deliberately does NOT reuse the per-server `board-changed` event (which is scoped to a tmux server and uncached), since an order write is host-global.

**`broadcastStatusRefresh` ‚Äî server-global, BROADCAST-ONLY (no cached slot, no replay)** (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`): the SSE hub gains `broadcastStatusRefresh(completedAt time.Time)` (`api/sse.go`), fanning `event: status-refresh` with payload `{"completedAt":"<RFC3339 UTC>"}` (`completedAt.UTC().Format(time.RFC3339)`) to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key incl. the `?metrics=1` sentinel, under `h.mu.Lock()` with the same drop-on-full `slog.Warn` debounce as its siblings. A manual PR-status refresh is a HOST-global concern (both PR pollers are process-wide, not per-`?server=`), so it fans out like `broadcastServerOrder`/`broadcastUpdateAvailable`, NOT to one server's clients like `broadcastBoardChanged`. **Unlike server-order/board-order/version/update-available it is the sole broadcast fn with NO cached slot and NO `addClient` replay case** ‚Äî a completion pulse is transient by design; a client connecting after a pass completes is NOT owed a replayed event because freshness for a late connector is surfaced independently by the StatusDotTip's "checked Xs ago" line (`PrFetchedAt`), so a missed pulse loses nothing. Emitted from `finishStatusRefresh()` (nil-guarded, once per completed pass ‚Äî see the `POST /api/status/refresh` row above); the frontend routes it through `session-context.tsx`'s `subscribeStatusRefresh` fan-out to clear the PANE-header refresh button's spinner (ui-patterns.md ¬ß WindowPanel refresh button).

**`event: version` (set-once cached slot) + `event: update-available` (broadcast + cached replay)** (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`): two more server-global cached slots on `sseHub`, both delivered to EVERY client across every `h.clients` key including the `?metrics=1` sentinel (fan-out identical to `server-order`/`board-order`), replayed on connect from `addClient` (after the server-order/board-order sends, both gated on a non-empty cached string; NOT gated on `c.server`). They differ in whether they broadcast:

- **`event: version`** ‚Äî the RUNNING daemon version (ldflags `main.version`, sentinel `"dev"` for local builds), payload `{"version":"0.5.3","boot":"<per-process id>","brew":<bool>}` (the `boot`+`brew` fields additive since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`), cached in `cachedVersionJSON`. Seeded ONCE via `sseHub.setVersion(version, boot, brew)` (called from `Server.SetVersion` after `NewRouterAndServer` ‚Äî see ¬ß API Server version/checker wiring); the running version cannot change for the process lifetime, so there is **NO broadcast path** ‚Äî it is a **replay-on-connect-only** slot (an empty version is ignored, leaving the slot empty ‚Üí no event; `boot`/`brew` ride the same set-once slot). **`boot`** is a per-process identity generated ONCE at startup (16 hex chars from `crypto/rand` via `cmd/rk`'s `newBootID`), in-memory only (Constitution II); a *fresh* boot on every daemon start is what lets a reconnecting tab detect a **same-version** restart and reload (the reconnect after a restart is exactly the signal the frontend reload guard keys on ‚Äî see ui-patterns.md ¬ß Update Notification ‚Üí Reload guard). **`brew`** is `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled` computed ONCE at startup in `serve.go` (`resolveBrewInstalled`; a resolve failure reports `false` ‚Üí the palette's brew-gated force-update entry safely stays hidden); it gates the client-side force-update palette entry. This is the sole version-exposure mechanism ‚Äî deliberately no `GET /api/version` (minimal surface ¬ßIV); the SSE connect IS the moment the client needs it.
- **`event: update-available`** ‚Äî a qualifying pending update, payload `{"current":"0.5.3","latest":"0.6.0"}`, cached in `cachedUpdateAvailableJSON`. `broadcastUpdateAvailable(current, latest)` (pattern: `broadcastBoardOrder`) marshals the payload, sets the cache, and fans the `event: update-available` frame to every client under `h.mu.Lock()` (drop-with-`slog.Warn` on a full channel). Empty until a check qualifies. Invoked via the `Checker.OnQualify` callback wired in `serve.go` (see below), so a later NEWER release re-broadcasts (the checker's re-fire gate) and a late-connecting client gets the cached slot on connect.

### Riff Engine Injection + Repo-Root Derivation (`260713-sbk1-web-spawn-agent`)

The `POST /api/riff` + `GET /api/riff/presets` handlers surface the extracted `internal/riff` spawn engine (full engine in [rk-riff](rk-riff.md)). Two seams are load-bearing:

**`RiffEngine` interface ‚Äî a DEDICATED dependency, NOT folded into `TmuxOps`** (`api/router.go`): `type RiffEngine interface { Spawn(ctx, riff.Options) (riff.Result, error) }`, injected onto the `Server` struct as a nil-safe `riff RiffEngine` field mirroring the `metrics`/`services`/`prStatus` collector-injection pattern. `riff.Options` carries `{Server, Session, RepoRoot, Task, Preset}` plus the dialog-v2 spawn-shaping fields `{Where, WorktreeName, Tier}` (since `260714-q9cg`). Production wiring is `prodRiffEngine{}` (delegates to `riff.Spawn`); tests inject a focused mock via the new `NewTestRouterWithRiff(logger, sf, ops, engine, hostname)` constructor (its recorded-inputs mock also records `Where`/`WorktreeName`/`Tier`). **Why a separate field rather than a `TmuxOps` method**: `TmuxOps`/`mockTmuxOps` are shared by every handler test, so a spawn method there would force a mock method into dozens of unrelated tests; the dedicated field keeps the blast radius to the riff handler + its own mock. `NewTestRouter` leaves `riff` nil (riff-unrelated tests never reach it).

**New-field validation is at the handler, before repo-root derivation** (since `260714-q9cg`): `handleRiffSpawn` runs the full v2 validation ladder ‚Äî `where` enum, `worktreeName`+`checkout` rejection, `validate.ValidateWorktreeName`, `validate.ValidateTier` ‚Äî **before** `deriveRepoRoot` or any subprocess, so a malformed request `400`s with nothing created (constitution ¬ßI). See the `/api/riff` endpoint row above and [rk-riff](rk-riff.md) ¬ß Security / Trust Boundary. `handleRiffPresets` additionally reads `fabconfig.ReadTiers(repoRoot)` into the response so the dialog's Agent dropdown rides the one preflight fetch ‚Äî **gated on `fabconfig.IsFabProject(repoRoot)` since `260714-gsmu-spawn-dialog-tier-gate-sidebar-entry`** (a non-fab repo, no `fab/project/config.yaml`, returns `tiers: []` so the dialog hides the Agent Tier field ‚Äî see the `/api/riff/presets` endpoint row and [rk-riff](rk-riff.md) ¬ß `IsFabProject`).

**Repo-root derivation from the target session's active pane** (`deriveRepoRoot` in `api/riff.go`, shared by both handlers): `ListWindows(ctx, session, server)` ‚Üí the active window (`IsActiveWindow`, else the first) ‚Üí that window's active pane (`PaneInfo.IsActive`, else the first pane, else the window's `WorktreePath`) ‚Üí `Cwd` ‚Üí `config.FindGitRoot`. It returns `(root, cwd, err)` so a non-repo caller can name the offending cwd in its `400`. The three no-root outcomes are distinguished: a derived-but-non-repo cwd, a session with no window/pane to derive a cwd from (the practical nonexistent-session path ‚Äî the real `ListWindows` swallows its tmux error into an empty result), and a tmux-read failure (surfaced as a `400` "does it exist?" message, since a named-session read failure is most likely a gone session, client-correctable). This uses the existing `ListWindows` surface ‚Äî no new tmux primitive ‚Äî and is session-scoped (not window-scoped) because the endpoint's spawn target is a session, not a window.

### Frontend API Client

`app/frontend/src/api/client.ts` ‚Äî typed fetch wrappers for all endpoints using POST-only mutations with path-based intent. Uses relative URLs ‚Äî works with both Vite proxy in dev and same-origin in production. Exports individual functions per endpoint:

| Function | Method | Path |
|----------|--------|------|
| `getHealth()` | GET | `/api/health` |
| `getSessions()` | GET | `/api/sessions` |
| `createSession(name, cwd?)` | POST | `/api/sessions` |
| `killSession(session)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/kill` |
| `createWindow(server, session, name, cwd?, rkType?, rkUrl?)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/windows` (session-scoped ‚Äî no window ID yet) |
| `killWindow(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/kill` |
| `moveWindow(server, windowId, targetIndex)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/move` (source by ID, body `{targetIndex}`) |
| `moveWindowToSession(server, windowId, targetSession)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/move-to-session` |
| `renameWindow(server, windowId, name)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/rename` |
| `setWindowOptions(server, windowId, options)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` ‚Äî partial-merge; `options` is `Record<string, string \| null>` (since `260529-jad6`) |
| `updateWindowUrl(server, windowId, url)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` ‚Üí `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@rk_url": url}`) |
| `updateWindowType(server, windowId, rkType)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` ‚Üí `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@rk_type": rkType === "" ? null : rkType}`). **Deletion candidate since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens`** ‚Äî that change removed both view-switch call sites (the `IframeWindow` `>_` button and the `toggle-iframe-terminal` palette action / tty-branch hint bar), so zero non-test references remain (only its own `client.test.ts` case). Kept for now; the backend `POST /options` endpoint stays regardless (shared with `updateWindowUrl`, and `@rk_type` remains legitimate substrate state an external process may set) |
| `sendKeys(server, windowId, keys)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/keys` |
| `getDirectories(prefix)` | GET | `/api/directories?prefix=...` |
| `selectWindow(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/select?server=...` |
| `splitWindow(server, windowId, horizontal, cwd?)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/split` |
| `closePane(server, windowId)` | POST | `/api/windows/{windowId}/close-pane` |
| `reloadTmuxConfig()` | POST | `/api/tmux/reload-config?server=...` |
| `uploadFile(session, file, window?)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/upload?server=...` |
| `listServers()` | GET | `/api/servers` ‚Äî returns `Promise<ServerInfo[]>` where `ServerInfo = { name: string; sessionCount: number; rank?: number \| null }` (the optional `rank`, mirroring `@rk_server_rank`, added by `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder`; `null`/absent when unset ‚Äî unranked servers sort after ranked ones). `ServerInfo` is exported alongside `listServers` from `app/frontend/src/api/client.ts`. All consumers (`SessionProvider`, `Sidebar`, `ServerPanel`, `ServerListPage`, `app.tsx` palette actions) read `.name` from each entry |
| `createServer(name)` | POST | `/api/servers` |
| `setServerOrder(order)` | POST | `/api/servers/order` ‚Äî persists the user-defined server display order (backend writes rank `i` to the i-th listed server and broadcasts server-global `event: server-order`). **Server-independent** (like `listServers`/`createServer`/`killServer`) ‚Äî the order spans the whole `/api/servers` list, not one server, so it takes NO `server` arg and hits the bare URL (no `withServer`). Added by `260705-bpnr-server-tiles-drag-reorder` |
| `killServer(name)` | POST | `/api/servers/kill` |
| `getKeybindings()` | GET | `/api/keybindings?server=...` |
| `getThemePreference()` | GET | `/api/settings/theme` |
| `setThemePreference(theme)` | POST | `/api/settings/theme` (migrated PUT‚ÜíPOST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `setServerColor(server, color)` | POST | `/api/settings/server-color` (migrated PUT‚ÜíPOST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `setWindowColor(server, windowId, color)` | POST | delegates to `setWindowOptions` ‚Üí `/api/windows/{windowId}/options` (`{"@color": color === null ? null : String(color)}`; since `260529-jad6`) |
| `setSessionColor(session, color)` | POST | `/api/sessions/:session/color` |
| `setSessionOrder(server, order)` | POST | `/api/sessions/order` (migrated PUT‚ÜíPOST by `260529-jad6`) |
| `refreshStatus()` | POST | `/api/status/refresh` ‚Äî kicks BOTH server-side PR pollers (viewer collector 90s + branch‚ÜíPR refresher 30s) on demand (`260715-jykd-manual-status-refresh`; renamed/repointed from `refreshPrStatus()` ‚Üí `/api/pr-status/refresh`). The server responds `202` immediately and runs the refreshes on a detached goroutine; refreshed statuses arrive via the SSE `sessions` stream (~2.5s cadence), never the response body. **Returns the tri-state 202 body (since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`)**: `Promise<{ status: "started" | "coalesced" | "throttled" }>` (exported `RefreshStatusOutcome` union) ‚Äî parsed from `{"status": ...}` and **defaulted to `"started"` for any unknown/missing value** (an older daemon returns the opaque `{"status":"refreshing"}`, so defaulting to `started` = spin-until-event, the safe superset). Completion is NOT the promise resolution ‚Äî it arrives as the server-global `status-refresh` SSE event; the button consumes both (branch the resolved status, then wait for the event). Server is the single frequency choke point (coalescing + min-interval throttle), so this is **safe to over-fire** ‚Äî extra calls coalesce/throttle server-side and still 202. Best-effort / fire-and-forget (a non-2xx rejects via the shared `throwOnError`; the button swallows it). Server-independent (no `?server=`). Triggered by the PANE-header refresh button (¬ß ui-patterns ‚Üí WindowPanel refresh button) and the `PR: Refresh Status` palette action |
| `triggerUpdate()` | POST | `/api/update` ‚Äî one-click daemon self-upgrade (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`). `Promise<void>`, no args, empty JSON body `{}`; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError` (so the chip/palette caller can surface the `409` reason as a toast). Server-independent (no `?server=`), plain `fetch` not `deduplicatedFetch` ‚Äî follows the `refreshStatus`/`initTmuxConf` empty-body POST-helper idiom. The server responds `202` then spawns a detached `rk update`; the ensuing daemon restart drops SSE and the reconnect's differing `event: version` drives the frontend reload guard. Imported into `session-context.tsx` and wrapped as the context `updateNow()` |
| `triggerForceUpdate()` | POST | `/api/update` with body `{"force":true}` (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `Promise<void>`, no args; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError`. Same server-independent plain-`fetch` shape as `triggerUpdate`, but the `{"force":true}` body makes the server skip the qualify 409 (keeps the brew 409), so a **patch release** ‚Äî unreachable via the qualifying-gated `triggerUpdate()` ‚Äî is installable from the web. Wrapped as the context `forceUpdateNow()`; backs the `run-kit: Update Now` palette entry |
| `triggerRestart()` | POST | `/api/restart` with empty body `{}` (`260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`). `Promise<void>`, no args; **rejects on non-2xx** via `throwOnError` (e.g. `409` on a dev build). Server-independent plain `fetch`. The server responds `202` then spawns a detached `rk daemon restart`; the reconnect's differing `boot` id (same version) drives the reload guard. Wrapped as the context `restartNow()`; backs the `run-kit: Restart Daemon` palette entry |
| `setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)` | POST | `/api/preview-scope` (via `withServer`) ‚Äî declares the SSE connection `conn`'s expanded-session set so the poll captures previews only for those windows. Body `{conn, expanded}`. Called by `SessionProvider`'s context `setPreviewScope`; best-effort (errors swallowed) (`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`) |
| `spawnRiff(server, session, opts?)` | POST | `/api/riff` (via `withServer`) ‚Äî spawns a riff agent window in `session`'s repo. Signature changed by `260714-q9cg` to an **options object** `SpawnRiffOptions = {task?, preset?, where?, worktreeName?, tier?}` (was positional `task?, preset?`). Body is built by omitting each field when unset/**default** ‚Äî `task`/`preset`/`worktreeName` when falsy, `where` when `"worktree"` (the backend default), `tier` when `"default"` (resolves the same tier as an omitted value) ‚Äî so a **defaults-only call is byte-identical to the shipped two-field body**. `where` is the typed `RiffWhere = "worktree" | "checkout"` union. Resolves the parsed `RiffSpawnResult = {server, session, window, windowId}`. Throws via `throwOnError` on a non-ok response (a `400` carries a human-readable message, e.g. non-repo cwd). Consumed by the spawn-agent dialog (`260713-sbk1`, extended `260714-q9cg`) |
| `getRiffPresets(server, session)` | GET | `/api/riff/presets?session=<session>` (via `withServer` + `deduplicatedFetch`) ‚Äî the dialog's **preflight**. Return type changed by `260714-q9cg` to `RiffPreflight = {presets: RiffPreset[]; tiers: string[]}` (was bare `RiffPreset[]`), tolerantly unwrapping the `{presets, tiers}` envelope (`presets ?? []`, `tiers ?? []`). `RiffPreset = {name, layout, paneCount}`. Throws on a non-ok response; the dialog treats a failure as "no presets, tier `default` only" and still allows a task-only spawn (`260713-sbk1`, extended `260714-q9cg`) |

All API functions (except `listServers`, `createServer`, `setServerOrder`, `killServer`, `getDirectories`, `getHealth`, `getThemePreference`, `setThemePreference`, `refreshStatus`, `triggerUpdate`, `triggerForceUpdate`, `triggerRestart`) append `?server={active}` via a module-level `setServerGetter()` mechanism. The `SessionProvider` sets the getter on mount. No multiplexed `action` field ‚Äî each mutation is a separate function with its own URL path.

**Request deduplication**: A module-level `deduplicatedFetch` wrapper maintains a `Map<string, Promise<Response>>` of in-flight GET requests. When a GET to a URL already has an in-flight promise, the existing promise is returned (with `Response.clone()` so each caller can independently consume the body). POST/PUT requests always make fresh `fetch()` calls. Promises are cleaned up via `.finally()` on resolve or reject. All GET functions (`getHealth`, `getSessions`, `getDirectories`, `listServers`, `getKeybindings`, `getThemePreference`) use `deduplicatedFetch`; all mutation functions use plain `fetch`. Deduplication key is the full URL string (after `withServer()` appends `?server=`), so requests scoped to different tmux servers are not incorrectly merged.

## State Socket (`/ws/state`, `260716-qf3j-state-socket`)

**One WebSocket per tab multiplexes every session-state + host-metrics stream.** Change `260716-qf3j-state-socket` **retired `GET /api/sessions/stream` + `handleSSE`** (decision D2 ‚Äî the frontend was the sole consumer; one `git revert` recovers it) and replaced the per-server + `?metrics=1` **EventSource** pool with a single established WebSocket. **Why**: SSE holds an HTTP/1.1 pool slot in EVERY browser engine and the pool caps at 6 per origin (spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`); a multi-server host held all 6 slots from SSE alone on plaintext origins, and on Firefox/WebKit a saturated pool **blocks new WebSocket handshakes entirely** ‚Äî so terminal relays could never connect. An **established WebSocket holds NO pool slot** in any engine, dropping steady-state pool usage to ~zero and immune to multi-tab aggregation. A muxed *SSE* was rejected: it still holds one slot and needs out-of-band subscribe POSTs, reintroducing the POST-races-the-stream race class (memory: `relay-connect-select-alignment`). In-band subscribe frames are totally ordered with the events they gate, which also structurally fixes the long-standing `attachServer`‚ÜíSSE race (memory: `multi-server-group-expand-async-race`, now the change's explicit acceptance test). **Non-goals** (at Change 1): the chat SSE (`GET /api/windows/{id}/chat/stream`, `use-chat-stream.ts` ‚Äî Change 3) and terminal relays (`/relay/{windowId}` ‚Äî Change 2) were UNTOUCHED. *(Change 2, `260717-803u-relay-mux`, has since retired `/relay/{windowId}` for the `/ws/terminals` mux ‚Äî see ¬ß Terminal Relay; the tab now holds a fixed 2 WebSockets. The two sockets stay SEPARATE ‚Äî D6, bulk binary terminal output must not share a send buffer/scheduler with state events. Change 3, `260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`, has since moved chat onto THIS socket as a `kind:"chat"` subscription and retired the chat SSE ‚Äî see ¬ß chat kind below; the tab now holds a fixed 2 WS + 0 SSE on EVERY route, the socket-unification goal state.)*

### Wire protocol (JSON text frames both directions)

`app/backend/api/state_ws.go` owns the envelope types + `handleStateWS`. Client ‚Üí server ops: `hello` (once, first frame, carrying a client-generated `conn` id), `subscribe {kind, key?, server?, from?, req}`, `unsubscribe {kind, key?, server?}`, `preview-scope {server, expanded[]}`. (`clientMsg` gained `From int64` (`from`) for the chat kind, `260717-vhvz`.) Server ‚Üí client frames:

- **`ack {req, snapshot?, offset?}`** ‚Äî answers a subscribe. For `server`/`metrics` it carries the current `snapshot` (the same payload the SSE `event: sessions` / cached-metrics slot carried); `snapshot` is `json.RawMessage` (empty ‚Üí `null`, tolerated). For a `kind:"chat"` subscribe it carries the tail-start byte `offset` (`ackFrame.Offset int64`, `omitempty`) and **NO snapshot** (`260717-vhvz`, D5 ‚Äî the transcript came from the GET backfill).
- **`event {kind, key?, type, data}`** ‚Äî a producer event. `data` is `json.RawMessage` embedded **verbatim** ‚Äî byte-identical to the retired SSE frame's `data:` body (**contract-preservation rule**, load-bearing: today's SSE event names + payloads move into `type`/`data` unchanged, so every consumer above the `subscribe*` seams is untouched). Per-server events carry `kind:"server"` + `key`; host-global events carry `kind:"global"`; chat events carry `kind:"chat"` + `key:<windowId>` (`260717-vhvz`).
- **`gone {kind, key, reason}`** ‚Äî replaces the SSE `event: server-gone` (¬ß dead-server reap below).
- **`error {req, message}`** ‚Äî a malformed/unhonorable op; `req` echoes the offending op's `req` (0 when none). The socket stays live.

**Event catalogue** ‚Äî the `type` string equals the retired SSE event name for every session/host type (`sessions`, `session-order`, `preview`, `board-changed` as `kind:"server"`; `metrics`, `services`, `server-order`, `board-order`, `version`, `update-available`, `status-refresh` as `kind:"global"`). Their producers, cached slots, poll cadence, `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel semantics, PR-status join, previews, and every `broadcast*`/`setVersion`/`setPreviewScope` helper are **identical** to the pre-change hub ‚Äî see the ¬ß SSE Hub family below (Event-Driven SSE Loop, PR-Status Join, Session-Tile Previews, `broadcastServerOrder`/`broadcastBoardOrder`/`broadcastStatusRefresh`, version/update-available slots). **`kind:"chat"` (`260717-vhvz`) adds three types** ‚Äî `chat` (`ChatEvent[]`) and `chat-state` (`{pending}`) byte-identical to the retired chat SSE, plus a NEW lightweight `chat-reset` (`{}`) rotation/shrink signal ‚Äî driven NOT by the poll set but by a per-subscription producer goroutine (¬ß chat kind below).

### Hub edge refactor (`api/sse.go`)

The `sseClient` (single-server, channel of pre-rendered SSE bytes) generalizes to a per-connection **subscription set**: a `stateConn` holds `ch chan hubEvent`, `connID`, and `subs map[string]*sseClient` (one routing record per subscribed server key). **`hubEvent`** is the structured unit producers fan out ‚Äî `{kind, typ, key, data}` plus a `gone bool` marker and a `raw []byte` escape hatch for pre-composed frames (the `ack`, and `error` frames) that must ride the SAME ordered channel as the subscription's events. The producer edge renders each `hubEvent` via `renderEnvelope()` into the JSON envelope; a parallel `hubEvent.String()` renders the legacy SSE-frame shape used ONLY by tests (deletion candidate ‚Äî relocate to a test helper). **Every producer/collector/broadcast signature is unchanged** (decision: generalize the client edge, keep producers frozen ‚Äî the whole machinery is proven, so only the send/route path changed).

- **Metrics subscription = the retained `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel as the internal registry key** (Design Decision 6, as **amended in rework** ‚Äî the intake's original assumption-5 shape was NOT implemented). The wire protocol exposes `subscribe kind:"metrics"`, but `stateSubscribe` registers it internally under the reserved `metricsOnlyServer = "\x00metrics-only"` key ‚Äî the same sentinel the retired `?metrics=1` stream used. This leaves `safetyIntervalEffective`'s coverage gate and ALL poll logic **untouched** (minimal diff; the fast-cadence-on-`/` behavior is verified by acceptance A-003). Only the sentinel's HTTP-routing branch inside `handleSSE` (the `?metrics=1` ‚Üí sentinel mapping) was retired.
- **Server-key validation on the WS edge** (Constitution ¬ßI barrier preserved). The retired SSE edge validated the server via `serverFromRequest`; the WS edge restores it: `validate.ValidateServerName` guards `stateSubscribe`/`stateUnsubscribe`'s `kind:"server"` key (`api/sse.go`) and the in-band `preview-scope` op's `server` (`api/state_ws.go` calls `hub.emitError`). An invalid name / unknown kind gets an `error` frame carrying the offending `req` (routed through the send channel so ONLY the writer pump ever writes to the socket ‚Äî gorilla forbids concurrent writes), never a silent drop. `sse.go`'s "validated by ValidateServerName" comment is truthful again.
- **Ack ordering** (rework cycle 2 fix ‚Äî the load-bearing correctness property). `stateSubscribe` reads the ack snapshot (`previousJSON[key]` for a server, `cachedMetricsJSON` for metrics) **inside the SAME `h.mu` critical section that enqueues the ack**, AFTER `addClient` registers the routing record. This guarantees the ack's snapshot is ‚â• every `sessions`/`metrics` frame already on the channel: a concurrent poll tick either ran before this lock (the read sees its value) or after the ack (the client's newest-wins apply is correct). Reading under an EARLIER lock ‚Äî as the first cut did ‚Äî let a poll tick enqueue a NEWER `sessions` event ahead of a stale-snapshot ack; the client applies the ack's snapshot last and `previousJSON` dedup then suppresses re-emission, stranding stale UI on a quiet server. Regression-tested by `TestStateWS_SubscribeAckNotStaleUnderPollInterleave` (proven to FAIL against the earlier-read shape, clean under `-race`).
- **Writer-pump cleanup** (rework cycle 1, mirrors `relay.go`). The per-connection writer pump drains `sc.ch` to the socket. On a `WriteMessage` failure it `cancel()`s AND sets a short read deadline (`stateWSCleanupWait = 100ms`) on the connection, so the read loop's parked `conn.ReadMessage()` returns promptly and runs `dropStateConn` cleanup instead of leaking the goroutine + its hub subscriptions until TCP teardown. The connection's lifecycle context is rooted at `context.Background()` (NOT `r.Context()` ‚Äî the request context may be cancelled at the WS upgrade / hijack).

### Dead-server `gone` reap

The existing SSE poll-set reap on a dead-server fetch error (memory: `tmux-sessions` ¬ß SSE Poll-Set Lifecycle) now also fans an in-band `gone` frame: when `poll()` fetch returns `tmux.IsServerGone`, the loop-local `deadServers` collect, and the post-loop reap block sends `hubEvent{gone: true, key: server}` (rendered as `{"op":"gone","kind":"server","key":...,"reason":"server-exited"}`) to that server's subscribed connections before deleting it from every per-server map. A later re-subscribe re-registers the server cleanly. This is the `gone` frame's ONLY emit path (replaces the SSE `event: server-gone\ndata: {}` frame). Full reap mechanics + concurrency contract: `tmux-sessions.md`.

### chat kind ‚Äî a per-subscription producer, NOT the poll set (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`)

Chat's live stream is a `kind:"chat"` subscription (`app/backend/api/chat_ws.go`; full contract in [chat](chat.md) ¬ß Live stream). It is deliberately **NOT** a poll-set member: transcript appends generate no tmux events (the recorded reason chat had a dedicated stream), so each subscription instead owns a **per-subscription producer goroutine** (`chatProducer`), tracked in a per-connection `chatProducers` map on `stateConn` (keyed `server\x00windowID`) that is **separate from `subs`** (the `h.clients`/poll routing records ‚Äî Design Decision: a chat sub is a goroutine+cancel, not a fan-out record). A `chatResolver` function field on `sseHub` (default over `h.fetcher.FetchSessions` + `sessions.ResolveChatPane`, mirroring the `captureFn`/`fetcher` injection idiom) resolves the window's chat without giving the hub a `*Server`.

- **Subscribe** (`startChatSubscribe`): validates `msg.Key` (`ValidateWindowID`) + `msg.Server` (`ValidateServerName`) ‚Üí `error` frame carrying `req` on failure (no producer). Following the **terminals-mux S2 pattern**, it registers a placeholder producer synchronously under `h.mu`, then does resolve+`Lookup`+ack in the producer goroutine (never on the socket read loop ‚Äî a stalled `FetchSessions` must not freeze the connection's other ops). The ack carries `offset: from` + NO snapshot, enqueued before the producer's first emit (ack-before-first-emit). A repeat subscribe for the same key cancels+replaces the prior producer.
- **Producer** (`runChatProducer`): a TAIL/DORMANT machine. **TAIL** = an incremental `chat.Adapter.TailFrom(ref, from)` (the self-priming `Tail` was retired) emitting `Events`‚Üí`chat`+`chat-state`. **DORMANT** = on a ~2s `chatRefResolveInterval` re-resolve seeing a fresh ref (rotation) or a shrink `Reset`, it CANCELS the tail and does NOT re-tail from 0 (that would re-stream a whole conversation over the shared socket, D5), emitting a single `chat-reset` **only once the rotated-to transcript EXISTS** (`transcriptExists` probe); the fresh tail belongs to the client's re-subscribe. Lazy-transcript not-yet tolerance is preserved on initial subscribe AND rotation. A dropped `chat`/`chat-state` `hubEvent` under channel pressure sets `pendingReset`, flushed as one `chat-reset` when the channel drains (`sendConnLockedOK`/`flushPendingReset`).
- **Teardown**: the producer ctx is cancelled on unsubscribe, on `dropStateConn` (which cancels every chat producer + clears `chatProducers`), and on repeat-subscribe ‚Äî no goroutine outlives its subscription (Constitution II). The `chat-error` (`{error}`) type is reserved client-facing protocol tolerance the producer never emits today (every failure converges via the subscribe-time `error` frame or DORMANT‚Üí`chat-reset`; `chatEventError` is a zero-emit deletion candidate).

### Frontend `StateSocket` client (`src/lib/state-socket.ts`)

One `StateSocket` per tab owns the `/ws/state` WebSocket. On open it sends `hello` (conn id via `crypto.randomUUID()`) then resubscribes every active subscription (each re-acks with a fresh snapshot ‚Äî the reconnect recovery path); on drop it reconnects with **exponential backoff 1s ‚Üí 15s cap**. It exposes `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`/`subscribeMetrics`/`unsubscribeMetrics` (idempotent, **ref-counted** by a stable id `"server:<name>"` | `"metrics"` so overlapping consumers ‚Äî e.g. the current server plus an expanded sidebar group naming the same server ‚Äî share one wire subscription), a `sendPreviewScope(server, expanded)` in-band twin, and `onEvent`/`onAck`/`onGone`/`onConnectionChange` callbacks that demux the envelope back into `(kind, type, key, data)`. It tracks a `reqToKey` map to route an `ack` back to its subscription's kind/key, and **drops the pending `reqToKey` entry on an `error` frame** so a rejected subscribe doesn't leak a row. Pure/testable (injectable conn id; the WS is the standard browser global). The **Vite dev proxy gained a `/ws` entry with `ws: true`** (`app/frontend/vite.config.ts`) so the upgrade is forwarded in dev. **Chat (`260717-vhvz`)** adds `subscribeChat({server, windowId, from})`/`unsubscribeChat({server, windowId})` (sub id `chat:<server>:<windowId>`, `from` on the subscribe frame) and dispatches `kind:"chat"` events + the chat ack `offset` to handlers; because chat's `from` is a stateful cursor a blind resubscribe would send stale, **chat is EXCLUDED from the `onopen` blind reconnect resubscribe loop** (kept out of `this.subs`) ‚Äî the owner hook re-runs fetch‚Üísubscribe on reconnect instead (there is an OPEN-guard on the `req` recording). The chat seam is exposed to consumers through `session-context` (`subscribeChat`/`unsubscribeChat`/`registerChatHandlers`/`socketConnected`); the successor hook `use-chat-subscription.ts` holds no socket handle. See ui-patterns.md ¬ß Chat View and [chat](chat.md) ¬ß Chat View Frontend.

### `session-context.tsx` transport swap (seams preserved)

`session-context.tsx` replaces the per-server EventSource pool + the dedicated host-metrics EventSource effect with one `StateSocket` held in `socketRef` (survives effect re-runs / StrictMode remounts). `attachServer` and every `subscribe*` helper keep their exact signatures ‚Äî no consumer above the seams changed. The `attachedSet` drives a diff effect that `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`s; a `metrics` subscription is opened when `attachedSet` is empty (the `/` Host case) and dropped when a server is attached (the host-global `metrics` event rides every server subscription). Acked snapshots + events route into the existing slice-update paths; version/update/order/preview/`setPreviewScope` behave identically, and `setPreviewScope` now sends **in-band** over the socket (no POST-races-the-stream window).

- **Connection dots = socket-connected AND subscription-acked** (with the existing 3s debounce). Per-server `isConnected` flips true on that server's subscription `ack` (mirrors the pre-change "first sessions event"); `ackedServersRef` tracks acked subscriptions and an `applyServerConnected` pass publishes `isConnected` on every socket connection-state change. `hostMetricsConnected` = the dedicated metrics subscription's debounced health when no server is attached, else true iff ANY attached server slice is connected (the host-global `metrics` event is delivering through that subscription). Reconnect nuance (nice-to-have): on socket re-open a previously-acked server flips Connected before its fresh re-ack lands (ms-scale window). See ui-patterns.md ¬ß connection dots / reload guard.
- **StrictMode safety** (rework cycle 2 MUST-FIX). `main.tsx` wraps in `<StrictMode>` (the real dev + e2e runtime), which double-mounts the provider. The socket-construction effect destroys+recreates the `StateSocket` across the remount, but the guard refs (`metricsSubscribedRef`, `subscribedServersRef`, `ackedServersRef`) survive in refs ‚Äî so mount 2 would see its guards already true and never re-subscribe on the FRESH socket, permanently losing the metrics subscription on `/` (Host dot dead forever; when this tab is the hub's only client the poll loop never starts). Fix: the socket effect's **cleanup resets all three guard refs**, so the remount re-subscribes cleanly. StrictMode-wrapped unit tests cover metrics + server re-subscription.
- **`onGone` releases the subscription** (rework cycle 1). On a `gone` for a still-attached server, `onGone` deletes it from `ackedServersRef` + `subscribedServersRef` AND calls `socketRef.current.unsubscribeServer(key)`, releasing the StateSocket ref-count so the diff effect re-subscribes cleanly when `attachedSet` recomputes (via `onGone`'s `fetchServers`) and the server is still desired ‚Äî no permanently-dead UI for a server the user restarts.

## Terminal Relay ‚Äî `/ws/terminals` mux (`260717-803u-relay-mux`)

**One `/ws/terminals` WebSocket per tab carries ALL pane relay streams.** Change `260717-803u-relay-mux` **retired `GET /relay/{windowId}` + `handleRelay`** (decision D2 ‚Äî the frontend was the sole consumer, no API-compat contract; constitution IV) and replaced the per-pane relay socket with a single muxed connection: a board with N panes now holds ONE terminals socket instead of N, giving one reconnect path and one upgrade handshake instead of N. Combined with change 1's state socket the tab's steady-state connection budget is a **fixed 2 WebSockets** (`/ws/state` + `/ws/terminals`) and zero SSE. **Why**: this is connection hygiene (TCP count, handshake count, one backoff loop) ‚Äî the user-facing HTTP/1.1-pool fix rode change 1 (an established WS holds no pool slot, but every extra WS *handshake* can block behind a saturated pool on Firefox/WebKit ‚Äî spike `docs/findings/socket-pool-accounting.md`). Same port as the API, no separate relay port; `gorilla/websocket` + `creack/pty`. Handler in `app/backend/api/terminals_ws.go` (sibling of `state_ws.go`); `relay.go` retains only the shared `upgrader` + `forceTERM`, both consumed by the mux.

### Wire protocol (binary data frames + JSON control ops)

Lifted verbatim from the plan ¬ßTerminal socket. **Binary data frames `[u32 BE streamId][payload]`** in both directions (server‚Üíclient PTY output, client‚Üíserver keystrokes). **JSON text frames for control**:

- Client ‚Üí server: `{"op":"open","id":<u32>,"server":..,"windowId":"@N","cols":<u16>,"rows":<u16>}`, `{"op":"resize","id":<u32>,"cols":<u16>,"rows":<u16>}`, `{"op":"close","id":<u32>}`.
- Server ‚Üí client: `{"op":"opened","id":<u32>}`, `{"op":"closed","id":<u32>,"code":4004|4001|1000,"reason":..}`.

Stream IDs are **client-allocated u32s, unique within a socket connection** (the `open` op carries the client's chosen id). A malformed control frame is ignored (the socket stays live, forward-compat); an unknown op is ignored. **Today's WS close codes `4004`/`4001` become per-stream `closed` control events with the same code/reason ‚Äî the SOCKET itself never closes for a stream-level failure** (`4004` = ResolveWindowSession/SelectWindowInSession failed / bad window ID; `4001` = `pty.StartWithSize` failed; `1000` = graceful client `close` op or PTY EOF).

### Per-stream lifecycle ‚Äî reproduces `handleRelay` exactly, per stream

Each stream reproduces the retired `handleRelay` per-stream (same resolve ‚Üí session-scoped select ‚Üí direct attach ‚Üí PTY pump). `startStream` runs on the socket read loop but does only cheap synchronous work there ‚Äî validate the (already JSON-decoded) `windowId` via **`validate.ValidateWindowID`** (the same validator `decodeWindowID` wraps, so the REST and mux entry points share one validator and cannot drift ‚Äî bug #205; the mux path needs no percent-decode since its id arrives decoded in JSON, not a URL segment) and **register a PLACEHOLDER stream (queue + closed chan, nil ptmx) under the connection mutex** ‚Äî then dispatches the blocking tmux work to a goroutine (`attachStream`), so a resolve (‚â§5s) + select + `ReloadConfig` + attach never serializes behind other panes' keystrokes/opens (rework S2). The placeholder-first registration makes duplicate-id checks and racing resize/close ops deterministic (a resize/close arriving mid-attach finds the placeholder). `attachStream`:

1. **Resolves the owning session** via `s.tmux.ResolveWindowSession(ctx, server, windowID)` (5s timeout) ‚Äî the ONE session that owns the window (home OR `_rk-pin-*` pin-session; O(1) `display-message` lookup, `260609-enic`). Resolve failure/empty ‚Üí per-stream `closed` 4004, socket open.
2. **Session-scoped select** via `s.tmux.SelectWindowInSession(session, windowID, server)` ‚Äî a bare `select-window -t @N` is ambiguous inside a tmux session group, so select and attach must agree on the same resolved session (the group-ambiguity rationale carried over from the old `relay.go:88-99`). Failure ‚Üí `closed` 4004.
3. **Initial size rides the `open` op** ‚Äî `pty.StartWithSize` at the open frame's `cols`/`rows` (falls back to 80√ó24 on zeros), **replacing the old wait-for-first-`resize`-message dance**. Best-effort `tmux.ReloadConfig(server)` first (true-color terminal-overrides on a foreign server), then `tmux [-L server] attach-session -t <session>` via `creack/pty` with `forceTERM` (TERM=xterm-256color). Attach failure ‚Üí `closed` 4001.
4. **Publishes the attach into the placeholder under the lock** (if the stream was torn down mid-attach, the just-started attach is cleaned up rather than orphaned), then **enqueues `opened` onto the stream's OWN bounded queue BEFORE starting the PTY reader** (rework M2). Channel FIFO + the scheduler's short-frame priority then guarantees the client sees `opened` before the first data frame ‚Äî the ordering the client's deferred-reset re-arm depends on (data-before-`opened` wiped the reset). A `closed` for a FAILED open rides a reserved control pseudo-stream (`controlStreamID = math.MaxUint32`), never a real pane id ‚Äî a failed open produced no data, so its `closed` has no ordering concern.
5. **Per-stream cleanup** (client `close` op, PTY EOF, socket teardown): `sync.Once`-guarded cancel + ptmx close + attach-process kill, remove from the registry ‚Äî exactly as `handleRelay`'s cleanup, no orphaned attach processes. Socket teardown tears down every stream.

### Write path ‚Äî per-stream bounded queues + fair scheduler (D3, a v1 protocol requirement)

**Per-stream bounded send queue (`streamQueueDepth = 8` √ó `streamFrameSize = 4096B`) drained by a SINGLE writer goroutine** that schedules control/short frames (`shortFrameMax = 256B`; a keystroke echo) ahead of bulk output and round-robins across ready streams ‚Äî **never FIFO across streams** (gorilla forbids concurrent writes, so all output funnels through this one writer). **This is a protocol requirement, not an optimization** (decision D3): spike 2 measured a shared FIFO at **1.66s** interactive echo p50 under a co-stream 1 Mbps flood vs **32ms** with per-stream queues + this scheduler at identical goodput (`docs/findings/relay-mux-hol.md`). The per-stream PTY reader is the queue producer; a **full queue PAUSES that stream's PTY reader** (backpressure into tmux's per-client buffering ‚Äî the same mechanism a stalled per-pane TCP socket exerted before the mux) and **NEVER drops bytes** (dropping mid-stream corrupts VT state). The kernel TCP send buffer is the shared tail after the scheduler (default autotuning acceptable ‚Äî the scheduler bounds everything above it). `writeFrame` is an **injectable seam** (production writes the socket; the HOL unit test substitutes a paced writer). *(Note: exact RR variant ‚Äî plain vs deficit ‚Äî is unobservable to the pinned test bound; D8 left it to apply. The shipped `drainReady` is a single short/control-priority pass with a round-robin bulk handoff per stream.)*

### Frontend ‚Äî `RelayMux` singleton + `TerminalClient` port

Frontend consumes the mux via a `RelayMux` singleton (`app/frontend/src/lib/relay-mux.ts`) ‚Äî see `ui-patterns.md` ¬ß Terminal Write Batching and ¬ß Terminal Relay (frontend). `terminal-client.tsx:813`'s `new WebSocket('/relay/...')` was the ONLY socket-creation site replaced; the stream handle is surfaced through the existing `wsRef` seam via a WebSocket-shaped adapter (`readyState`/`send`/`close`). Socket-level reconnect is owned by `RelayMux` (exponential backoff, one loop for the whole tab); a stream-level `closed` is handled per-pane (4004 ‚Üí `onSessionNotFound` redirect; non-4004 ‚Üí print `[reconnecting‚Ä¶]` + one probed re-open, else `[disconnected]`). RefreshButton remains the manual full-page recovery affordance.

**No startup sweep, no ephemeral** (unchanged from `260602-qn62`): the relay still attaches directly to the durable owning session ‚Äî there was never an ephemeral relay session under the move-based model, and there is no in-server session class to reap. See `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß Terminal Relay.

### HOL scheduler Go unit test (`terminals_ws_test.go`)

`TestScheduler_EchoNotHeadOfLineBlocked` ports the spike harness with **no real network**: the scheduler is wired to a paced `writeFrame` (sleeps ‚àù bytes written), stream A floods 4096B frames, a stream-B echo frame is enqueued, and the test asserts B is written within a small **bounded number of A frames** (pins the observable non-FIFO fairness bound, not the exact RR algorithm). Relay behaviors are re-asserted per-stream against `/ws/terminals`: `opened` precedes the first data frame (`TestTerminals_OpenedPrecedesData`, pinning M2), initial-size attach + TERM forcing (`_InitialSizeAndTERM`), `resize` sets the PTY size (`_ResizeSetsClientSize`), client `close` ‚Üí `closed` 1000 (`_ClientCloseYields1000`), bad/missing window ‚Üí `closed` 4004 with the socket still open (`_BadWindowIDClosed4004`/`_MissingWindowClosed4004`), and `-race`-clean across the terminals+scheduler suite.

## Daemon Lifecycle

The Go binary manages its own daemon lifecycle via the top-level `rk daemon` subcommand tree (sibling of `rk serve`, not nested under it). The daemon runs in a dedicated tmux server (socket `rk-daemon`, session `rk-daemon`, window `serve`) ‚Äî separate from the `runkit` server used for agent sessions. The session name matches the socket name so the combined exact-match target (`=rk-daemon:=serve`) cannot collide with user-facing sessions via tmux prefix matching. `LegacySessionName = "rk"` is consulted only by `Stop`/`Restart` (via `runningSessionCtx`, which checks `SessionName` first then falls back to the legacy name) so a daemon started by a pre-rename binary can still be stopped cleanly during the first upgrade. Daemon helpers live in `internal/daemon/`; the CLI surface lives in `app/backend/cmd/rk/daemon*.go` (one file per subcommand: `daemon.go` parent, `daemon_start.go`, `daemon_stop.go`, `daemon_restart.go`, `daemon_status.go`, plus `daemon_portowner.go` for the shared port-owner helper).

- `rk daemon start [--force]` ‚Äî start daemon (errors if already running)
- `rk daemon stop [--force]` ‚Äî graceful shutdown via C-c to the tmux pane, with a mode pre-cancel and a force-kill fallback (see `Stop()` sequence below); prints `rk daemon not running` and exits 0 when no session exists
- `rk daemon restart [--force]` ‚Äî idempotent: stop existing daemon (the full `Stop()` sequence below ‚Äî mode pre-cancel ‚Üí C-c ‚Üí wait up to `stopGracePeriod` 12s for graceful exit, an independent grace-deadline timer sized to cover the inner serve's ~10s worst-case shutdown ‚Äî see `internal/daemon` row; a session that vanished on its own counts as a clean stop, and a C-c that fails to deliver now degrades to `kill-session` rather than wedging) then start new one; starts fresh if no daemon running
- `rk daemon status [--json]` ‚Äî read-only report of daemon state (running / not running, socket, session, window, target) AND port owner (free / held by the daemon / held by another process). `--json` emits a structured machine-readable form (`daemon.{running,socket,session,window,target,pid}` + `port.{host,port,state,holder_pid,holder_command}`)
- `rk update` ‚Äî auto-restarts daemon after successful `brew upgrade` using `RestartWithBinary(brewBinPath)` where `brewBinPath` is `<brewPrefix>/bin/run-kit` derived from the resolved `/Cellar/run-kit/` path (resolves to the new Cellar version post-upgrade, avoiding stale `os.Executable()` path from the running process; the `run-kit` bin/Cellar identity since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`). Operates at the Go API layer, not the CLI surface

The pre-`260528-5zvv` flags `rk serve -d`, `rk serve --restart`, and `rk serve --stop` were removed in a hard break ‚Äî no deprecation forwarders. Invoking them now surfaces cobra's standard `unknown flag` error. `rk serve` is foreground-only.

**Naming collision note**: `rk daemon status` is distinct from `rk status` (the top-level tmux session summary in `cmd/rk/status.go`). The collision is sibling-namespaced ‚Äî cobra disambiguates cleanly ‚Äî but `rk daemon status --help` includes a one-line note pointing this out so users typing `rk status` expecting daemon info land at the right command.

**`--force` semantics** ‚Äî consistently "override the safety check that prevents claiming the port from a non-rk-daemon owner":

- `rk daemon start --force` ‚Äî lazy / on-error. The happy path is identical to the non-forced path (`daemon.Start()` ‚Üí port-probe). Only when `Start()` returns the port-in-use error does the command look up the port owner, refuse to kill if the holder identifies as the rk daemon (`daemon.InnerServePID()` match), otherwise SIGTERM the owner with graceful-then-forceful escalation, and retry `Start()`.
- `rk daemon stop --force` ‚Äî stop the daemon first (if running), then regardless of step 1's outcome probe the port. If still held by a non-daemon process, SIGTERM it. If the port is free at probe time, exit 0 silently (no `Killed port owner` line). If the holder identifies as the rk daemon itself, exit non-zero with a "manual investigation needed" message.
- `rk daemon restart --force` ‚Äî stop the daemon if running, then proactively probe the port BEFORE the start step. Any non-daemon holder is SIGTERMed (with graceful-then-forceful escalation) before `daemon.Start()` is called.

`rk daemon status` is read-only and does NOT accept `--force` ‚Äî passing it produces cobra's `unknown flag` error.

**`Stop()` sequence** (`internal/daemon/daemon.go`, resolved-session target `targetFor(session)` throughout so the legacy `rk` name is handled): (1) **mode pre-cancel** ‚Äî `copy-mode -q` runs FIRST, before the C-c send, best-effort (a failure is `slog.Debug`-logged and never aborts `Stop()`). This defends against a root-cause wedge: a pane left in tmux copy-mode does NOT receive C-c as a literal key ‚Äî tmux looks the key up in the mode key table (`copy-mode` binds `C-c` ‚Üí `send-keys -X cancel`, a non-read-only command) and dispatches that binding through the session's only attached client, run-kit's own read-only `-CC` control bridge (attached with `-r` ‚Äî see the `internal/tmuxctl` production dial), which tmux rejects with `client is read-only`, so the interrupt never reaches the serve process. `copy-mode -q` returns the pane to normal mode so the subsequent send injects C-c literally; it is idempotent (exit 0 when the pane is not in a mode ‚Äî `-q` since tmux ‚â•3.2), so it runs unconditionally on every `Stop()`. (2) **C-c send** ‚Äî `send-keys ... C-c` triggers graceful shutdown; on failure it does NOT early-return (an `slog.Warn` fall-through) so the grace-timer ‚Üí `kill-session` fallback below is now reachable on any graceful-delivery failure.
