Before this fix the send failure was wrapped and returned, wedging `Stop()` and everything layered on it (`rk daemon restart`, `rk update`'s `RestartWithBinary`, `POST /api/restart`) even though the force-kill would have stopped the daemon. (3) **grace-timer ‚Üí kill-session** ‚Äî the independent `stopGracePeriod` (12s) timer + `stopPollInterval` (200ms) polls (each under a fresh `cmdTimeout` context, per the per-command-context discipline documented in the `internal/daemon` row); the full grace is still waited before the kill even when the C-c send failed (no shortened-grace special case). A session that vanished on its own by kill-time ‚Äî or after a `kill-session` that errored ‚Äî is the success outcome (returns nil); only a session still alive after a failed kill surfaces an error.

Binary resolution: `Start()` uses `os.Executable()` + `filepath.EvalSymlinks()` (works for the standard `rk daemon start` / `restart` paths where the running binary is valid). `StartWithBinary(path)` accepts an explicit binary path and resolves its symlinks (used by `update` after `brew upgrade` deletes the old Cellar directory). Both delegate to shared `startSession(exe)` for tmux session creation.

Detection: `tmux -L rk-daemon has-session -t =rk-daemon` (anchored `=` prefix forces exact-match ‚Äî see PR #196). `runningSessionCtx` consults `=rk-daemon` first, then falls back to `=rk` for transparent stop/restart of pre-rename daemons. No polling loop, no signal files, no supervisor script.

**Port-based liveness probe**: Before `Start()`/`StartWithBinary()` create the tmux session ‚Äî and AFTER the `IsRunning()` check passes ‚Äî they call `guardPortAvailable()`, which loads `config.Load()` and runs `net.DialTimeout("tcp", host:port, 400ms)` against `RK_HOST:RK_PORT`. Wildcard/empty hosts (`""`, `"0.0.0.0"`, `"::"`, `"[::]"`, `"[::1]"`) substitute `127.0.0.1` via `probeHost()` ‚Äî dialing `0.0.0.0` itself is platform-inconsistent and not a reliable liveness signal. If the dial succeeds (something is listening), `Start` returns an error containing the substrings `already serving on`, `not under the rk-daemon`, and `RK_PORT` so scripts can pattern-match. Cobra `RunE` propagates the non-zero exit. This closes the split-brain detection gap where a foreground `rk serve` was invisible to the tmux-only `IsRunning()` check.

**Stale-socket reaping**: When `IsRunning()` is false AND the port probe passes, `Start`/`StartWithBinary` call `reapStaleDaemonSocket(ctx)` which invokes `runTmux(ctx, "kill-server")` ‚Äî scoped strictly to `serverSocket = "rk-daemon"` (never the agent-session `runkit` server). Idempotent: tmux's "no server running" surface on cold start is the common case. Errors are logged at `slog.Debug` and never block startup; if anything is genuinely broken, the subsequent `startSession` surfaces it. This self-heals the orphaned-socket state that arose when a previous inner serve died on a port collision before this fix shipped.

**Startup logging via `RK_DAEMON_LOG`**: `startSession` resolves `os.UserCacheDir()/rk/daemon.log` (e.g. `~/.cache/rk/daemon.log` on Linux, `~/Library/Caches/rk/daemon.log` on macOS) via `resolveDaemonLogPath()` and passes it to the inner `tmux new-session` via `-e RK_DAEMON_LOG=<path>`. The serve startup's `setupSlog(level)` reads the env var, `os.MkdirAll(filepath.Dir(p), 0o755)`, opens the file with `O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` (mode 0o644), and wraps `io.MultiWriter(os.Stderr, file)` so slog output is teed to both the tmux pane (preserves `tmux attach` debugging) and a durable log file. Open failures fall back to stderr-only with one `slog.Warn("daemon log unavailable", ...)`; `UserCacheDir()` failure in `startSession` spawns the inner serve without the env var (single `slog.Warn` upstream). Logging is best-effort ‚Äî never blocks daemon creation. Constitution ¬ßVI compliance: the log is a passive append-only artifact, no supervisor, no signal file, no liveness derivation from contents.

The exported constant `daemon.LogEnvVar = "RK_DAEMON_LOG"` is the single source of truth (consumed by both `internal/daemon/startSession` and `cmd/rk/serve.go/setupSlog`).

**Port-owner lookup (`daemon_portowner.go`)**: shared helper used by all four `rk daemon` subcommands. `findPortOwner(ctx, host, port) (*PortOwner, error)` queries who is listening on the configured TCP port via `lsof -ti:<port>` (primary), falling back to `ss -tlnp '( sport = :<port> )'` when `lsof` is unavailable or errors. Both queries are port-only ‚Äî the `host` argument is pass-through for display (both tools correctly cover loopback and wildcard binds). Holder command is resolved via `/proc/<pid>/comm` on Linux, `ps -p <pid> -o comm=` on macOS. Returns `(nil, nil)` when nothing is listening; `(nil, error)` only when both tools fail. The companion `terminateOwner(ctx, owner)` mirrors `daemon.Stop`'s graceful escalation: `syscall.Kill(pid, syscall.SIGTERM)` ‚Üí 200ms polling for exit via `syscall.Kill(pid, 0)` up to a 5s grace period ‚Üí `syscall.Kill(pid, syscall.SIGKILL)` on timeout. Signal delivery uses `syscall.Kill` directly ‚Äî never a shell `kill` invocation. All subprocess calls (`lsof`, `ss`, `ps`) use `exec.CommandContext` with a 5s `context.WithTimeout` per Constitution ¬ßI. `var findPortOwner = findPortOwnerImpl` is overridable in tests so CLI tests drive `--force` paths without spawning the real tools.

**Holder-identity check (`daemon.InnerServePID()`)**: small helper in `internal/daemon` that returns the PID of the `rk serve` process running inside the daemon tmux pane, derived from tmux's `pane_pid` format spec via `tmux -L rk-daemon list-panes -t =rk-daemon:=serve -F '#{pane_pid}'` (a new `runTmuxOutput` internal captures stdout where `runTmux` would have discarded it). Returns `(0, error)` when the daemon session is absent or the tmux query fails. Used by every `--force` code path and by `rk daemon status` to recognize the daemon as the port owner ‚Äî when `owner.PID == innerServePID`, the port is classified as held by us (no signal sent in `--force`; `held-by-daemon` state in `status`). The CLI layer wires this through a package-level `var innerServePIDFn = daemon.InnerServePID` so tests can drive the self-recognition branch.

## tmux Control-Mode Subscription (`internal/tmuxctl`)

Package `app/backend/internal/tmuxctl/` owns the long-running `tmux -CC` control-mode subscriptions that drive sub-500ms SSE freshness. It is the **only sanctioned bypass** of the `internal/tmux/` boundary ‚Äî every other tmux interaction goes through the request-response helpers in `internal/tmux/tmux.go` with their 10s `context.WithTimeout`. The bypass exists because a single long-lived subscription is structurally incompatible with the `exec.CommandContext`-plus-timeout shape of `internal/tmux/`. The package's `doc.go` documents the boundary explicitly.

### Core types

- **`Client`** (`client.go`) ‚Äî one PTY-backed `tmux -CC` subscription per tmux server (identified by socket name). Runs `tmux [-L <socket>] -CC attach-session -t =<bootstrap> -r` via `creack/pty.Start` (the `-r` flag puts the connection in read-only mode ‚Äî see Design Decision below). The `=`-anchored target prevents prefix-match collisions, matching the convention established in PR #196. A single goroutine reads lines via `bufio.Scanner` and dispatches them through `ParseLine`. Public surface:
  - `Open(ctx, socket, sink) (*Client, error)` ‚Äî non-blocking; errors only on initial PTY allocation or process start failure.
  - `Close() error` ‚Äî idempotent; cancels the Client's context, kills the subprocess, terminates the reconnect loop.
  - `Generation() int64` ‚Äî atomic per-server counter incremented on every handled notification.
  - `Wait(after int64) <-chan struct{}` ‚Äî returns a channel closed once generation > after. Single-use; callers re-call after each consumed event.
- **`Supervisor`** (`supervisor.go`) ‚Äî owns `map[socket]*Client` guarded by `sync.Mutex`, plus an `fsnotify.Watcher` on the watch directory. Resolves the watch dir from `TMUX_TMPDIR` if set, else `/tmp/tmux-<euid>/`; missing directories are created via `os.MkdirAll(dir, 0o700)` and watched as sockets appear. `Start(ctx)` enumerates existing sockets synchronously (so the SSE hub never races an empty Client map for sockets that already exist on disk) and then runs an fsnotify event loop. Re-creating a socket of the same name closes the prior Client before opening a new one. `Stop(ctx)` closes every Client and the watcher; bounded 5s in production. `Get(socket) *Client` is the lookup used by the SSE bridge.
- **`EventSink`** (`event_sink.go`) ‚Äî consumer interface with 8 callbacks (`OnSessionWindowChanged`, `OnWindowAdd`, `OnWindowClose`, `OnWindowRenamed`, `OnSessionsChanged`, `OnLayoutChange`, `OnConnectionLost`, `OnConnectionEstablished`). All callbacks dispatch from a single goroutine ‚Äî the Client's read loop. Sink implementations MUST NOT block. The production sink in `api/tmuxctl_bridge.go` (`hubSink`) is active since `260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation`: it records per-group active-window state into a per-Client `ActiveWindowTracker` (see ¬ß SSE Hub Bridge). The SSE hub still observes *change* via the per-server generation counter (that path is untouched); the sink's tracking is an additive side effect that supplies the Tier-1 active-window signal to the fetch path. `NoOpSink` is exported for tests, PTY-unavailable scenarios, and as the degraded sink a `nil` SinkFactory produces.
- **`ParseLine(line string) Event`** (`parser.go`) ‚Äî pure function (no I/O, no time dependence). Recognises the six relevant tmux 3.6a notifications (`%session-window-changed`, `%window-add`, `%window-close`, `%window-renamed`, `%sessions-changed`, `%layout-change`) and framing markers (`%begin`/`%end`/`%error`). `%output` and `%unlinked-window-*` are silently dropped. Unknown notification names return `UnknownEvent{Raw}` and log `slog.Debug` exactly once per unique name (surfaces protocol additions without log noise). Malformed input returns `MalformedEvent{Raw}` ‚Äî never panics.

### Reconnect FSM

When the PTY read loop encounters EOF or any error other than a Close-driven context cancellation, the Client calls `sink.OnConnectionLost()` exactly once, tears down the subprocess (`cmd.Process.Kill()` if still running, `cmd.Wait()` to reap), waits a backoff, then retries `pty.Start`. The backoff sequence is `initialBackoff = 250ms` ‚Üí `500ms` ‚Üí `1s` ‚Üí `2s` ‚Üí `5s` ‚Üí `5s` ‚Ä¶ capped at `maxBackoff = 5 * time.Second`. The backoff resets to `initialBackoff` on the first non-`%begin` event after a successful reconnect (see `client.go` `handleEvent`). Reconnect retries continue indefinitely until `Close()` is called. Test injection points: `dialFn` and `sleepFn` are swappable so the FSM can be exercised with stubbed I/O and a fake clock.

### Anchor session (`_rk-ctl`)

`tmux -CC` requires an attached session to emit notifications. `resolveBootstrap` (in `client.go`) **always** creates a hidden anchor session named `_rk-ctl` via `tmux [-L <socket>] new-session -d -s _rk-ctl` ‚Äî unconditionally on every observed server, not only when the server is empty (changed by `260602-a1wo-prevent-exit-empty-server-death`; the anchor is now a permanent **session floor** that keeps the server's session count above zero so tmux's `exit-empty` cannot reap it ‚Äî see ¬ß Constitution Alignment ¬ßVI below and `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß `_rk-ctl` Anchor). The anchor is tagged with the server-scoped user-option `@rk_ctl_keepalive 1` via `set-option -t =_rk-ctl @rk_ctl_keepalive 1` (constant `tmuxctl.AnchorKeepaliveOption = "@rk_ctl_keepalive"`). The tag is a defensive marker only ‚Äî v1 has no runtime consumer, but it allows future code to identify the anchor without depending on the literal session name. A "duplicate session" error from `new-session` (concurrent `rk serve` created the anchor first) is treated as benign by `isDuplicateSessionError` and the Client proceeds to attach. **Floor vs. attach target are decoupled**: the anchor is always created (the floor), but the control-mode attach target still prefers the first existing real session (`firstSessionName`, which now skips `_rk-ctl` so the always-present anchor is not picked), falling back to `_rk-ctl` only when no real session exists. The anchor is hidden from user-facing surfaces via `tmux.ControlAnchorSessionName` ‚Äî see `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß `_rk-ctl` Anchor for the filtering chokepoints, the `exit-empty off` backstop, and the explicit-kill-only lifetime contract.

### SSE Hub Bridge (`api/tmuxctl_bridge.go`)

The `api` package owns the bridge between `tmuxctl.Supervisor` and the SSE hub. Three artefacts:

- **`WindowChangeSubscriber`** (interface defined in `api/sse.go`) ‚Äî the interface the hub uses to receive per-server change notifications. Methods: `Generation(server string) int64` and `Wait(server string, after int64) <-chan struct{}`. Generation semantics mirror `tmuxctl.Client`: every observed notification increments the counter; `Wait(after)` returns a channel closed once `generation > after`.
- **`supervisorSubscriber`** ‚Äî the production adapter. Forwards `Generation` and `Wait` calls to `Supervisor.Get(server).Generation()` / `.Wait(after)`. When no Client exists for a server (PTY-unavailable host, socket not yet allocated), `Wait` returns a **never-closing** channel via `neverChan()` so `selectFirst` falls through to the safety-net timer rather than busy-looping `FetchSessions`. Exported via `NewSupervisorSubscriber(sup)`.
- **`hubSink`** ‚Äî the production EventSink, one per Client, built by the `SinkFactory` returned from `NewHubSinkFactory()` (the `Supervisor` calls the factory per socket, passing that socket's own `ActiveWindowTracker` ‚Äî see ¬ß Active-Window Event Derivation below; `NewHubSink()` was removed by `260530-v6hm`). Beyond the generation-counter path (which the Client bumps itself, before invoking the sink, so the hub still observes *change* via `Wait`), `hubSink` records active-window state into its tracker: `OnSessionWindowChanged(sid, wid)` resolves `sid`‚Üígroup via the tracker's cached map (O(1), no subprocess) and records `wid` as that group's active window (latest-event-wins; an unresolved `sid` is dropped for tracking, never errors/blocks); `OnSessionsChanged` refreshes the `$sid`‚Üígroup map; `OnConnectionEstablished` re-seeds the tracker (refresh map + seed Tier 1 from current `#{window_active}` per group). The two re-seed callbacks issue read-only tmux queries that could block, so they are **offloaded to a goroutine** (the read loop returns immediately ‚Äî honoring the EventSink "MUST NOT block" contract); the tracker's concurrency-safety makes a slightly-delayed refresh racing an event harmless. The read-only query seams (`listSessionGroups`/`listActiveByGroup`) are injectable struct fields so tests stub them without spawning tmux. The remaining callbacks (`OnWindowAdd`/`Close`/`Renamed`/`OnLayoutChange`/`OnConnectionLost`) stay no-ops.

`Server.SetWindowChangeSubscriber(sub)` materialises the lazy SSE hub (`initSSEHub`) and stores the subscriber. Safe to call before any SSE client connects. `Server.SetActiveWindowProvider(provider)` (since `260530-v6hm`) injects the Tier-1 `ActiveWindowProvider` (the Supervisor) into the production `prodSessionFetcher` so the REST + SSE fetch paths derive `isActiveWindow` from control-mode events; it is a no-op when the fetcher is a test-injected fake, keeping the seam optional.

### Active-Window Event Derivation (`260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation`)

The active-window highlight is **event-derived per session group** rather than read from the base session's `#{window_active}` pointer alone. The base pointer goes stale whenever an attachment moves the active window while another group member keeps an independent active-window pointer ‚Äî historically the per-WebSocket `rk-relay-*` ephemeral, and still `rk riff` / an external `new-window`; reading the base pointer produced the wrong-highlight bug. This whole derivation subsystem (`internal/tmuxctl/*`) was scoped *investigate-only, NOT deletable* by `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions` (it is driven by the `_rk-ctl` anchor and serves the SESSIONS highlight independent of boards) and is **left untouched** ‚Äî note that `260602-qn62` removed the `rk-relay-*` ephemeral, so the relay is no longer one of the stale-pointer sources, but the subsystem's internal comments still reference relays (out of scope for that change). The fix corrects the *read signal* ‚Äî it does not change any window creator.

**Tracker** (`internal/tmuxctl/active_window.go`) ‚Äî `ActiveWindowTracker` is a concurrency-safe, in-memory (Constitution ¬ßII) store for ONE server, owned by one `Client` (the read-loop goroutine is the sole writer; the fetch path reads). Two `sync.RWMutex`-guarded maps: `byGroup` (group name ‚Üí active `@wid`, latest-event-wins via `Set`, bulk re-seeded via `SeedGroups`) and `sidGroup` (`$sid` ‚Üí group, resolved via `ResolveGroup`, refreshed wholesale via `ReplaceSidGroups`). `Get`/`Snapshot` are the read accessors.

**Ownership/wiring** ‚Äî `NewSupervisor(factory SinkFactory)` takes a `SinkFactory` (a `nil` factory degrades every Client to `NoOpSink` ‚Äî control-mode observed only via the generation counter, no tracking). `Supervisor.openSocket` allocates a fresh tracker per socket and binds the sink to it (a close-then-reopen gets a new tracker so stale state never leaks across the gap ‚Äî `OnConnectionEstablished` re-seeds it). `Supervisor.ActiveWindow(server, group) (wid, ok)` is the server-keyed read accessor ‚Äî a server with no Client, or a group with no tracked entry, returns `("", false)` so the caller falls back to Tier 2. The Supervisor satisfies `sessions.ActiveWindowProvider` directly. Wired in `cmd/rk/serve.go`: `tmuxctl.NewSupervisor(api.NewHubSinkFactory())`, then after `Start` both `SetWindowChangeSubscriber(NewSupervisorSubscriber(supervisor))` and `SetActiveWindowProvider(supervisor)`.

**Two-tier derivation** (`internal/sessions/sessions.go`) ‚Äî `FetchSessions(ctx, server, provider)` threads an `ActiveWindowProvider` (nil ‚áí Tier-2-only, exactly today's behavior). Per session it queries `provider.ActiveWindow(server, sessionName)` ‚Äî the user-facing session name IS the group key after `parseSessions` filtering. **Tier 1 (authoritative):** when a tracked `@wid` exists, the pure helper `applyActiveWindow(windows, trackedWid)` marks exactly the matching window active and clears the rest, overriding the parsed `#{window_active}` flag. **Tier 2 (fallback):** no tracked entry ‚áí the base-pointer flag from `parseWindows` stands. Tier 1, once set, is authoritative ‚Äî the base pointer never overrides it; external clients (iTerm/Ghostty) also emit `%session-window-changed`, so "latest event wins" subsumes them with no override path. `applyActiveWindow` also enforces the single-highlight-per-session invariant and falls back to Tier 2 for a session when the tracked `@wid` matches no live window (e.g. closed between event and fetch) rather than highlighting nothing. The fetcher reaches `FetchSessions` via `prodSessionFetcher` (holding the provider) in `api/router.go`. Frontend auto-follow needs no change ‚Äî the existing `app.tsx` URL-writeback effect navigates once the corrected `isActiveWindow` arrives via SSE; board panes pin explicit window IDs and never read it.

### Event-Driven SSE Loop

`app/backend/api/sse.go` refactored its per-server snapshot loop from a 2.5s ticker to an event-driven `select` with a 12s safety-net backstop. Three constants govern the cadence:

| Constant | Value | Role |
|----------|-------|------|
| `safetyPollInterval` | `12 * time.Second` | Backstop when a `WindowChangeSubscriber` is wired (production). Heals missed events across reconnect gaps; primary freshness driver is the Client's `Wait` channel. |
| `legacyPollInterval` | `2500 * time.Millisecond` | Used when no subscriber is wired (PTY-unavailable startup, unit tests). The snapshot-rebuild cadence is then the only freshness guarantee. |
| `metricsPollInterval` | `2500 * time.Millisecond` | Cadence for `metrics.Collector` host CPU/memory polling. Deliberately decoupled from the SSE intervals so metrics sampling frequency is not coupled to the SSE event/safety cadences. |
| `prStatusPollInterval` | `90 * time.Second` | Cadence for `prstatus.Collector`'s single batched `gh` call (`260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar`). Deliberately slow (~40 calls/hr vs. the 5000/hr authenticated limit) ‚Äî the SSE hot path reads the cached snapshot, never `gh`, so PR-status freshness is decoupled from the SSE cadence; on-demand `POST /api/status/refresh` covers the "I want it now" case (`260715-jykd`; was `POST /api/pr-status/refresh`). |

`sseHub.safetyIntervalEffective()` picks `safetyPollInterval` when `subscriber != nil`, else `legacyPollInterval` ‚Äî preserves correctness for the PTY-unavailable case and for tests exercising the hub without a control-mode driver.

The loop body (`poll` + `waitForNext` + `selectFirst`) blocks on a `select` over (a) one `subscriber.Wait(server, perServerGen[server])` channel per active server and (b) `time.NewTimer(safetyIntervalEffective())`. When a subscriber fires, the winning server's prior generation is refreshed and the server is marked event-driven so the next iteration invalidates its 500ms `cache` entry and observes the post-mutation tmux state immediately. Non-winning servers are peeked non-blockingly so their backlog isn't replayed unnecessarily. `selectFirst` reads `timer.C` in the outer select to avoid the goroutine leak that would otherwise occur if a subscriber wins the race and the timer goroutine blocked on `timer.C` forever (`Stop` does not deliver on `C`). Heartbeat is wall-clock-based (`sseHeartbeatPeriod = 15 * time.Second`) ‚Äî wall-clock cadence prevents the slower safety interval from starving heartbeats.

### No Killed-Window Board Cleanup Diff (removed)

Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions`, the SSE hub no longer detects killed windows to clean up board membership. The old `detectKilledWindowIDs(prev, current) []string` pure function, the per-server `sseHub.previousWindowIDs` tracking, the per-tick window-kill cleanup loop, and the `BoardEntriesFetcher.RemoveAllByWindowID` dependency are all **deleted**. In the move-based model board membership is derived live from `_rk-pin-*` sessions, so a killed pinned window's pin-session simply drops out of the next `ListBoardEntries` read ‚Äî the frontend's refetch on the next session-list change picks it up. There is also no `@rk_board` first-poll bootstrap broadcast (`broadcastBoardBootstrap`/`boardBootstrapPayload`/`previousBoardJSON` removed) and no cached-board send on `addClient`. `BoardEntriesFetcher` is now a one-method interface (`ListBoardEntries`) kept only so tests can stub the tmux dependency; `broadcastBoardChanged` (pin/unpin/reorder) remains and the `"cleanup"`/`"bootstrap"` change strings are gone.

### PR-Status SSE Join (`260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar`)

The SSE hub attaches live PR status to **any window with a derived `PrURL`** on each poll via a PURE in-memory read ‚Äî the 2.5s hot path makes ZERO network/`gh` calls (the `gh` cost lives entirely on the collector's 90s background tick, the branch‚ÜíPR refresher's 30s tick, and the on-demand `POST /api/status/refresh` ‚Äî which kicks BOTH, since `260715-jykd`). Since `260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier` the change-bound gate is gone: `PrURL` is derived from the pane's branch (¬ß Branch‚ÜíPR Derivation), so PR status now appears for any pane on a branch with an open PR, not only fab-change-bound windows.

**Seam + wiring**: `PRStatusSnapshotter` (one method, `Snapshot() map[string]prstatus.PRStatus` ‚Äî URL-keyed, since PR numbers are only unique per repo, in `api/sse.go`) is implemented by `*prstatus.Collector` and held on the hub (`sseHub.prStatus`). `newSSEHub(fetcher, mc, svc, pc)` takes it as the fourth arg; `NewRouterAndServer` constructs `pc := prstatus.NewCollector(prStatusPollInterval); pc.Start(ctx)` next to the metrics collector, stores it on `Server.prStatus`, and `Server.initSSEHub` passes it through ‚Äî but as a true nil interface when `s.prStatus` is nil (the explicit `var pc PRStatusSnapshotter; if s.prStatus != nil { pc = s.prStatus }` wrap avoids the typed-nil-interface trap so the hub's `h.prStatus == nil` check actually fires). A nil `prStatus` degrades gracefully (no PR fields attached) ‚Äî used by tests and unwired routers.

**`attachPRStatus(sess []sessions.ProjectSession)`**: called in `poll()` AFTER the 500ms session-cache write (so the cached snapshot slice stays free of mutable PR fields conceptually, though it operates on the same slice by reference). For every window it FIRST resets the **collector-only** fields (`PrChecks/PrReview/PrIsDraft` ‚Üí zero, `PrFetchedAt` ‚Üí nil since `260715-nwla-status-refresh-feedback`) so a window that lost its PR (merged/closed ‚Üí dropped from the snapshot) clears cleanly even on a cached result slice; **`PrState` is deliberately NOT reset here** ‚Äî it is dual-sourced (the branch-derived `MapBranchState` fallback seeded upstream by `enrichWindowPR`), so it survives a collector miss and is overridden below only on a collector hit. THEN, gating only on a **non-empty `PrURL`** (`w.PrURL == nil || *w.PrURL == ""` ‚Üí skip; the `FabChange` gate was **dropped** by `260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier` per R7), it looks `*w.PrURL` up in the URL-keyed `Snapshot()` and copies `State/Checks/ReviewDecision/IsDraft` onto the window, plus `PrFetchedAt = &fetchedAt` where `fetchedAt := st.FetchedAt` ‚Äî a per-hit copy of the snapshot value scoped to the loop body, so taking its address yields a stable pointer independent of the range variable. `PrFetchedAt` (`prstatus.PRStatus.FetchedAt`, stamped `now` on each collector rebuild) is thus collector-join-owned exactly like the `PrChecks`/`PrReview`/`PrIsDraft` siblings ‚Äî set on a URL hit, nil on a miss (a URL-miss/empty/nil-`PrURL` window carries no stale freshness timestamp) ‚Äî and is surfaced as the StatusDotTip's ambient "checked Xs ago" line (ui-patterns.md ¬ß Status Dot hover-card). The join key is the **canonical PR URL, never a bare number** ‚Äî numbers are unique only per repo, so a number join can pick up an unrelated repo's PR state (the collision the URL-keying fixed). No-op when `h.prStatus == nil`. `PrURL`/`PrNumber` are NOT touched here ‚Äî since `260705-dmex` they come from the branch‚ÜíPR enrichment in `internal/sessions` (`enrichWindowPR` ‚Üí register + snapshot-join against the `prstatus` branch refresher), upstream of the hub.

### Branch‚ÜíPR Derivation (`260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier`)

`PrURL`/`PrNumber` are **derived server-side from the pane's git branch**, no longer joined from `fab pane map` (Constitution ¬ßX ‚Äî PR links are derivable, not pushed). This surfaces PR status for **any** pane on a branch with an open PR, in any repo under any workflow ‚Äî not only fab-change-bound windows.

**Two layers, both network-isolated from the SSE hot path:**

1. **Background `BranchRefresher`** (`internal/prstatus/prstatus_branch.go`): resolves each registered `(repoDir, branch)` ‚Üí PR via `gh pr list --head <branch> --state all --json number,url,state,updatedAt` (run in the repo via `cmd.Dir`, `exec.CommandContext` + `ghTimeout` + explicit argv ‚Äî ¬ßI), on a 30s tick (`branchPRRefreshInterval`, mirroring `Collector.Start`'s immediate-warm-then-tick lifecycle). It gates on ONE availability probe per pass (`checkAvailable` ‚Äî the `ghAvailable` verdict is cached positive AND negative for 60s so an unauthenticated gh never re-probes per pair), keeps the last-good entry on a transient exec/network error OR malformed JSON (true stale-while-revalidate ‚Äî never fail-to-negative), records a **successfully parsed empty/no-PR result as a valid negative** (`nil pr` ‚Äî clears the entry directly; no grace/negative-stamp retention), and ages out pairs no longer observed after 5m. `pickBranchPR` selects by **precedence ‚Äî open > merged > closed** (`branchStateRank`, case-insensitive), most-recently-updated within a class, skipping URL-less nodes and returning `nil` for an empty/all-skipped array. Started in `router.go` via `prstatus.DefaultBranchRefresher.Start(ctx)` next to the viewer-wide collector.

2. **Hot-path register + snapshot-join** (`internal/sessions.enrichWindowPR`): the FetchSessions loop does ZERO network work ‚Äî it `prstatus.Register(repoDir, branch)`s the observed pair (a cheap lock-guarded set touch) and `prstatus.SnapshotBranchPR(repoDir, branch)`s the last-good derived PR from the in-memory snapshot, assigning `WindowInfo.PrURL`/`PrNumber`. The window's `(repoDir, branch)` is `windowBranchRepo`'s choice: the active pane's cwd/branch, else the first pane with a resolved branch.

**D2 merged durability ‚Äî state-all + precedence, stateless/restart-proof** (revised by `260706-4h26-durable-merged-pr-register-keys`; status-pyramid.md ¬ß Open Decisions ‚Äî D2): the earlier `260706-y1ar` shape (`--state open` lookup + a `branchPRMergedGrace` 10-min grace clock on a `wentNegativeAt` field) DROPPED a PR the moment it merged, then leaned on an in-memory grace window to keep serving the last-known PR so the purple/orange **done-square** survived. That grace clock **decayed the merged square into a green fab square minutes after merge** and was **wiped by any rk restart** (in-memory state, Constitution II). The revised model derives durability **from `gh` directly, statelessly**: the branch query is now `--state all` (¬ß prstatus package row + layer 1 above), so a merged PR keeps resolving to a positive result on **every** refresh pass ‚Äî `pickBranchPR` ranks it by precedence (open > merged > closed) and serves it as the last-good entry. There is **no grace clock to expire and none to wipe on restart** ‚Äî a cold `BranchRefresher` (fresh process, no prior positive) serves the merged PR on its first pass, so the done-square is durable **statelessly and restart-proof end-to-end**. `refresh` now clears the entry directly on a successfully parsed empty/no-PR result (a true negative) and keeps last-good only on a transient exec error or malformed JSON (stale-while-revalidate) ‚Äî the `branchPRMergedGrace` const, the `wentNegativeAt` field, and the grace/negative-stamp retention branch in `refresh` were **deleted**. The viewer-wide collector (which queries OPEN/MERGED/CLOSED) supplies the merged `prState` via the URL join, so the dot shows the done-square; a **closed-unmerged** PR (still derived for the register/tip) has its fall-back to the live fab tier handled **frontend-side** (`statusDotState`'s `prOwnsDot` drops PR ownership for `prState === "closed"` ‚Äî see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) ¬ß Status Dot D2). The **branch-reuse edge**: an open PR always outranks an older merged PR on the same branch (state precedence beats recency across classes), so a reopened branch's live PR wins.

This is the T007/T008 **rework shape** (from `260705-dmex`): the original apply resolved `gh` inline in the enrichment loop, which broke `api/sse.go`'s zero-network-call hot-path invariant and code-review.md's 5s cap; review flagged it must-fix and it was restructured to register-off-tick + snapshot-join. The `prstatus` viewer-wide collector (URL-keyed live state/checks/review) is untouched and composes exactly as before: derive `PrURL` here ‚Üí `attachPRStatus` joins live status by that URL.

The old **`FabChange` gate is dropped** from `attachPRStatus` (R7) ‚Äî see ¬ß PR-Status SSE Join. The cross-repo contract for the fab-kit divestment this enables is in [`docs/specs/agent-state.md`](../../specs/agent-state.md); the run-kit-side agent-state tier that landed alongside it is [agent-state](agent-state.md).

### Web Push on Sustained Waiting (`260706-y1ar-status-pyramid-ui-surfacing`)

The SSE poll seam fires exactly **ONE Web Push per sustained-`waiting` episode** ‚Äî an agent blocked on a HUMAN (the most notification-worthy state) that stays `waiting` for ‚â• `waitingPushSustain` (15s). `idle`/`active` never push. It rides the per-server poll tick where the rolled-up window `AgentState` already exists ‚Äî **no new goroutine, no new poller** (Constitution II applies to *durable* state; the episode map is in-memory only, mirroring the metrics/prstatus collectors). Logic lives in `api/waiting_push.go`; the seam wiring is in `api/sse.go`'s `poll()`.

**Episode model + tracker** (`waitingPushTracker`, own mutex ‚Äî independent of the hub lock): a waiting EPISODE is a maximal run of consecutive `waiting` ticks for one window, keyed `waitingKey(server, windowID)` (`server\x00windowID` ‚Äî window ids are unique only within a server). `waitingEpisode{since, pushed}` stamps when the current run began and whether it has pushed. The **pure `decide(wins []pushWindow) []waitingPush`** advances the tracker for one server's windows at `now` and returns the pushes to send: waiting + no run ‚Üí start the run; waiting + run < sustain ‚Üí wait; waiting + run ‚â• sustain + `!pushed` ‚Üí PUSH once + mark pushed; not-waiting ‚Üí **delete the key** (re-arm ‚Äî the next `waiting` run is a fresh episode that can push again). It is pure w.r.t. its inputs + the tracker map (the only side effect is mutating that map, which IS the episode memory). `decide` is the extracted testable helper (drives enter/sustain/push/continue/leave/re-enter ‚Äî A-022/A-023).

**Sync decision, detached send** (T014 rework ‚Äî the load-bearing invariant): `notifyWaiting(server, sess)` runs `decide` **synchronously** (in-memory map mutation, no I/O ‚Äî the caller observes the tracker advance in-tick) but fans the actual `push.Notify` sends out in a **detached `context.Background()` goroutine** ‚Äî a slow/hung Web Push endpoint can NEVER stall the SSE poll loop's documented zero-network hot path. Push errors are logged (`slog.Warn`), never surfaced (matches the `/api/notify` posture). Body: window name + `"waiting for input"`. The `notify` send fn is a seam (defaults to `push.Notify`, stubbed in tests).

**Scoped reap** (`retain(live, polled)` ‚Äî the other T014 rework): the poll loop accumulates `liveWaitingKeys` across all polled servers, then reaps episodes for windows that vanished (so a re-created window id can't inherit a stale `pushed` flag). The sweep is **SCOPED to servers actually observed this tick** ‚Äî the ones successfully polled (`polledServers`) PLUS the ones confirmed gone (`deadServers`). A server whose fetch failed TRANSIENTLY (non-`IsServerGone`) is in neither set and contributes zero live keys, so scoping the sweep leaves its still-waiting episodes untouched ‚Äî otherwise its `since`/`pushed` would reset every failing tick, re-arming and firing a DUPLICATE push the moment the server recovered. `retain` recovers the server from a key by splitting on the NUL separator and reaps only `polled[server] && !live[key]`.

**Wiring**: `sseHub` gained a `waitingPush *waitingPushTracker` field (`newWaitingPushTracker()` in `newSSEHub`); in `poll()`, after `attachPRStatus(result)` for each successfully-fetched server, `h.waitingPush.notifyWaiting(server, result)` runs and its returned live keys accumulate into `liveWaitingKeys`; after the server loop, `h.waitingPush.retain(liveWaitingKeys, polledServers‚à™deadServers)` sweeps. Uses the existing `internal/push` subsystem (¬ß Web Push Notifications) ‚Äî no new endpoint. `@rk_agent_msg` question text in the body is a **future tenant** (out of scope; the body is the fixed `"waiting for input"`).

**Deep-link URL (`260714-r7rq-chat-read-frontend`)**: each `waitingPush` now carries a `url` ‚Äî the notification's click target, built by the pure `waitingPushURL(server, windowID, hasChat)`: `/{server}/{N}` where `N` is the window id's numeric part (tmux `@N` sans `@`, matching `windowIdToUrlSegment`), with `?view=chat` appended **iff the window is chat-capable** (`hasChat`), else the plain window URL (which resolves the window's own view pref on load). `server` and the numeric segment are `url.PathEscape`-d so a reserved-character name stays a valid same-origin relative URL. `hasChat` is read off the rolled-up window's `ChatProvider != ""` in `pushWindowsForServer`. The URL threads through `decide` ‚Üí `waitingPush.url` ‚Üí the detached-goroutine `t.notify(ctx, title, body, url)` ‚Üí `push.Notify`. Go units (`waiting_push_test.go`) cover the chat-vs-plain URL construction.

### Session-Tile Previews ‚Äî `event: preview` + preview-scope (`260701-70a0-session-window-tile-grid`)

The `SessionTiles` density view (`ui-patterns.md` ¬ß Session Tiles) shows a periodic **text snapshot** of each expanded window's active pane. Snapshots ride the existing SSE hub as a **dedicated `event: preview`** ‚Äî deliberately NOT extending the `sessions` payload and NOT a live xterm/relay per tile (that would re-trigger the documented HTTP/1.1 6-per-origin pool starvation ‚Äî the load-bearing constraint). This decoupling keeps the `sessions` dedup/order machinery lean (growing preview text never bloats the sessions dedup cache) and lets preview cadence stay independent of structural updates. `WindowInfo` is **unchanged** ‚Äî no `preview` field.

**Per-connection expanded-set scope**: each `sseClient` carries `connID` (from the `?conn=` stream query param) and `expanded map[string]bool` (the session names that connection currently has expanded). Both are in-memory only (Constitution II) and drop with the client on disconnect (`removeClient` deletes the whole `*sseClient` ‚Äî no leaked hub state, no separate cleanup path). `setPreviewScope(server, connID, expanded)` finds the client whose `connID` matches (under the hub lock) and replaces its `expanded` set; a `connID` miss is a silent no-op. It also immediately emits the cached preview subset for the just-changed set via `sendCachedPreviewLocked` (a no-op when the set is empty or nothing is cached).

**Capture in `poll()` (rides the existing tick ‚Äî no new goroutine/loop)**: after the `sessions` broadcast for a server, the poll computes `expandedUnionLocked(clients)` ‚Äî the union of every client's expanded session names on that server. When the union is empty (capture-nothing default ‚Äî previews are opt-in per expansion), nothing is captured. Otherwise `capturePreviews(result, union, server, h.captureFn)` captures each window in a union session **once per tick, deduped by window ID** (`h.captureFn` defaults to `capturePreviewForWindow`; tests inject a stub so the broadcast path runs without a live tmux server). The full `{windowId ‚Üí text}` union map is cached in `previousPreviewJSON[server]` (seeds cached-on-connect), then each client is sent a **per-connection-filtered subset** (`previewSubsetFor`, keyed off its own `expanded` set via `windowsBySession(result)`) over `event: preview`. The tmux captures run OUTSIDE the hub lock (each is an exec with its own timeout); only the cache write + per-client emit take the lock.

**Capture primitive (reused, no new tmux helper)**: `capturePreviewForWindow(w, server)` in `api/preview.go` picks the window's active pane via `activePaneID(w)` ‚Äî the `PaneInfo` in `WindowInfo.Panes` whose `IsActive` is true, falling back to the first pane, `("", false)` when the window has no panes ‚Äî then calls the existing `tmux.CapturePane(paneID, previewCaptureLines, server)` (Constitution I ‚Äî `exec.CommandContext` + timeout, arg slices). `previewCaptureLines = 18` (named constant, within the ~15‚Äì20 range). Best-effort: a no-pane window or a capture error yields no entry (skipped, never a hard failure). **No new tmux resolution helper was added** ‚Äî the active pane ID is already on `WindowInfo.Panes` from `ListWindows`'s `list-panes` enrichment (apply Assumption #1; the intake's conditional `tmux-sessions` memory modify did NOT trigger).

**Cached-on-connect**: `addClient` calls `sendCachedPreviewLocked` after the metrics cached-on-connect send, mirroring the `sessions`/`session-order`/`metrics` pattern ‚Äî filtered to the new client's current expanded set (a no-op for a fresh connection, since scope is declared by a POST that arrives after connect).

**Frontend seam** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`): since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` the transport is the single `StateSocket` (one `hello` conn id per tab, not a per-server `connId` ‚Äî the pooled per-server EventSource + `&conn=<id>` stream-URL append are gone). The provider routes the `preview` event through the socket's `onEvent` demux (merging the `{windowId ‚Üí text}` map into that server's slice so a preview for one window doesn't clobber the others), exposes `previewsByServer: Map<string, Record<string,string>>` + a `setPreviewScope(server, expanded[])` context method, and that method sends the scope **in-band** via `socketRef.current.sendPreviewScope(server, expanded)` (addressed by the socket's own conn id ‚Äî decision D4; no POST-races-the-stream window). The `api/client.ts` `setPreviewScope(server, conn, expanded)` HTTP helper is now unimported ‚Äî a deletion candidate; the server-side `POST /api/preview-scope` endpoint stays (D4). The `SessionTiles` view calls the context method whenever its expanded set changes.

### `rk serve` Wiring

`cmd/rk/serve.go` instantiates the Supervisor after `tmux.EnsureConfig()` but BEFORE the `server.ListenAndServe()` goroutine, so the SSE hub never races an empty Client map for sockets that already exist on disk. (Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions` there is no longer a `sweepOrphanedRelaySessions(ctx)` step between them ‚Äî relay ephemerals are gone and pin-sessions are persistent, so `serve_sweep.go` was deleted and the startup ordering dropped to `EnsureConfig ‚Üí Supervisor.Start ‚Üí ListenAndServe`.) The Supervisor is constructed with `api.NewHubSinkFactory()` (since `260530-v6hm` ‚Äî the per-socket tracker-bound sink factory; was `api.NewHubSink()`) and started synchronously; per-socket `Open` failures (PTY unavailable, etc.) are logged inside the Supervisor and never block startup. Once `Start` returns, `apiServer.SetWindowChangeSubscriber(api.NewSupervisorSubscriber(supervisor))` wires the change-notification bridge and `apiServer.SetActiveWindowProvider(supervisor)` wires the Tier-1 active-window read path (see ¬ß Active-Window Event Derivation) ‚Äî if `Start` itself fails (rare; usually fsnotify allocation), a single `slog.Warn` falls back to safety-net-only mode without aborting the server.

On SIGINT/SIGTERM, the shutdown handler runs `supervisor.Stop(ctx5s)` BEFORE `server.Shutdown(ctx)`. Stop errors are logged at `slog.Warn` and never block shutdown ‚Äî matches PR #197's daemon-log graceful-degradation pattern. The 5s bounded teardown matches the existing `tmux.TmuxTimeout = 10s` shape (control-mode subprocesses are expected to close cleanly within half that bound).

### API Server version/checker wiring (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`)

The version-exposure + update-checker wiring lives in `cmd/rk/serve.go` (NOT `NewRouterAndServer`) because it needs the ldflags-injected `main.version`, which is known only in `cmd/rk`. Immediately after `router, apiServer := api.NewRouterAndServer(ctx, logger)`:

```go
apiServer.SetVersion(version, newBootID(), resolveBrewInstalled()) // seed SSE event: version (version+boot+brew) + hold version on Server
updateChecker := updatecheck.New(version)                          // construct with the running version
updateChecker.OnQualify = apiServer.WireUpdateAvailableBroadcast() // bind BEFORE Start
updateChecker.Start(ctx)                                           // background poll, bound to serve ctx
apiServer.SetUpdateChecker(updateChecker)                          // inject so /api/update reads its snapshot
```

`newBootID()` / `resolveBrewInstalled()` are `cmd/rk/serve.go` helpers (since `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`): `newBootID` returns `hex.EncodeToString` of `bootIDBytes = 8` random bytes (‚áí 16 hex chars) from `crypto/rand`, or `""` on a rand failure (degrades to version-only reload ‚Äî no worse than before boot ids); `resolveBrewInstalled` resolves the self path once and tests the Cellar marker (`selfpath.Resolve` ‚Üí `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled`), reporting `false` on a resolve error. Both are computed ONCE per `rk serve` start and passed positionally into `SetVersion`.

The three `*api.Server` seams (all in `api/tmuxctl_bridge.go`, co-located with `SetWindowChangeSubscriber`/`SetActiveWindowProvider`):

- **`SetVersion(version, boot string, brew bool)`** ‚Äî (signature extended by `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette` from the single-string `SetVersion(version)`) stores `s.version = version` (a held copy) AND calls `s.initSSEHub()` + `s.sseHub.setVersion(version, boot, brew)` to seed the cached `event: version` slot with all three additive fields. Safe to call before any SSE client connects. **`s.version` now has a live reader**: `handleRestart`'s dev guard reads `s.version == devVersion` to `409` a restart on a dev build (see `/api/restart` in the API Layer table) ‚Äî so the struct field is no longer write-only (the `4zap` "latent dead field" note is retired; the anticipated future reader arrived with `3law`).
- **`SetUpdateChecker(c *updatecheck.Checker)`** ‚Äî stores `s.updateChecker = c` so `handleUpdate` reads its `Snapshot().Qualifies`. A nil checker makes `/api/update` report `409 no update available` for every request (the test/unwired-router degradation).
- **`WireUpdateAvailableBroadcast() func(current, latest string)`** ‚Äî `initSSEHub()`s then returns a closure `func(current, latest) { s.sseHub.broadcastUpdateAvailable(current, latest) }`, assigned to `checker.OnQualify`. The end-to-end chain: `updatecheck.checkOnce` ‚Üí `OnQualify(current, latest)` ‚Üí this closure ‚Üí `broadcastUpdateAvailable` ‚Üí caches `cachedUpdateAvailableJSON` + fans `event: update-available` to all clients.

The whole block sits before the tmuxctl Supervisor start and the HTTP listen. The checker suppresses itself for the `"dev"` sentinel / unparseable versions (so a local `go build` never fetches or notifies), and its goroutine exits on `ctx.Done()`.

#### Shared detached spawn-self seam (`spawnSelfFn`, `260714-3law-force-update-restart-palette`)

Both self-restarting handlers spawn a detached `rk <subcommand>` child through **ONE shared package-var seam** in `api/update.go` (generalized from `4zap`'s `spawnUpdateFn`, which was update-only):

```go
var spawnSelfFn = func(selfPath string, logName string, args ...string) error { ‚Ä¶ }  // exec.Command(selfPath, args...), Setsid, logs to ~/.rk/<logName>
```

- `handleUpdate` calls it `("update.log", "update")`; `handleRestart` calls it `("restart.log", "daemon", "restart")` ‚Äî two call sites, one implementation, no per-verb duplication. The two log names are `const`s (`updateLogRelPath` / `restartLogRelPath`) so the update and restart spawn logs stay independent.
- **Detached shape** (identical to `4zap`'s): `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` (own session/process group ‚Äî the child MUST outlive the server, because both `rk update` and `rk daemon restart` restart the daemon and kill the serving process mid-request), stdout/stderr redirected to `~/.rk/<logName>` via the generalized `openRkLog(logName)` (`O_APPEND|O_CREATE|O_WRONLY` 0644, `~/.rk` mkdir'd; **a log-open failure is non-fatal** ‚Äî the spawn proceeds without redirection), and a deferred parent-side `logFile.Close()` after `cmd.Start()` dups the fd into the child (the child keeps its own copy, so the log stays open for the detached process).
- **Deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** ‚Äî the Constitution ¬ßI timeout rule exists to stop a hung subprocess *blocking* the server, and a detached child that must survive the server cannot inherit the request/server context and cannot block it; argument-slice construction + no user-provided argv still hold.
- **Test seam**: the package var lets handler tests record `(logName, args)` without launching a real child ‚Äî the same seam pattern `4zap` established (mirrors `upgrade.go`'s `runBrewFn`/`restartDaemonFn`). The `resolveSelfPathFn` seam (default `selfpath.Resolve`) is shared by both handlers too.

### Constitution Alignment

- **¬ßI (Security First)** ‚Äî all subprocess calls in `tmuxctl/` use `exec.CommandContext` with explicit argument slices; no shell strings. The Client's `tmux -CC` invocation has no overall timeout because the connection is long-lived (per-call timeouts are not appropriate); the context is cancelled by `Close()` and propagates through the goroutine.
- **¬ßII (No Database)** ‚Äî no file is written under `~/.run-kit/`, `~/.cache/rk/`, or anywhere else. The Supervisor's `map[socket]*Client` mirrors the kernel-observable filesystem view of tmux sockets; nothing persists across `rk serve` lifetimes. The only persistent artefact in this neighbourhood is `~/.cache/rk/daemon.log` from PR #197, unchanged by this package.
- **¬ßVI (Tmux Sessions Survive Server Restarts)** ‚Äî `tmuxctl` observes tmux state changes and pushes them to SSE clients; it never mutates *user* sessions (it creates/reads only the `_rk-ctl` anchor and sets the server-scoped `exit-empty off` option ‚Äî never touching any window, pane, or user session). Since `260602-a1wo-prevent-exit-empty-server-death` the `_rk-ctl` anchor is created **on every observed server** (including the user's `default` with live sessions), as a permanent session floor ‚Äî NOT, as before, only on servers with zero pre-existing sessions. This is itself the deliberate Constitution VI *prevention*, not a violation: the floor + the server-global `set-option -g exit-empty off` (set imperatively in `productionDial` before the anchor on every dial/reconnect, plus baked into the embedded conf) together stop tmux's default `exit-empty on` from reaping a server when its session count momentarily hits zero ‚Äî the recurring failure (`runWork`/`utils`/`kit`, ‚â•3x) that killed live agent sessions. (Pre-`260602-qn62` this happened when the last real session closed and the remaining `rk-relay-*` ephemerals drained to zero; since `qn62` removed those ephemerals, the same backstop now also keeps an *empty home session* alive after its only window is pinned away into a `_rk-pin-*` session ‚Äî pin-session persistence relies on `exit-empty off`.) The anchor is harmless on a server with real sessions: it is filtered from every user-facing list (`tmux.ControlAnchorSessionName` chokepoint in `parseSessions`), ungrouped, and the control-mode connection attaches read-only (`-r`). Managed servers now die only via explicit `kill-server` / `rk reaper`; empty anchor-only servers persist by design (no auto-reaping, no cross-process state per ¬ßII).
- **No new network surface** ‚Äî the Client is a local subprocess attached via PTY. `ss -tlnp` still shows only the existing HTTP listener.

## SPA Static Serving

Dual-mode SPA serving in `app/backend/api/spa.go`. `hasEmbeddedAssets()` checks if the `embed.FS` contains real build output (more than `.gitkeep`):

- **Production** (`mountEmbeddedSPA`): serves from `embed.FS` via `fs.Sub(build.Frontend, "frontend")` + `http.FS`. SPA fallback rewrites to `index.html`.
- **Development** (`mountFilesystemSPA`): serves from `app/frontend/dist/` on the local filesystem. Path traversal prevented (resolved path must stay within SPA directory).

Both modes: any request not matching `/api/*`, `/relay/*`, or `/proxy/*` serves `index.html` for client-side routing. In development, Vite handles SPA fallback natively.

## Chrome Architecture

**Lazy-loaded components**: `CommandPalette`, `ThemeSelector`, and `CreateSessionDialog` are loaded via `React.lazy()` with dynamic `import()` (not static imports). Each uses `.then(m => ({ default: m.X }))` to re-wrap named exports for `React.lazy()` compatibility. Render sites wrapped in per-component `<Suspense fallback={null}>` boundaries. These components are overlays/dialogs that render conditionally ‚Äî lazy loading keeps them out of the initial bundle for faster first paint.

**Shell wrapper (CSS Grid topology)** ‚Äî `<Shell>` (`app/frontend/src/components/shell/shell.tsx`) is the shared chrome wrapper used by both `AppShell` and `BoardPage`. The shell is a single CSS Grid root carrying `height: var(--app-height, 100vh)` (preserves iOS keyboard handling via `useVisualViewport`). Desktop topology (`>= 640px`):

```
grid-template-areas:
  "sidebar topbar"
  "sidebar content"
  "sidebar bottombar"
grid-template-rows:    auto 1fr auto
grid-template-columns: ${sidebarWidth}px 1fr   (when sidebarOpen)
grid-template-columns: 0 1fr                   (when !sidebarOpen)
transition: grid-template-columns 150ms ease-out
```

Sidebar is full-height ‚Äî it spans all three rows and owns the entire left column. Topbar/content/bottombar stack in the right column. Sidebar collapse zeroes the first grid column (no 48px rail) ‚Äî the topbar/content/bottombar cells extend their left edge to page.left automatically; no JS-side conditional rendering or component mutation. The drag-resize handle is hidden when `sidebarOpen === false` (the only re-open affordance is the hamburger). Drag-handle wiring is AppShell-only ‚Äî `BoardPage` does not need a drag-handle (the dimension lives in `ChromeContext` and is shared).

Mobile topology (`< 640px`): single column, `grid-template-areas: "topbar" / "content" / "bottombar"`. Sidebar renders as an overlay child of the Shell positioned via `gridRow: "2/4"` (spans content + bottombar, leaves the topbar visible). Backdrop and `<aside>` use `position: absolute` (NOT `fixed inset-0`) so the overlay starts below the topbar ‚Äî matches the existing project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md`. The aside carries `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. Sidebar overlay open/close is driven by the same `sidebarOpen` state ‚Äî `drawerOpen` is removed from `ChromeContext`.

**Hamburger placement** ‚Äî the hamburger icon is statically rendered at `TopBar.left` in both `sidebarOpen` states. Visual "relocation" on collapse is a side effect of the grid column collapsing; there is no component-level relocation logic. When `sidebarOpen === true`, the hamburger sits at the sidebar.right / topbar.left seam (pixel-identical to "attached to sidebar"). When `sidebarOpen === false`, it sits at page.left because the topbar grid cell has extended to page.left.

**Keyboard toggle** ‚Äî `Cmd+\` (macOS) / `Ctrl+\` (Linux/Windows) toggles `sidebarOpen` from any route that mounts `<Shell>`. The chord is registered in the `KeyboardShortcuts` modal under "Toggle sidebar" per Constitution V (Keyboard-First). The chord is suppressed when focus is inside a real text input/textarea/contenteditable, but NOT when focus is on xterm.js's helper textarea (recognized by `target.closest('.xterm') != null`) ‚Äî without the xterm exception, the most common focus state would silently swallow the toggle.

**Sidebar width persistence** ‚Äî width state lives in `ChromeContext` (`sidebarWidth`). The dispatch surface is split: `setSidebarWidth(width)` updates in-memory state only (called per-pointermove during drag), and `persistSidebarWidth(width)` writes `localStorage["runkit-sidebar-width"]` (called once at drag-end). This explicit split avoids localStorage thrash on every pointer event. Callers like the AppShell drag handler track the last-seen width in a ref (`dragLastWidthRef`) and call `persistSidebarWidth` once in `handleEnd`.

**Routing branches inside the `content` grid area**:
- AppShell (`/$server/$window`): `<TerminalClient>` (the `tty` lens) | `<IframeWindow>` (the `web` lens) | `<ChatView>` (the `chat` lens) | `<SessionTiles>` (no window param). Since `260714-t97o-web-view-lens` the renderer is chosen by the **resolved view** (`chatViewActive ? ChatView : resolvedView === "web" && rkUrl ? IframeWindow : TerminalClient`, `chatViewActive = resolvedView === "chat"`), NOT by `@rk_type` identity ‚Äî the chat lens (`260714-r7rq`) folds into the SAME `resolveView` machinery; see `ui-patterns.md` ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model). The former tty-branch "Switch to iframe view" hint bar (which mutated `@rk_type`) was **removed** by that change.
- BoardPage (`/board/$name`): `DesktopRow` / `MobileCarousel` body (the existing horizontal-scroll panes), flush with `sidebar.right` (no left gutter).

No `max-w-4xl` constraint ‚Äî all zones span full width.

**ThemeProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/theme-context.tsx`) ‚Äî outermost provider. Split into ThemeStateContext (preference + resolved theme) and ThemeActionsContext (setTheme). Three modes: system, light, dark. Preference persisted to `localStorage` key `runkit-theme`. System mode listens to `matchMedia("(prefers-color-scheme: dark)")` change events. Theme applied via `data-theme` attribute on `<html>`. Blocking inline script in `index.html` `<head>` reads localStorage and sets `data-theme` before first paint (no-flicker initialization).

**ChromeProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/chrome-context.tsx`) ‚Äî split into two React contexts: `ChromeStateContext` (read-only state: `currentSession`, `currentWindow`, `sidebarOpen`, `sidebarWidth`, `isConnected`, `fixedWidth`) and `ChromeDispatchContext` (stable setter functions: `setCurrentSession`, `setCurrentWindow`, `setSidebarOpen` ‚Äî persists to `localStorage["runkit-sidebar-open"]`, `setSidebarWidth` ‚Äî in-memory only, `persistSidebarWidth(width)` ‚Äî writes localStorage on drag-end, `setIsConnected`, `toggleFixedWidth`). `drawerOpen`/`setDrawerOpen` were removed when the rotated shell collapsed the desktop-vs-mobile sidebar split into a single `sidebarOpen` boolean (the rendering form differs per breakpoint, the state does not). Chrome derives its content from the current selection ‚Äî no slot injection. `setLine2Left`, `setLine2Right`, `setBottomBar` removed; top bar and bottom bar read the selection directly. `Breadcrumb` type includes optional `dropdownItems` for session/window switching.

**FocusedTerminalContext** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/focused-terminal-context.tsx`) ‚Äî tracks the currently-focused terminal across the app so the shell-level `BottomBar` can target the right WebSocket regardless of route. Mounted in `RootWrapper` between `SessionProvider` and `OptimisticProvider`; provider tree order is `ThemeProvider > ChromeProvider > RootWrapper(SessionProvider > OptimisticProvider > FocusedTerminalProvider > Outlet)`. Shape:

```ts
type FocusedTerminal = {
  wsRef: React.RefObject<WebSocket | null>;
  server: string;
  session: string;
  windowIndex: string;
} | null;

type FocusedTerminalContextValue = {
  focused: FocusedTerminal;
  setFocused: (t: FocusedTerminal) => void;
  composeOpen: boolean;
  setComposeOpen: (open: boolean) => void;
};
```

Producers: `TerminalClient` registers on mount when its `registerFocus` prop is `true` (single-terminal route default) and clears on unmount. `BoardPane` registers when its `isFocused` prop becomes true (and on initial pane mount); it manages the registration itself and passes `registerFocus={false}` to its inner `TerminalClient` to avoid producer contention. `BoardPane` does NOT clear on focus loss ‚Äî the next pane to gain focus overwrites.

Consumers: the shell-level `BottomBar` reads `focused?.wsRef` (replacing the removed `wsRef` prop); the focused pane's `TerminalClient` reads `composeOpen` and gates `<ComposeBuffer>` rendering on `isFocused && composeOpen` (board route) or `composeOpen` (single-terminal route). `composeOpen` persists across route navigation by design ‚Äî the user dismisses explicitly via Escape. The compose target is frozen at open-time via `compose-buffer.tsx`'s existing wsRef snapshot on mount; cycling focus while compose is open does NOT retarget. When `focused === null` (e.g., Dashboard route with no terminal), BottomBar input handlers natural-no-op via the existing `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard.

**SessionProvider** (`app/frontend/src/contexts/session-context.tsx`) ‚Äî root-mounted multi-server React Context. One `SessionProvider` instance lives above `<Outlet />` in `RootWrapper` and is shared by every route (`/`, `/$server/...`, `/board/$name`); it does NOT remount on server-route switches. State is keyed per server: `sessionsByServer: Map<string, ProjectSession[]>`, `sessionOrderByServer: Map<string, string[]>`, `isConnectedByServer: Map<string, boolean>`, `metricsByServer: Map<string, MetricsSnapshot | null>`. It also exposes a scalar `hostMetricsConnected: boolean` (host-metrics source health for the Host-page connection dot, `260704-9o7k` ‚Äî see ¬ß Server-independent host-metrics subscription). *(The `/` page and its `top-bar` mode were renamed from Cockpit/Server Cabin to Host/tmux Server in `260715-zs1y`: the component is now `HostOverviewPage` in `host-overview-page.tsx`, and the page-mode strings are `"host"` (`/`) and `"server"` (`/$server`), was `"cockpit"`/`"root"`.)* `currentServer: string | null` is dispatched from the matched route via `useMatches()` ‚Äî `params.server` for `/$server/...`, `null` for `/board/$name` and `/`. Consumers read the per-server slice they need via `ctx.sessionsByServer.get(name)`; there is no transitional accessor ‚Äî all consumers consume the keyed shape directly. Provider tree order: `ThemeProvider > ChromeProvider > RootWrapper(SessionProvider > OptimisticProvider > Outlet)`. The provider mirrors `currentServer`'s connection state into `ChromeProvider` so existing chrome consumers (top-bar connection dot) keep working unchanged. Persists most-recently active server to `localStorage` key `runkit-server` (single value, not split per server).

**State-socket transport (since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`; was a per-server EventSource pool)** ‚Äî the provider owns ONE `StateSocket` per tab (`src/lib/state-socket.ts`, ¬ß State Socket above) held in `socketRef`, replacing the former one-EventSource-per-server pool (which connected each to `/api/sessions/stream?server=<name>`). The current server is auto-attached; non-current servers attach lazily via the `attachServer(name)` API exposed on context ‚Äî `attachServer`/`unsubscribe`/every `subscribe*` seam keeps its exact signature so no consumer above the seams changed. The `attachedSet` drives a diff effect that `subscribeServer`/`unsubscribeServer`s (ref-counted on the socket); each subscribe `ack` updates only that server's slice. When a server disappears from `/api/servers` it is unsubscribed and its entries removed from every per-server map. A 3-second disconnect debounce runs per server, driven by socket-level connection-state changes ‚Äî an `onerror` doesn't flip a still-acked server's `isConnectedByServer` until the debounce fires. `useBoards` and `useWindowPins` call `attachServer` for every known server when the sidebar mounts (they now cost nothing on the pool budget ‚Äî one shared WS).

**`subscribeBoardChange`** (`session-context.tsx`) ‚Äî context API that lets any consumer register a `(server: string) => void` handler and receive cross-server `board-changed` events through the one shared socket. `useBoards` and `useWindowPins` use it to react to per-server board mutations without opening their own connections ‚Äî the state socket already streams `board-changed` (as `kind:"server"`), so multiplexing through one subscriber API keeps the wire-subscription count bounded. (Signature unchanged across the transport swap ‚Äî it always operated above the transport seam.)

**Server-independent host-metrics subscription + `useHostMetrics()`** (`session-context.tsx`, since `260701-vshd-cockpit-host-console-home`; transport is the state socket's `metrics` subscription since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`) ‚Äî a `subscribeMetrics()` on the shared socket (the in-band `kind:"metrics"` op, internally the retained `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel) that receives ONLY the server-independent `metrics`/`services` global events, so host health is available where there is no `currentServer` and no per-server subscription to carry it (the Host-page host-console home `/`; see ui-patterns.md ¬ß HOST HEALTH Zone). It is **opened only when `attachedSet.size === 0`** (`hostMetricsWanted`) and dropped once any server attaches ‚Äî the per-server subscription's `metrics` event already fans the same server-global payload into the shared `hostMetrics` state. The former dedicated-stream mutual-exclusion still holds, but no longer for pool-budget reasons: the one WebSocket holds no HTTP/1.1 pool slot at all (the connection-starvation motivation that drove this is exactly what the state socket eliminated ‚Äî see ¬ß State Socket / ui-patterns.md ¬ß Desktop Relay-Connection Suspension). A `metricsSubscribedRef` guard drives the subscribe/unsubscribe; the socket effect's cleanup resets it (+ `subscribedServersRef`/`ackedServersRef`) so a StrictMode remount re-subscribes on the fresh socket (¬ß State Socket ‚Üí StrictMode safety). The parsed snapshot lands in provider state `hostMetrics` (`MetricsSnapshot | null`, `null` pre-tick) exposed via `HostMetricsContext` + the `useHostMetrics(): MetricsSnapshot | null` hook. **`useHostMetrics()` is NOT `currentServer`-gated** ‚Äî unlike `useMetrics()` (which returns `currentServer ? metricsByServer.get(currentServer) : null`, hence `null` on `/`); both hooks use the same undefined-sentinel throw-outside-provider idiom. `useMetrics()` (current-server-scoped, for `HostPanel`'s sidebar call site) is unchanged. Backend contract for the `metrics` subscription / `metricsOnlyServer` sentinel: see ¬ß State Socket + ¬ß API Layer `/ws/state`.

**Host-metrics stream health (`hostMetricsConnected`, `260704-9o7k-top-bar-button-pyramid`)** ‚Äî the health of the host-metrics *source*, exposed on `SessionContextType` as a `hostMetricsConnected: boolean` for the **Host-page connection dot** (`host-overview-page.tsx` passes it as `isConnected` to `<TopBar mode="host">`, replacing the old hardcoded `isConnected={false}`; see ui-patterns.md ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí connection dot). This closes the gap where the dedicated `?metrics=1` stream's health was previously **untracked**. Two sources, mirroring the dedicated-stream ‚Üî per-server-fan-out switch above:
- **Dedicated-subscription health** ‚Äî while `hostMetricsWanted` (attached set empty, so the `metrics` subscription IS the source), a `dedicatedMetricsConnected` state tracks it: set `true` on the metrics subscription's `ack` (or a recovered socket connection while it is acked), cleared via a **3s debounce** driven by the socket's `onConnectionChange` ‚Äî so a transient socket blip doesn't flicker the dot. The flag is reset when a server attaches (the `hostMetricsWanted ‚Üí false` branch unsubscribes metrics and drops `METRICS_SUB` from `ackedServersRef`). `false` until the first metrics `ack`. (Transport swapped from a dedicated `?metrics=1` EventSource to the shared socket's `metrics` subscription by `260716-qf3j-state-socket`.)
- **Per-server fan-out fallback** ‚Äî when a per-server subscription is attached (metrics subscription dropped, the fan-out now carries host metrics), the derived value reads `true` iff **any** attached server slice `isConnected` (that server is delivering the server-global `metrics` event).

The exposed `hostMetricsConnected` is a `useMemo` selecting between the two: `hostMetricsWanted ? dedicatedMetricsConnected : (any slice connected)`. It is added to the context type, both provider `value` memos (+ deps), and `StandaloneSessionContextProvider` defaults (`false`).

**Kill-redirect gate (`currentWindowEverSeen`)** ‚Äî The "session/window gone" redirect in `app/frontend/src/app.tsx` (around the `useEffect` that calls `computeKillRedirect` from `app/frontend/src/lib/navigation.ts`) MUST NOT fire for a freshly-navigated URL whose (session, window) pair has not yet been observed as valid in the SSE `sessions` stream. `computeKillRedirect` accepts a `currentWindowEverSeen?: boolean` param (defaults to `true` for legacy callers and unit tests) and short-circuits to `null` when false ‚Äî bypassing both the "session gone ‚Üí dashboard" and "window gone ‚Üí nearest sibling" branches. The caller maintains two refs: `currentWindowEverSeenRef` (boolean, flipped `true` whenever the memoized `currentWindow` is non-null) and `lastObservedUrlKeyRef` (string, `${server}|${session}|${window}`). Any URL-key change resets the seen flag to `false`. This gates two transient SSE states that are not proof the URL is unreachable: (a) a stale cached first payload that replays an older server snapshot before delivering current data, and (b) a session whose `windows` array is briefly empty while tmux enumeration propagates into the next poll tick. Without the gate, either state makes `currentSession` or `currentWindow` null on the first SSE event after navigation, the redirect fires, and `TerminalClient` unmounts mid-initialization ‚Äî surfacing as an e2e flake where `.xterm-screen` briefly appears then disappears. Genuine kills from another client still redirect normally, because the URL key only resets on navigation, not on SSE payload changes: once the seen flag is `true`, a subsequent payload that drops the window triggers the redirect as before.

**Window state (Zustand)** ‚Äî window optimistic state is managed by a Zustand store at `app/frontend/src/store/window-store.ts`, keyed by the immutable tmux `windowId` (`@N`). `zustand` is a production dependency in `app/frontend/package.json`. The store tracks `killed` and `pendingName` overrides per window ID, and ghost windows awaiting SSE confirmation. `AppShell` drives `setWindowsForSession` from SSE `rawSessions`. `OptimisticContext` retains session and server optimistic state only (name-based keys, not index-based). See ui-patterns.md "Zustand Window Store" section for full shape and action surface.

**`WindowInfo` type** (`app/frontend/src/types.ts`) ‚Äî includes `windowId: string` (non-optional) as the immutable tmux `@N` identifier, alongside `index: number` (tmux ordering, display-only, not used as a store key). Backend populates `windowId` from `#{window_id}` in the `ListWindows()` format string. `color?: string` ‚Äî optional color-value descriptor (`"4"` single index or `"1+3"` blend) from the tmux `@color` user option (was `number` before `260615-6rnr-expand-swatch-palette-blends`); `ProjectSession.sessionColor?: string` is the analogous per-session field. `panes?: PaneInfo[]` is an optional field (undefined when absent ‚Äî existing fixtures omit it without type error). `PaneInfo` type: `{ paneId: string; paneIndex: number; cwd: string; command: string; isActive: boolean }`. `rkType?: string` ‚Äî `"iframe"` or undefined; determines frontend renderer (terminal vs iframe). `rkUrl?: string` ‚Äî URL for iframe windows; populated from tmux `@rk_url` user-defined option. Both fields use `omitempty` on backend / optional on frontend ‚Äî terminal windows omit them. `WindowEntry` in `window-store.ts` gains `panes: PaneInfo[]` (non-optional, defaults to `[]` when absent from incoming `WindowInfo`); `setWindowsForSession` syncs panes from incoming data on every SSE tick.

**`MetricsSnapshot` type** (`app/frontend/src/types.ts`) ‚Äî mirrors the backend `metrics.MetricsSnapshot` struct. Fields: `hostname` (string), `cpu` (`{ samples: number[], current: number, cores: number }`), `memory` (`{ used: number, total: number }` bytes), `load` (`{ avg1, avg5, avg15: number, cpus: number }`), `disk` (`{ used: number, total: number }` bytes), `uptime` (number, seconds). Rendered by the shared `HostMetrics` presentational component (ui-patterns.md ¬ß HostPanel / HOST HEALTH Zone), fed from `useMetrics()` (sidebar `HostPanel`, current-server-scoped) or `useHostMetrics()` (the `/` zone, server-independent ‚Äî see ¬ß Server-independent host-metrics subscription above), both via `SessionProvider` context.

**TopBar** (`app/frontend/src/components/top-bar.tsx`) ‚Äî the full-width top bar / navbar; reads from ChromeProvider + its props. Since `260702-6m46-full-width-topbar-navbar` it spans both columns of the Shell grid (`app.tsx`/`board-page.tsx`) or is pinned above the Host page's scroll container (`host-overview-page.tsx`, no Shell). Single line (`border-b-[3px] border-border`). LEFT is a breadcrumb `<nav>`: the brand (logo + `hidden sm:inline` "Run Kit" wordmark) as the left-most `<a href="/">` root crumb, then (where a sidebar exists) the hamburger, then the mode-specific crumbs, `‚Ä∫`-separated. RIGHT is a **3-level cumulative button pyramid** (`260704-9o7k`): L1 terminal-only (split √ó2 + FixedWidthToggle) ‚Üí L2 terminal+board (terminal-font `Aa` + close/unpin ‚úï) ‚Üí L3 always-in-every-mode (Notification ‚Üí Theme ‚Üí Refresh ‚Üí Help) ‚Üí the right-most connection dot (now rendered in **all four modes**). The old right-side "Run Kit" anchor is GONE (it moved to the left as the root crumb). See ui-patterns.md ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí Right cluster + ¬ß Shell Grid Layout for the full per-mode breakdown and the crumb/affordance vocabulary.

**TopBar `mode` prop** ‚Äî `mode: "terminal" | "board" | "server" | "host"` (default `"terminal"`; the `host` mode was added by `260702-6m46`, renamed from `"cockpit"` in `260715-zs1y`) controls the left-nav content. AppShell passes `"terminal"` (server link + session/window dropdown crumbs) or `"server"` (tmux Server ‚Äî server name as the `aria-current` leaf, which REPLACED the deleted literal "Dashboard" label; the mode string was `"root"` before `260715-zs1y`). `HostOverviewPage` passes `"host"` (brand crumb only ‚Äî no hamburger, no terminal-font/split/close, and no FixedWidth button since `260704-9o7k`; renders the L3 always-block Notification/Theme/Refresh/Help **plus the connection dot**, passing `hostMetricsConnected` as `isConnected`). BoardPage passes `"board"` with `boardName`/`paneCount`/`serverCount`: brand + hamburger + `‚Ä∫` + `BoardModeBreadcrumb` (`Board ‚ñ∏ {name} ‚ñæ` via the shared `BreadcrumbDropdown`) + inline-info `{N} pane[s] ¬∑ {M} server[s] ¬∑ ‚åò[‚åò] cycle`, `hidden sm:inline`, plus the L2 pair (Aa + the ‚úï, which is a real **close-pane kill** of the focused tile's active pane since `260715-6jwn` ‚Äî reversing the earlier unpin behavior; unpin moved to the tile-header pin-glyph + palette) and the L3 always-block; board mode also renders the two L1 SplitButtons (wired to the focused tile's window via the slot's `focusedPane`, `260715-6jwn`). It passes a `boardConnected` AND-over-attached-servers value as `isConnected`. Since `260704-9o7k` the connection dot renders in **all four modes** (the former board/host hide-gate is gone); its per-page meaning ("this page's live data is flowing") is derived by each caller. See ui-patterns.md ¬ß Chrome (Top Bar) ‚Üí Right cluster.

**BoardPage adopts Shell** ‚Äî `BoardPage` (`app/frontend/src/components/board/board-page.tsx`) wraps its body in `<Shell>` like AppShell; the bespoke `h-screen w-screen flex` root, the inline mini-header (`Board ‚ñ∏ {name} ‚ñæ`), and the per-route mini-sidebar wrapper are gone. `BoardSwitcherDropdown` moved to/imported by `TopBar` in board mode. BoardPage gets a `<BottomBar>` for the first time ‚Äî the board route had none pre-change. The `<BottomBar />` invocation is byte-identical across AppShell and BoardPage: the same three callbacks (`onOpenCompose`, `onFocusTerminal`, `onScrollLockChange`) are wired identically. `onOpenCompose` calls `setComposeOpen(true)` from `FocusedTerminalContext`; `onFocusTerminal` invokes a ref-tracked `focusFocusedPaneRef.current()` that re-focuses the currently-focused board pane; `onScrollLockChange` plumbs through `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel` ‚Üí `BoardPane` ‚Üí `TerminalClient.scrollLocked`.

**Sidebar** (`app/frontend/src/components/sidebar/`) ‚Äî session/window tree with bottom-aligned collapsible panels. The same `<Sidebar>` instance renders for both AppShell (`/$server/...`) and BoardPage (`/board/$name`); BoardPage no longer ships its own mini-sidebar. Sessions are grouped per server ‚Äî one `CollapsiblePanel`-style group per server in `servers`, each fed by its slice from `sessionsByServer`. The `currentServer` group carries a visual marker; on board routes (`currentServer === null`) no group is marked. Desktop: drag-resizable (default 220px, min 160, max 400, persisted to `localStorage`), collapsible via `‚ò∞`. Mobile (< 768px): drawer overlay from the left, triggered by `‚ò∞`. Layout: ServerPanel -> Boards section -> per-server session groups (`flex-1 overflow-y-auto`) -> WindowPanel (collapsible, `storageKey="runkit-panel-window"`) -> HostPanel (collapsible, `storageKey="runkit-panel-host"`). The Sidebar reads multi-server state from context (`sessionsByServer`, `sessionOrderByServer`, `isConnectedByServer`, `metricsByServer`); `currentServer` is passed in as a prop (AppShell reads it from context and forwards; BoardPage passes `null`). Action callbacks (create/kill, resize start, select) come in as props.

**BottomBar** (`app/frontend/src/components/bottom-bar.tsx`) ‚Äî rendered at shell level via `<Shell>`'s `bottombar` grid area on every route that mounts `<Shell>` (single-terminal, board, dashboard). Width tracks the right grid column (page width minus sidebar). Single row of `<kbd>` buttons: modifier toggles (Ctrl/Alt with sticky armed state ‚Äî Cmd removed), Esc, Tab, arrow keys, Fn dropdown (F1-F12, PgUp/PgDn, Home/End). No compose button (moved to top bar). Buttons: 36px desktop (`min-h-[36px] min-w-[36px]`), 44px touch (`coarse:min-h-[44px] coarse:min-w-[36px]`). Modifier state managed by `useModifierState` hook (Ctrl/Alt only). The `wsRef` prop was removed from `BottomBarProps` ‚Äî input handlers read `focused?.wsRef` from `FocusedTerminalContext` and send ANSI escape sequences through it. When `focused === null` (Dashboard route, no terminal), input handlers natural-no-op via the existing `wsRef.current?.readyState !== OPEN` guard ‚Äî no error, no toast.

**ComposeBuffer** (`app/frontend/src/components/compose-buffer.tsx`) ‚Äî native `<textarea>` overlay triggered by the compose button or file upload. Supports iOS dictation, autocorrect, paste, multiline. Send button (or Cmd/Ctrl+Enter) transmits entire text as a single WebSocket message. Terminal dims (`opacity-50`) while compose is open. Escape dismisses without sending. Accepts optional `initialText` prop for pre-populating with uploaded file paths; appends on subsequent updates while open.

**iOS Keyboard Support** ‚Äî `useVisualViewport` hook (`app/frontend/src/hooks/use-visual-viewport.ts`) listens to both `resize` and `scroll` events on `window.visualViewport`, setting `--app-height` CSS custom property from `visualViewport.height`. In the single-view model (fullbleed always on), `globals.css` applies `position: fixed; inset: 0; height: var(--app-height, 100vh)` to the app shell. The bottom bar stays pinned above the keyboard; the terminal shrinks via `flex-1` and xterm refits via `ResizeObserver`.

**iOS Touch Scroll Prevention** ‚Äî Fullbleed is always active in the single-view model. The `fullbleed` class is added to `<html>` by `useVisualViewport` on mount (also present as a static default in `index.html` for FOUC prevention). `globals.css` applies `overflow: hidden` and `overscroll-behavior: none` to both `html` and `body` via `html.fullbleed` selectors, preventing iOS Safari elastic bounce scrolling. The terminal container div uses `touch-none` (`touch-action: none`) so the browser yields touch gestures to xterm.js for scrollback handling.

**Browser title** ‚Äî `useBrowserTitle` hook sets `document.title` dynamically based on hostname (fetched once from `GET /api/health` on app init) and route params. Dashboard: `RunKit ‚Äî {hostname}`. Terminal: `{session}/{window} ‚Äî {hostname}`. Omits hostname suffix when empty. Static `<title>RunKit</title>` in `index.html` remains as pre-hydration fallback.
