Single-view model: there are no page transitions or per-page chrome injection. The chrome reads the current selection and renders directly.

## CLI Subcommands (Cobra)

`app/backend/cmd/rk/` uses `spf13/cobra` for CLI management. `root.go` declares `var version = "dev"` (overridden by ldflags) and registers all subcommands. `main.go` just calls `execute()`. Version info via `--version`/`-v` global flag (Cobra built-in, not a subcommand).

**Shared output convention ‚Äî persistent `--quiet` + `outputSink`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9). A single **persistent `--quiet` bool** is registered on `rootCmd` (`root.go`, bound to package-level `quiet`), so every present and future subcommand accepts it uniformly and inherits it with zero registration work; it is a deliberate no-op on any command not yet routed through the sink (incremental adoption). The convention, decided once, lives in `cmd/rk/output.go` (package `main`, no `internal/` package for a CLI-only concern): **`outputSink{data, chatter io.Writer}`** with `Dataf` (data channel) / `Notef` (chatter channel). **stdout carries data** ‚Äî machine-consumable results (outcome lines, `--json` documents, requested previews/lists) ‚Äî never gated by `--quiet`; **stderr carries chatter** ‚Äî progress/decoration ‚Äî routed to `io.Discard` under `--quiet`. **Errors always survive** (they flow through `RunE` returns and ungated stderr writes); `--quiet` never changes exit codes; a successful run with nothing to report is silent under `--quiet`. Built on `cmd.OutOrStdout()`/`cmd.ErrOrStderr()` (never bare `os.Stdout`/`os.Stderr`) so gating is unit-testable ‚Äî the idiom `doctor.go`/`agent_setup.go` already used; `newSink(cmd)` reads `--quiet` off the invoked command (falling back to the package var for a bare test command), `newSinkWriters(data, chatter)` builds a test sink from explicit writers. **Adopted by `update`/`doctor`/`agent-setup`** (the audit-named chatter carriers ‚Äî see their rows); `reaper` takes a display cap instead of a quiet conversion (its output is all data ‚Äî see its row). This flipped toolkit Principle 9 to conformant ‚Äî see [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) ¬ß Requirement: Bounded, high-signal output (Principle 9).

| Subcommand | File | Behavior |
|------------|------|----------|
| *(none)* | `root.go` | Defaults to `serve` (backwards compat) |
| `serve` | `serve.go` | Start HTTP server (foreground-only) ‚Äî loads config from env vars, chi router, graceful shutdown via SIGINT/SIGTERM. No lifecycle flags (the pre-`260528-5zvv` `-d`/`--restart`/`--stop` flags were removed in a hard break ‚Äî use `rk daemon ...` instead). Still imports `internal/daemon` for `daemon.LogEnvVar` consumed by `setupSlog`'s tee-to-file logic |
| `daemon` | `daemon.go`, `daemon_start.go`, `daemon_stop.go`, `daemon_restart.go`, `daemon_status.go`, `daemon_portowner.go` | Top-level command tree (sibling of `serve`, not nested) managing the background daemon. Subcommands: `start [--force]`, `stop [--force]`, `restart [--force]`, `status [--json]`. `--force` overrides the port-claim safety check by SIGTERMing a non-daemon port owner (graceful-then-forceful via `terminateOwner`); refuses to kill itself when the owner PID matches `daemon.InnerServePID()`. `status` is read-only and rejects `--force`. Port-owner lookup via `lsof -ti:<port>` ‚Üí `ss -tlnp` fallback in shared `daemon_portowner.go` (port-only query, host pass-through for display, `exec.CommandContext` 5s timeout). Subcommand vars (`daemonStartCmd`, etc.) injectable in tests via package-level `var findPortOwner = findPortOwnerImpl` and `var innerServePIDFn = daemon.InnerServePID`. See `## Daemon Lifecycle` for full semantics |
| `update` | `upgrade.go` | Alias: `upgrade`. Detect Homebrew install via the shared `internal/selfpath` package (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade` ‚Äî `resolveExeFn` now defaults to `selfpath.Resolve` and detection is `selfpath.IsBrewInstalled(resolved)` / `strings.Index(resolved, selfpath.CellarMarker)`; the `/Cellar/run-kit/` marker + resolver were extracted so this CLI path and `api/update.go`'s `POST /api/update` share ONE brew-detection impl that cannot drift ‚Äî see ¬ß Backend Libraries `internal/selfpath`). The Cellar marker follows the `run-kit` formula name since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`. If Homebrew: `brew update --quiet`, check latest version via `brew info --json=v2`, skip if already up to date, else `brew upgrade sahil87/tap/run-kit` + auto-restart daemon via `daemon.RestartWithBinary(brewBinPath)` where `brewBinPath` is derived from the Cellar path (`<brewPrefix>/bin/run-kit`), not stale `os.Executable()`. Non-Homebrew: print the single fully-qualified reinstall hint `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit` (never the unqualified `brew install run-kit` ‚Äî homebrew-core ships an unrelated `run-kit` formula that wins unqualified resolution). **`--skip-brew-update` flag** (local cobra bool, default `false`; since `260531-ckwv-skip-brew-update-flag`): gates ONLY the internal `brew update --quiet` tap-metadata refresh; the `brew info` version check, up-to-date short-circuit, `brew upgrade`, and daemon restart all still run. Default (flag absent) behavior is byte-for-byte unchanged. The three brew call sites and the daemon restart route through package-level seam vars (`runBrewFn`, `restartDaemonFn`, `resolveExeFn`) matching the `innerServePIDFn` idiom so `upgrade_test.go` can stub them without spawning `brew` or restarting a real daemon. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9 ‚Äî see ¬ß CLI Subcommands intro for the shared `outputSink`): the RunE builds `newSink(cmd)` and routes progress/decoration (`Current version: v‚Ä¶`, `Updating v‚Ä¶ ‚Üí v‚Ä¶`, `Restarting run-kit daemon‚Ä¶`, `run-kit daemon started (‚Ä¶)`) through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`) while routing **outcome lines** (`Already up to date (v‚Ä¶).`, `Updated to v‚Ä¶.`, and the not-a-Homebrew-install guidance block ‚Äî silence there would misreport a no-op as success) through `Dataf` (data, survives). The **streamed brew subprocess output** is the definitional "raw brew output" chatter: the `brewStreams(quiet)` helper selects the `update`/`upgrade` stdout/stderr ‚Äî under `--quiet` stdout ‚Üí `io.Discard` and stderr is **buffered** into a `*bytes.Buffer` (non-nil only under quiet), so on a non-zero exit `runBrewFn` **wraps the captured stderr detail into the returned error** (a failing `rk update --quiet` keeps its diagnostics rather than a bare `exit status 1` ‚Äî R2's errors-always-survive rule; cycle-1 rework). Non-quiet runs stream to the real `os.Stdout`/`os.Stderr` (a nil errBuf ‚Äî the detail is already on the terminal). The `info` path is unaffected (it captures stdout via `.Output()`; its bytes are data) |
| `doctor` | `doctor.go` | Check runtime dependencies only ‚Äî `exec.LookPath("tmux")`. Exit 1 if any check fails (worst-check-wins). **`--json`** (`260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`, toolkit Principle 2): emits a structured `{ok, checks:[{name, ok, hint}]}` document to **stdout** (data), where `ok` is the worst-check-wins overall verdict; exit stays 0 all-pass / 1 any-fail. The **human diagnostic output goes to stderr** (`cmd.ErrOrStderr()`, bound as `stderr`) ‚Äî it is diagnostics, not the data a machine parses ‚Äî and is unchanged by the flag. The verdict is computed once in the pure `runDoctorChecks() doctorReport` so the human and JSON renderers share one source of truth. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9): the human path builds `newSink(cmd)` and routes the `Checking runtime dependencies‚Ä¶` banner, per-check `[ OK ]` rows, and the `All checks passed.` tail through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`); **`[FAIL]` rows carry the remediation hint** (actionable error detail) and are written to **ungated stderr** so they survive `--quiet`, along with the non-zero exit. The `--json` path is untouched ‚Äî `--quiet --json` emits exactly the JSON document to stdout |
| `status` | `status.go` | List tmux sessions with window counts via `internal/tmux.ListSessions()` + `ListWindows()`. No server required. **`--json`** (`260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`, toolkit Principle 2): emits a stable JSON array of `{name, windows}` to stdout via `writeSessionStatusJSON(ctx, cmd, server, sessions)` (context-first arg order); human output unchanged otherwise. **Empty-vs-error semantics** (both mirror the human path, both verified empirically): a **cleanly-absent** server (no tmux server for the `runkit` socket) is empty-success ‚Äî `[]` + exit 0, stderr empty (deliberate `internal/tmux.ListSessions` behavior ‚Äî an empty result is data, not a failure); an **errorful unreachability** (stale socket / permission ‚Äî a genuine tmux failure) surfaces the error on stderr with a non-zero exit and **no partial JSON** on stdout (unlike the human path, which prints a per-session error line and continues, the JSON path fails the whole command so a consumer never parses a truncated document as complete). See [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) ¬ß `status --json` empty-vs-error semantics |
| `url` | `url.go` | **Prints the config-derived run-kit server URL** (`260718-icxz-skill-display-topic-url-retire-context`) ‚Äî `http://<host>:<port>\n` from `config.Load()` (`RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT`, default `127.0.0.1:3000`, port-validated) to `cmd.OutOrStdout()`, exit 0, empty stderr. `Args: cobra.NoArgs`, `SilenceUsage`. The derivation is **byte-equal to the deleted `context.go` `serverURL()`** (`fmt.Sprintf("http://%s:%d", cfg.Host, cfg.Port)`) and reuses `internal/config.Load()` ‚Äî no `.env` read, no port-owner/liveness probe. It is a **config-derived heuristic** (what the server *would* bind given this environment), stated plainly in the `Long` text ‚Äî NOT proof a server is running; smarter port-owner discovery is a deferred enhancement, and `rk url` existing is the seam that keeps that door open. It is the **stable server-URL seam** an agent (or the `rk skill` bundle's "Where am I" recipe) uses in place of the retired `rk context` extraction (`rk context 2>/dev/null \| grep 'Server URL' \| awk '{print $NF}'`). Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go`; appears in `help-dump` automatically. Covered by `url_test.go` (defaults + `RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT` override, empty stderr, registration) |
| `skill` | `skill.go` | **The toolkit `<tool> skill` contract** (`260717-agst-rk-skill-agent-setup-hooks-only`; gained **topic pages** in `260718-icxz-skill-display-topic-url-retire-context`) ‚Äî prints run-kit's canonical **static** agent skill bundle (a one-page usage briefing: when to reach for rk, its capabilities, composition, gotchas) as raw markdown to `cmd.OutOrStdout()`, **byte-identical** to `docs/site/skill.md`, empty stderr, exit 0. `SilenceUsage`. No rendering/pager/framing ‚Äî stdout is data; static-only (carries NO session/pane/server-URL state ‚Äî an agent derives its location directly via the core bundle's "Where am I" recipe and the server URL from `rk url`, the dynamic residue formerly served by the retired `rk context`), so its bytes never vary by where/when it runs. **Topic pages (`260718-icxz`, per the merged shll skill standard, PR #47):** `Args` widened `cobra.NoArgs` ‚Üí **`cobra.MaximumNArgs(1)`**; bare `rk skill` prints the core bundle, `rk skill <topic>` prints one topic page (`docs/site/skill/<topic>.md`) under the same byte-identical/stdout-only contract, and an **unknown topic fails fast** ‚Äî `usageError(fmt.Errorf("unknown topic %q (valid: %s)", topic, ‚Ä¶))` ‚Üí **usage-class exit 2**, error naming the valid topics on **stderr**, **empty stdout** (never a silent empty document, never exit 0). Topics live in a `map[string][]byte` (`skillTopics`, v1: `display` ‚Üí the panes/iframes/Visual-Display-Recipe depth that would blow the core's ‚â§150 budget); `skillTopicNames()` returns them sorted for a deterministic error message. Bare `rk skill` **never inlines** any topic page. **Embed mechanism (mirrors shll's `standards`, extended per-topic):** the canonical `docs/site/skill.md` **and each `docs/site/skill/<topic>.md`** sit above the `app/backend/` module root so `//go:embed` cannot reach them directly; `scripts/sync-skill.sh` (`set -euo pipefail`, runs from repo root; also wired as a `//go:generate` directive in `skill.go`) copies **both** the core bundle ‚Üí `cmd/rk/skill/skill.md` and the display topic ‚Üí `cmd/rk/skill/display.md` (one `sync` call per file ‚Äî add a row per new topic), which `//go:embed skill/skill.md` (`skillBundle`) and `//go:embed skill/display.md` (`skillDisplayTopic`) embed ‚Äî so a clean `go build ./...` (which runs no script) compiles. `skill_test.go` is the drift guard ‚Äî **one byte-equality + one line-budget test per embedded file**: `TestSkillEmbedMatchesCanonical` / `TestSkillBundleWithinLineBudget` for the core, and `TestSkillDisplayEmbedMatchesCanonical` / `TestSkillDisplayWithinLineBudget` for the topic (each `bytes.Equal`s the embed against its `../../../../docs/site/...` canonical, hinting `scripts/sync-skill.sh` on failure, and pins ‚â§150 lines ‚Äî the standard's ceiling; the display topic is 81 lines), plus command tests `TestSkillCmdPrintsBundleByteIdentical` / `TestSkillBareStillPrintsCoreBundle` / `TestSkillDisplayPrintsTopicByteIdentical` / `TestSkillUnknownTopicFailsFast`. Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go`; appears in `help-dump` automatically (cobra-tree walk); topic pages render at `/run-kit/skill/<topic>` on shll.ai for free on next pull |
| `init-conf` | `initconf.go` | Scaffold default tmux.conf to `~/.rk/tmux.conf` from embedded config and create `~/.rk/tmux.d/` drop-in directory. `--force` to overwrite config (tmux.d contents untouched) |
| `notify` | `notify.go` | `rk notify <message>` (optional `--title` flag) ‚Äî sends a Web Push notification to all subscribed devices. Resolves the local server base URL via `config.Load()` (`RK_HOST`/`RK_PORT`, default `127.0.0.1:3000` ‚Äî the same derivation the `url` command exposes) and POSTs `{title, body}` to `{base}/api/notify` under an 8s context timeout. **Fail-silent**: any failure (server unreachable, POST error, non-2xx, timeout) ‚Üí exit 0 with no stdout/stderr (`SilenceErrors`/`SilenceUsage` set) so a notify failure never stalls the caller (the fab-kit operator loop). Registered on `rootCmd` in `root.go` `init()`. See `## Web Push Notifications` (`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications`) |
| `riff` | `riff.go` | Create a worktree, open a new tmux window in it, and launch a Claude Code session. Repeatable pane flags: `--skill <skill>` (claude pane), `--cmd <cmd>` (shell pane) ‚Äî argv order sets pane order; bare forms allowed (blank claude / bare shell). Layout flags: `--layout <name>` accepts 6 canonical tmux layouts + 6 shortforms (`a`/`t`/`h`/`v`/`deck-h`/`deck-v`); default `auto` picks by pane count. Preset flags: positional `rk riff <preset>` or `--preset <name>` resolve config-defined presets (`riff.presets.<name>` in `fab/project/config.yaml`); `--list-presets` prints them and exits. Fan-out: `--fan-out N` spawns N identical windows in parallel, each with its own `wt` worktree. `-- <wt-flags...>` passthrough to `wt create`. Preconditions: `$TMUX` set + `wt` on PATH (fast-fail, exit 1 ‚Äî the operational/precondition class since `260717-rex1`; was 2). Launcher resolved by shelling out to `fab agent --print` (fab-kit's default-tier session command) via `resolveLauncher`; silent best-effort fallback to `claude --dangerously-skip-permissions` when `fab` is absent/fails. All subprocess calls via `exec.CommandContext` (wt: 30s, tmux: 10s). `tmux.OriginalTMUX` restored in child env so tmux targets the user's current server. Exit codes since `260717-rex1` conform to the toolkit convention (Principle 4): precondition (`$TMUX` unset / `wt` missing) ‚Üí 1 (operational), validation/usage (unknown layout, invalid `--count`, unknown/conflicting preset) ‚Üí 2, subprocess (wt/tmux non-zero, parse failure, timeout) ‚Üí 3. A manual flag-parse error (`rk riff --nope`, `DisableFlagParsing` bypasses the root `FlagErrorFunc`) is wrapped locally as the CLI-local `usageError` (exit 2) so the central `execute()` seam owns the code; the riff-engine `*riff.ExitCodeError` path still `os.Exit`s its own class code directly. See [toolkit-standards](toolkit-standards.md) ¬ß principles P4 and `rk-riff.md` for full reference |
| `help-dump` | `help_dump.go` | **Hidden build tooling** (`Hidden: true`) ‚Äî not in user-facing help, self-excludes from its own dump. Emits the CLI help tree as JSON to stdout, or to a file when an optional `[output-path]` arg is given (`cobra.MaximumNArgs(1)`, stdlib `os.WriteFile` 0o644, no subprocess ‚Äî pure in-process Cobra introspection per ¬ßI). `captureNode` walks `rootCmd.Commands()` recursively to full depth, dropping `completion`, `help`, and any `Hidden` node at every level (a hidden parent's subtree is dropped entirely) via `includeInDump`; leaves serialize `"commands":[]` (non-nil slice), never `null`. Per-node fields `name`/`path`/`short`/`usage`/`text` come from `cmd.Name()`/`CommandPath()`/`Short`/`UseLine()`/`UsageString()` (raw, newlines preserved). The **frozen JSON contract** is `{tool:"run-kit", version, schema_version:1 (const), root:node}`, mirroring `sahil87/shll.ai` `help/wt.json`. **`captured_at` is deliberately NOT emitted** (removed in `260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`): the toolkit `help-dump` standard forbids it as a rule "with teeth" ‚Äî the capture timestamp is owned by the shll.ai puller (a tool cannot know its own capture time), which stamps it after capture. That fix dropped the `dump.CapturedAt` field, the `nowUTC` timestamp package-var + the `now` param on `buildDump` (now `buildDump(root, version)`), and the `time` import; the pure builder stays the test seam. `tool` became `"run-kit"` (was `"rk"`) with `schema_version` staying `1` ‚Äî a value change within the frozen shape, not a shape change ‚Äî when the canonical name flipped in `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`; `root.name`/`root.path`/`usage`/`text` follow automatically from the Cobra `Use: "run-kit"` root. `version` comes from `displayVersion()` (ldflags `-X main.version`, never hardcoded). shll.ai **pulls** this dump by running the CLI's `help-dump` itself on a schedule and capturing the output ‚Äî the in-repo release-pipeline publish step that used to push it was retired (`260603-iak3`, see `## Release Flow & CI/CD`); `help-dump` remains the single contract surface shll.ai depends on |
| `agent-setup` | `agent_setup.go` | Install (`--uninstall`) the agent-harness hooks that write the `@rk_agent_state` pane option; JSON merge with a diff + consent prompt before writing, `--yes`/`-y` (non-interactive consent) + `--dry-run` (preview, wins over `--yes`) + a non-TTY refusal naming `--yes` (`260717-c424`). Full consent flow + hook mechanism in [agent-state](agent-state.md) ¬ß `rk agent-setup`. **`--quiet`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9): the RunE builds `newSink(cmd)` threaded through `runAgentSetup`/`applyAgentConfig`/`applyAgentHooks`/`removeLegacySkill`; informational **status lines** (`‚Ä¶ hooks already ‚Ä¶ ‚Äî nothing to do.`, `‚Ä¶ wrote ‚Ä¶.`, `‚Ä¶ skipped (no changes written).`, the legacy rk-display-skill removal narration) route through `Notef` (chatter, dropped by `--quiet`). The settings **diff routes PER CONSENT MODE** via `consent.diffWriter(sink)`: on the **interactive-prompt** and **`--dry-run`** paths it is **data** (never gated ‚Äî a consent prompt without the diff it asks about is a dark pattern, and a dry-run's diff is the explicitly-requested output), while on the **`--yes`** path (write already authorized) it is **chatter**, so `--yes --quiet` is fully silent on success while `--yes` non-quiet still shows the diff on stderr (cycle-1 rework ‚Äî the diff had been written to `sink.data` unconditionally before `authorizeWrite`, printing the full diff to stdout under `--yes --quiet`). The interactive prompt itself (prompt suffix / dry-run note, via `authorizeWrite` on `sink.data`) and the non-TTY refusal (`errNonInteractiveConsent`, an error) are never gated |
| `reaper` | `reaper.go` | Operator-invoked janitor: scans `/tmp/tmux-{uid}/` and reaps every artifact matching `--prefix` (default `rk-test`) ‚Äî live servers killed, dead sockets/`*.lock` removed; dry-run by default (`--yes`/`--force` to act; `--force` also bypasses the dangerous-prefix guard for an empty/‚â§3-char prefix; `_rk-ctl`/`rk-daemon` skipped unconditionally). Output all via `cmd.OutOrStdout()` (data ‚Äî a dry-run list is the requested result, an act summary is the record of a destructive mutation), so **`--quiet` legitimately changes nothing** (no sink conversion). **Default 10-entry-per-list display cap + `--all`** (`260717-f8yv-cli-output-volume-controls`, toolkit Principle 9, mirroring `shll changelog`'s 10-release cap): `renderDryRun`'s candidate list caps at `reaperListCap` (10), and `renderReapSummary`'s `killed` and `removed` lists cap at 10 **each** (`renderCappedNames`, per-list); a **stated truncation notice** `‚Ä¶ and N more; pass --all to list all` (`renderTruncationNotice`) prints whenever a list is truncated (silent truncation reads as completeness). The **`--all`** bool restores the full list on either path. The cap is **display-only**: header counts stay **exact** (computed from the full `ReapResult`), `--yes`/`--force` still reap **every** match regardless of what was listed, and the dangerous-prefix guard, `_rk-ctl`/`rk-daemon` skips, and dry-run-by-default behavior are unchanged. The `Long` help text gained a sentence describing the cap/`--all`; `help_dump_test.go` asserts structure dynamically (no golden fixture) |

## Embedded Frontend Assets

`app/backend/build/embed.go` exposes `//go:embed all:frontend` as `build.Frontend` (`embed.FS`). During development, `frontend/` contains only `.gitkeep` (empty FS). Production builds copy `app/frontend/dist/` into `app/backend/build/frontend/` before `go build`.

`api/spa.go` uses dual-mode serving:
- **Production**: `hasEmbeddedAssets()` detects real build output (more than `.gitkeep`), serves from `embed.FS` via `mountEmbeddedSPA()`
- **Development**: Falls back to filesystem-based serving from `app/frontend/dist/` via `mountFilesystemSPA()` (Vite dev server handles frontend)

Both modes include SPA fallback (serve `index.html` for non-matching paths) and API/relay route guards.

## Version Management

- **Source of truth**: `VERSION` file at repo root ‚Äî plain semver string (e.g., `0.1.0`), no `v` prefix
- **Build injection**: `scripts/build.sh` reads `VERSION` and passes `-X main.version=$(cat VERSION)` via ldflags
- **Go variable**: `var version = "dev"` in `root.go` ‚Äî defaults to `"dev"` for local `go build` without ldflags
- **Displayed by**: the `--version`/`-v` global flag (Cobra built-in ‚Äî the `version` *subcommand* was removed in PR #90; `rk version` exits 1 `unknown command`); also read by `rk update` (shows current version, compares with latest via `brew info --json=v2`)
- **Version output string**: since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit` both `rk --version` and `run-kit --version` print `run-kit version <v>` (dev builds: `run-kit version dev`). The string flows from Cobra's version template, which prints the root's display name (`Use: "run-kit"`), so it is invocation-name-agnostic ‚Äî no per-name divergence
- **Exposed to the web UI over the state socket** (since `260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`; transport is the state socket since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` ‚Äî was the SSE stream): `cmd/rk/serve.go` plumbs the ldflags `main.version` into `*api.Server` via `SetVersion(version)` after `NewRouterAndServer`, which seeds the server-global `version` cached global slot (replayed once after `hello` ‚Äî the version is fixed for the process lifetime). There is deliberately **no `GET /api/version`** ‚Äî the socket connect is the moment the client needs it, and the reconnect after a `rk update`-driven daemon restart delivers a *different* version, which is exactly the signal the frontend's auto-reload guard keys on. Also fed to `internal/updatecheck.New(version)` (the running-version half of the semver compare). See ¬ß State Socket (global-slot replay), ¬ß SSE Hub (`event: version`) and ¬ß API Server version/checker wiring below

## Build Pipeline

`scripts/build.sh` encapsulates the full production build (frontend-first for embed):

1. `cd app/frontend && pnpm build` ‚Äî produces `app/frontend/dist/` (with vendor chunk splitting: `xterm` chunk for `@xterm/xterm`, `@xterm/addon-fit`, `@xterm/addon-web-links`; `router` chunk for `@tanstack/react-router`; plus lazy-loaded component chunks for `CommandPalette`, `ThemeSelector`, `CreateSessionDialog`). `zustand` is bundled as a production dependency.
2. Copy `app/frontend/dist/` ‚Üí `app/backend/build/frontend/` (Go embed cannot reference `../` paths)
3. Read version from `VERSION` file
4. `CGO_ENABLED=0 go build -ldflags "-X main.version=${VERSION}" -o ../../dist/run-kit ./cmd/run-kit`

Output: `dist/run-kit` ‚Äî single static binary with embedded frontend assets, tmux config, and baked-in version.

`justfile` recipes: `build` delegates to `scripts/build.sh`, `release` delegates to `scripts/release.sh`.

## PWA Layer

`vite-plugin-pwa` (devDependency) adds Progressive Web App support to the Vite build. Configured in `app/frontend/vite.config.ts` with `registerType: "autoUpdate"`.

**Manifest**: Generated from the `VitePWA` plugin config in `vite.config.ts` ‚Äî no separate `manifest.json` file. Specifies `display: "standalone"`, `start_url: "/"`, dark theme colors (`background_color` and `theme_color` set to `#0f1117`), and an icon array (192px, 512px, 512px maskable). The plugin injects a `<link rel="manifest">` tag into the built `index.html` automatically.

**Service worker**: Workbox-generated (`sw.js`). Precaches all static assets (JS, CSS, HTML) from the Vite build output. Runtime caching rules:
- `NetworkOnly` for URL patterns matching `/api/` and `/relay/` ‚Äî SSE streams and WebSocket connections always hit the server
- `navigateFallback: "/index.html"` ‚Äî ensures TanStack Router client-side routes work when served from cache (e.g., homescreen launch to `/{session}/{window}`)

Updates are silent (`registerType: "autoUpdate"`) ‚Äî the service worker detects new builds and caches updated assets without user interaction or reload prompts.

**Build output**: `app/frontend/dist/` gains `sw.js` and `manifest.webmanifest` alongside the existing Vite output. These files are copied into `app/backend/build/frontend/` by `scripts/build.sh` and served by the Go backend via the existing SPA static serving ‚Äî no backend changes required.

**Icons**: Canonical SVG mark at `app/frontend/public/icon.svg` (hexagonal cube, transparent background). Generated variants in `app/frontend/public/generated-icons/`: `favicon.svg` (copy of icon.svg), `icon-192.png`, `icon-512.png`, `icon-512-maskable.png` (PNGs have solid `#0f1117` dark background with 20% padding, maskable has 40%). Generated by `scripts/generate-icons.sh` (uses `sharp` Node library). Run via `just icons`.

## Web Push Notifications

`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications` lets any process on the box ‚Äî primarily the fab-kit operator agent via `rk notify` ‚Äî deliver a real OS-level notification that reaches the user **even when the RunKit PWA tab is closed**. This is the only browser-native mechanism that delivers to a closed tab: the *browser's* push service wakes the registered service worker, which shows the notification. It is the intended eventual replacement for fab-kit's `ntfy.sh` default (one feed across all operators on the box, content stays on infra the user runs).

**End-to-end delivery model**: a shell process runs `rk notify "msg"` ‚Üí POSTs `{title, body}` to the local server `POST /api/notify` ‚Üí the server iterates stored `PushSubscription`s and sends each a Web Push via `webpush-go` signed with the server's VAPID **private** key ‚Üí the browser's push service wakes the registered service worker ‚Üí `sw.js`'s `push` handler calls `self.registration.showNotification(title, {body, icon, data})` ‚Üí the user sees an OS notification with the tab closed.

**`Notify` signature carries an optional deep-link URL (`260714-r7rq`)**: `push.Notify(ctx, title, body, url string)` ‚Äî the 4th `url` param is threaded into the `payload` JSON as `url,omitempty` (empty ‚áí omitted, and the SW falls back to the app root on click). The only URL producer today is the waiting-push watcher (¬ß Web Push on Sustained Waiting ‚Üí deep-link URL, `/{server}/{N}?view=chat` for chat-capable waiting windows); the generic `/api/notify` path (`api/push.go`) and `rk notify` (`cmd/rk/notify.go`) pass `""`.

**Service worker** (`app/frontend/public/sw.js`): a hand-written service worker served at the origin root `/sw.js` (whole-app scope). Its `push` handler parses the JSON payload `{title, body, icon?, url?}` (default title `"RunKit"`, default icon `/generated-icons/icon-192.png`) and tolerates an empty / non-JSON payload by falling back to defaults; it stores the deep-link `url` on the notification via `showNotification(title, { body, icon, data: { url } })`. **Its `notificationclick` handler focuses an already-open RunKit tab and NAVIGATES it to the deep-link target** (or `openWindow`s a new tab at the target), falling back to the app root `/` when no `url` was carried (`260714-r7rq` ‚Äî previously hardcoded `openWindow("/")`). Two safety details (both review reworks): (a) the URL is normalized through `sameOriginPath(value)` ‚Äî it must start with `/` but **NOT `//`** (a protocol-relative `//evil.example` resolves to an EXTERNAL origin), and the resolved `new URL(value, origin).origin` is belt-and-braces compared to the SW's own origin ‚Äî so a malformed/hostile payload can never redirect off-origin; (b) `client.navigate()` REJECTS for uncontrolled clients (`matchAll` uses `includeUncontrolled: true`) and may be unavailable in some browsers, so the call is chained `.catch(() => client.focus())` ‚Äî a rejection must never propagate into `waitUntil` (it would surface as an unhandled SW error). **This is a separate file from any Workbox/`vite-plugin-pwa`-generated SW** ‚Äî the current frontend ships only this hand-written `public/sw.js` and a static `public/manifest.json` linked from `index.html` (the `## PWA Layer` section above describes the earlier `vite-plugin-pwa` build path; the manifest/SW generation tooling is not wired in the current tree). Registered on app load via `navigator.serviceWorker.register('/sw.js')` from `app/frontend/src/main.tsx`, guarded by `'serviceWorker' in navigator` so unsupported / insecure-context environments silently skip registration.

**Secure-context constraint**: service workers and `PushManager` require a **secure context ‚Äî HTTPS or `localhost`**. The user typically hits run-kit on `localhost:3000` (or behind a TLS reverse proxy such as Tailscale Serve), both secure contexts, so it is satisfied in practice ‚Äî but raw-IP / plaintext non-localhost access cannot subscribe (registration is skipped silently, no error).

**State persistence** (Constitution ¬ßII ‚Äî No Database): the `internal/push` package owns two JSON files under `~/.rk/` ‚Äî `vapid.json` (the VAPID keypair, private key written mode **`0600`**, never served) and `push-subscriptions.json` (the subscription array, de-duped by `endpoint`). See ¬ß Backend Libraries. There is no `/api/push/unsubscribe` in v1; dead subscriptions are pruned server-side on `404`/`410` during send.

**Fail-silent discipline** (end-to-end, constitution-aligned): every layer fails silently on its own prerequisite being absent. `rk notify` exits 0 with no output on any failure (server unreachable / non-2xx / timeout) so a notify failure never stalls the operator loop; the send fan-out tolerates individual subscription failures and prunes dead endpoints; the frontend subscribe flow aborts silently when permission is denied or the context is insecure / unsupported. The opt-in is a Cmd+K palette action with a terminal-themed label (NOT a bell) ‚Äî see `ui-patterns.md` ¬ß Notifications (Web Push opt-in).

## Release Flow & CI/CD

**Release script** (`scripts/release.sh`): accepts bump level (`patch`/`minor`/`major`), increments `VERSION` file semver, commits with message `v{version}`, creates git tag `v{version}`, pushes commit + tag. Tag push triggers CI.

**GitHub Actions** (`.github/workflows/release.yml`): triggers on `v*` tag push. Steps: checkout ‚Üí setup Go (from `go.mod`) ‚Üí setup Node 20 + pnpm ‚Üí install frontend deps ‚Üí build frontend ‚Üí copy dist to backend ‚Üí cross-compile 4 targets ‚Üí create GitHub Release with tarballs ‚Üí update Homebrew tap.

Cross-compile targets: `darwin/arm64`, `darwin/amd64`, `linux/arm64`, `linux/amd64`. Each target built with `CGO_ENABLED=0` and ldflags. Output: `rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz` tarballs uploaded to GitHub Release via `softprops/action-gh-release`.

**Help-tree publish to shll.ai ‚Äî RETIRED (push ‚Üí pull, `260603-iak3-teardown-shllai-publish-ci`):** the release job no longer publishes the help tree. The former **final** CI step (`Publish help tree to shll.ai`, deliberately placed after the GitHub Release and Homebrew tap) ran `dist/rk-linux-amd64/rk help-dump help/run-kit.json` (the versioned linux/amd64 artifact, so the dumped `version` matched the release) then opened a best-effort auto-merge PR into `sahil87/shll.ai` via the `SHLLAI_TOKEN` cross-repo write secret ‚Äî that entire step was removed. shll.ai inverted its integration model from **push** (each toolkit CLI produced its help JSON in CI and PR'd it into shll.ai) to **pull** (shll.ai now runs `rk help-dump` itself on a schedule and captures the output), making the push path redundant work and a redundant attack surface (dual writers to `help/run-kit.json` could race). The `SHLLAI_TOKEN` reference was removed from CI along with the step; the GitHub repo secret itself is an operator follow-up to delete (least-privilege, no remaining consumer). The hidden `rk help-dump` subcommand is **preserved unchanged** as the single contract surface shll.ai pulls from (see `## CLI Subcommands`). After removal, the `release` job's final step is **Update Homebrew tap**. (Historical: the push step was added in `260602-a36m-help-dump-shll-ai` and hardened in `260602-2dt9-fix-shllai-help-publish`.)

**Homebrew tap update** (now the **final** step in the `release` job): computes SHA256 for all 4 tarballs, clones `sahil87/homebrew-tap` via the `HOMEBREW_TAP_TOKEN` secret (exported as `TAP_TOKEN`), generates `Formula/run-kit.rb` from `.github/formula-template.rb` (placeholder substitution via `sed`), commits with message `run-kit ${version}`, and pushes. The output path/filename and commit message follow the `run-kit` formula name since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit` (was `Formula/rk.rb` / `rk ${version}`); the cross-compile step is untouched ‚Äî tarball artifact names stay `rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz` with a single `rk` member (the physical binary is not renamed; the formula renames it at install time).

## Homebrew Distribution

**Formula**: `Formula/run-kit.rb` in `sahil87/homebrew-tap` (generated by CI from `.github/formula-template.rb`; the formula class is `RunKit` and the file/name are `run-kit` since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit` ‚Äî was `Formula/rk.rb` / `class Rk`). Public repo ‚Äî plain URL downloads, no auth token needed. Platform detection via `on_macos`/`on_linux` + `on_arm`/`on_intel`. Version and SHA256 values substituted by CI. **Sequencing dependency** (out of this repo's scope, but binding): `sahil87/homebrew-tap` must gain `formula_renames.json` mapping `"rk": "run-kit"` (and drop the old `Formula/rk.rb`) before/with the next release so existing `rk` installs upgrade seamlessly via brew's rename redirect.

Install flow: `brew install sahil87/tap/run-kit` (fully qualified ‚Äî the shll meta-CLI always installs qualified, so the former unqualified-`brew install`-core-collision constraint that drove the March 2026 `run-kit`‚Üí`rk` rename no longer applies). Update: `rk update` (or `run-kit update`).

**Canonical command name ‚Äî `run-kit`, with `rk` as the permanent alias (since `260709-gidk-swap-canonical-cli-name-run-kit`)**: `run-kit` is now the **canonical** command; `rk` is a permanently-supported, fully-interchangeable short alias. This **reverses** the direction set by `260707-ook7-run-kit-command-alias` (which added `run-kit` as a symlink but kept `rk` canonical) and, further back, the original March 2026 `run-kit`‚Üí`rk` rename (`260323-ycod`, motivated by the Homebrew-core `run-kit` unqualified-install conflict ‚Äî a constraint that no longer applies now that the shll meta-CLI always installs fully qualified). What flipped:

- **Formula real-vs-alias flip**: `def install` now does `bin.install "rk" => "run-kit"` then `bin.install_symlink bin/"run-kit" => "rk"` ‚Äî the tarball's `rk` member is **renamed at install time** to `run-kit` (the real binary), and `rk` becomes the symlink back. The formula class is `RunKit`, published as `Formula/run-kit.rb`; the `test do` block asserts BOTH `#{bin}/run-kit --version` and `#{bin}/rk --version` match `"run-kit version"` (the `--version` flag, NOT a `version` subcommand ‚Äî removed in PR #90; see ¬ß Version Management).
- **Cobra root**: `Use: "run-kit"` + matching `Short` (static string ‚Äî argv[0]-dynamic `Use` was rejected for help-dump determinism, since shll.ai regenerates the help JSON on a schedule and its output must not depend on which name invoked the CLI). Version output prints `run-kit version <v>` for both invocation names.
- **help-dump**: `tool: "run-kit"` (`schema_version` stays `1`) ‚Äî see ¬ß CLI Subcommands (`help-dump` row).
- **`upgrade.go` moved wholly to `run-kit` markers**: `/Cellar/run-kit/` install-detection marker, `sahil87/tap/run-kit` brew refs, `/bin/run-kit` daemon-restart bin path. **No dual-marker back-compat** in code: an old installed binary runs its OWN old logic (self-resolves under `/Cellar/rk/`, brew's `formula_renames` redirects the upgrade to `run-kit`, and the persistent `rk` symlink still exists for the daemon restart), so the transition completes without new-binary back-compat.
- **Shell completion binds BOTH names** (zsh/bash): after the `Use` swap cobra generates completion for `run-kit` only, so `shell_init.go` appends an extra `compdef _run-kit rk` (zsh) and an extra `complete ‚Ä¶ rk` line reusing `__start_run-kit` (bash) so the daily-typed `rk` keeps tab completion. fish/powershell keep cobra's single-name binding.

**Invariants ‚Äî internals stay `rk`**: the Go module path (`module rk`), `cmd/rk/` directory, `RK_*` env vars, `rk-daemon` socket/session names, `~/.rk/` config dir, `dist/rk`/`bin/rk` build outputs, and release-artifact/tarball names (`rk-{os}-{arch}.tar.gz`, single `rk` member ‚Äî the physical binary is not renamed; the formula renames at install time) are all unchanged. `rk` remains a real on-PATH executable name **indefinitely** ‚Äî installed agent-setup hooks embed `/opt/homebrew/bin/rk` and fab-kit skills gate on `command -v rk`. Both names stay fully interchangeable for every subcommand. The effect is **release-gated** (reaches installed users on the first release after merge) and requires the tap-repo `formula_renames.json` `{"rk": "run-kit"}` follow-up to land before/with that release (see ¬ß Homebrew Distribution).

## Boards Feature

Pane boards are named collections of pinned tmux windows rendered as a horizontal pane dashboard at `/board/$name`. Since `260602-qn62-move-based-board-pin-sessions` the model is **move-based and server-scoped**: a pinned window is physically `move-window`'d into its own single-window session `_rk-pin-<id>`, and a board is the **set of pin-sessions sharing an `@rk_board` SESSION var** (not a tmux session itself, and no longer a `@rk_board` server-option encoding). Boards are server-scoped because `move-window` can't cross tmux servers ‚Äî the board *list* is summarized across reachable servers, but there is no cross-server window union. A board exists only while ‚â•1 pin carries its name (no empty boards, no registry). See `tmux-sessions.md` ¬ß Pin Sessions and ¬ß `@rk_board` for the full pin/unpin/reorder contract, the three session vars (`@rk_board`/`@rk_home`/`@rk_board_order`), order keys, and the direct-attach relay.

### Route Placement

| Route | View | Layout |
|-------|------|--------|
| `/board/$name` | Cross-server pane dashboard | Wrapped in the shared `<Shell>` grid (same wrapper as AppShell). Sidebar grid area = unified `<Sidebar currentServer={null}>`; topbar = `<TopBar mode="board">`; content = `DesktopRow`/`MobileCarousel`; bottombar = shared `<BottomBar>` (new on this route) |

`/board/$name` is registered as a child of `rootRoute` in `app/frontend/src/router.tsx`, peer to `serverLayoutRoute`. It does NOT mount AppShell ‚Äî boards aggregate windows across servers, so AppShell's single-server chrome semantics (server-scoped breadcrumbs, server-scoped command-palette actions) do not apply. As of `260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`, BoardPage shares the AppShell `<Shell>` grid wrapper and renders `<TopBar mode="board">` + `<BottomBar>` in the shell's named areas ‚Äî the route reuses the chrome topology while routing different breadcrumb / pane-area content into it. BoardPage retains its own `<CommandPalette>` mount because board-route-only entries (Switch / Leave Board View / Cycle Pane Focus) need a registration site, and the AppShell palette doesn't mount on `/board/<name>`. `SessionProvider` lives at the root and exposes per-server state, so the board route renders `<Sidebar currentServer={null} ...>` directly with no special-case. The Sidebar's per-server session groups + Boards section serve discovery and entry from any route. See ui-patterns.md ¬ß Boards View for the layout.

### Backend Surface

| Layer | File | Responsibility |
|-------|------|---------------|
| Storage | `app/backend/internal/tmux/board.go` | move-based `Pin`/`Unpin`/`Reorder`, `pinEntry`, `ListBoardEntries`/`ListBoards`/`GetBoard` (derived from `_rk-pin-*` session vars), `ComputeOrderKey`/`nextAppendKey` (lowercase-`a..z` fractional indexing), `BoardOption`/`HomeOption`/`BoardOrderOption` session-var keys, validators (`ValidBoardName`, `ValidWindowID`, `ValidOrderKey`). The old `@rk_board` server-option parser/serializer (`parseBoardValue`/`serializeBoardValue`/`setBoardValue`), cross-server `ListAllBoardEntries`, and `RemoveAllByWindowID` are **deleted** (since `260602-qn62`). Pin-session naming (`PinSessionPrefix`/`PinSessionName`/`WindowIDFromPinSession`/`ListPinSessionNames`) lives in `tmux.go` |
| HTTP handlers | `app/backend/api/boards.go` | `handleBoardsList` (rank-aware sort via the pure `sortBoardsByStoredOrder` helper + `settings.GetBoardOrder`), `handleBoardGet`, `handleBoardPin`, `handleBoardUnpin`, `handleBoardReorder`, and `handleBoardOrderPost` (`POST /api/boards/order` ‚Äî full-list validate/dedup/persist/broadcast, since `260708-a2qd`) ‚Äî register in `router.go` `buildRouter()`; the pin/unpin/reorder trio each emits its own per-server `board-changed` SSE event, while `handleBoardOrderPost` emits the server-global `board-order` event |
| Interface | `app/backend/api/router.go` `TmuxOps` | `ListBoards`, `GetBoard`, `ListBoardEntries`, `PinBoard`‚Üí`tmux.Pin`, `UnpinBoard`‚Üí`tmux.Unpin`, `ReorderBoard` (uses `lookupNeighbourKeys` + `ComputeOrderKey` then `tmux.Reorder`). `260602-qn62` removed `NewGroupedSession` and `SetSessionOwnerPID` from the interface + `prodTmuxOps` + `mockTmuxOps`. **Cross-server neighbour resolution** (`260708-rmiq-board-pane-reorder`): `lookupNeighbourKeys` enumerates `ListServers` and aggregates the board's `windowId ‚Üí orderKey` map across EVERY reachable server (mirroring `GetBoard`/`handleGetBoard`'s cross-server aggregation, `boards.go`), NOT just the moved pane's own server ‚Äî because a board spans servers (`move-window` can't cross servers, but a board is the union of `_rk-pin-*` sessions sharing an `@rk_board` on ANY server). The `400 neighbour window not found on board` (`neighbourNotFoundError`) fires ONLY when the `before`/`after` windowId is absent from the board on every server. Before this fix the lookup was server-scoped, so on a mixed-server board any move whose new neighbour was pinned from a different server 400'd ‚Äî failing the reorder and permanently desyncing the client's optimistic preview. A per-server `ListBoardEntries` error is `slog.Warn("board: ListBoardEntries failed", ...)` + skipped (log-and-continue like `GetBoard`/`ListBoards`), so an unreachable server leaves a trace rather than silently degrading to a 400 |
| SSE | `app/backend/api/sse.go` | `BoardEntriesFetcher` (now a one-method `ListBoardEntries` interface for test stubbing), `broadcastBoardChanged(server, payload)`, `event: board-changed` (kebab-case; `change` ‚àà `pin`/`unpin`/`reorder` only). Since `260602-qn62`: NO `previousBoardJSON` cache, NO bootstrap-on-first-poll, NO cached-snapshot replay, NO window-kill `cleanup` diff ‚Äî a killed pinned window's pin-session just disappears from the next live `ListBoardEntries` read. **Separately, `broadcastBoardOrder(order)` + `event: board-order` + the single `cachedBoardOrderJSON` replay slot** (since `260708-a2qd`) ‚Äî the server-global board-DISPLAY-order broadcast, distinct from the per-server `board-changed`; see the ¬ß SSE Hub `broadcastBoardOrder` note |

### Constitution Alignment

- **II (No Database)** ‚Äî pin state lives only in tmux: the `_rk-pin-*` session structure + its `@rk_board`/`@rk_home`/`@rk_board_order` session vars (a deliberate shift since `260602-qn62` from "a tiny derived server-option value" to "tmux session structure IS the record"). Browser `localStorage` holds only view-local pane widths
- **IV (Minimal Surface Area)** ‚Äî adds exactly one route (`/board/$name`); `260602-qn62` net-reduced backend surface (deleted the relay ephemeral subsystem, the `@rk_board` encoding, the startup sweep, and the SSE board-cleanup/bootstrap) while keeping one rendering path (`TerminalClient`/`/relay/{windowId}`)
- **V (Keyboard-First)** ‚Äî pin/unpin/switch/cycle reachable via Cmd+K palette; pane focus cycle via Cmd+[/]
- **VI (Tmux Sessions Survive Server Restarts)** ‚Äî pin state persists with the tmux server across rk-go restarts, so there is NO restore-sweep (since `260602-qn62`); `tmux kill-server` loses the boards on that server (expected and acceptable). An emptied home session (its only window pinned away) persists via the `exit-empty off` backstop (`260602-a1wo`) so unpin can restore the window to it
- **VII (Convention Over Configuration)** ‚Äî no new env vars, no new config files; reuses the established `@rk_*` user-option pattern

## Design Decisions

- **Go backend + Vite SPA over Next.js monolith** ‚Äî decouples frontend and backend for independent iteration. Go backend is a stable, long-lived API that outlives any individual frontend. Multi-client API support (web, mobile, CLI) without split API surface
- **Single port architecture** ‚Äî Go serves API, WebSocket relay, and SPA static files on one port. The two-port split (Next.js :3000, relay :3001) was a Node.js artifact ‚Äî separate processes required separate ports. Go serves everything in one binary
- **chi over stdlib ServeMux** ‚Äî chi for middleware chaining (CORS, logging, recovery). Go 1.22+ ServeMux has pattern matching but lacks ergonomic middleware composition
- **TanStack Router over React Router** ‚Äî type-safe params and search params, built-in loader pattern. Single route `/:session/:window` in the new frontend
- **Vite proxy in dev (not CORS)** ‚Äî single browser URL, no CORS config needed. WebSocket upgrade works transparently. Go includes chi CORS middleware for production/non-browser clients
- **SPA fallback in Go** ‚Äî Go serves standalone; TLS termination handled externally via Tailscale Serve when needed
- **SSE (not WebSocket) for session state** ‚Äî simpler, server-push only, naturally resilient. Module-level hub deduplicates polling across tabs (one `FetchSessions()` per server per interval). Clients indexed by server name (`map[string][]*sseClient`) ‚Äî broadcast iterates only the target server's slice. `sync.RWMutex` with `RLock` for read-only poll operations, `Lock` for writes. SSE data includes `isActiveWindow` per window, enabling UI sync when users switch tmux/byobu windows via terminal shortcuts
- **Full snapshots (not diffs)** ‚Äî small payload (<100 sessions), simple client logic
- **Independent panes per browser client** ‚Äî no cursor fights, agent pane untouched. The relay pty follows tmux window switches natively (runs `tmux -L runkit attach-session`)
- **Every tmux session is a project** ‚Äî no config, no "Other" bucket. Project root derived from window 0's `pane_current_path`
- **Config via env vars (not YAML)** ‚Äî `.env` committed with defaults (`RK_PORT`, `RK_HOST`), `.env.local` for overrides, loaded via `.envrc` (direnv). Go and Vite read `RK_PORT`/`RK_HOST` directly. `dev.sh` translates `RK_PORT+1` for the backend subprocess. No relay port ‚Äî single port serves everything
- **Dedicated tmux server (`-L runkit`)** ‚Äî run-kit sessions live on a named tmux server `runkit` with its own config (`internal/tmux/tmux.conf` loaded via `-f`). The default tmux server is also queried for session discovery (read-only display of external sessions). This replaces byobu integration: `CreateSession()` uses plain `tmux new-session` on the runkit server (no byobu dependency). The `runkit` server provides isolation, a custom status bar matching run-kit's dark theme, and byobu-style F-key keybindings (F2/F3/F4). `SessionInfo` carries a `Name` field; `ProjectSession` has `Name` and `Windows` fields. The caller passes the target server name to each tmux operation
- **Multi-server session enumeration** ‚Äî `ListSessions(ctx, server)` queries the specified tmux server. The API layer calls it once per server (e.g., `runkit` and `default`), merging results. Session-group filtering applies to both servers. See `docs/memory/run-kit/tmux-sessions.md`
- **Derived chrome (not slot injection)** ‚Äî Single-view model means only one chrome state (terminal-focused). Top bar and bottom bar derive content from the current session:window selection. No `setLine2Left`/`setLine2Right`/`setBottomBar` setters. Split React Context preserved for performance (state vs dispatch).
- **Root-mounted multi-server SessionProvider over one state socket** ‚Äî One `SessionProvider` instance lives at the root above `<Outlet />` (in `RootWrapper`) and is shared by every route. State is keyed per server (`Map<string, T>`); `currentServer: string | null` is dispatched from the matched route via `useMatches()`. Since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` the provider drives ONE `StateSocket` (was one `EventSource` per server): servers are subscribed lazily ‚Äî current server eager, others via `attachServer(name)` ‚Äî over the single wire. Provider survives server-route switches (no remount, no state rebuild) and lets the Board route render the same unified `<Sidebar>` as AppShell with `currentServer === null`. Cross-server `board-changed` events are multiplexed through `subscribeBoardChange` so cross-server hooks (`useBoards`, `useWindowPins`) add no separate connections. Rejected: per-route providers bridged via a sibling cross-server context ‚Äî adds two contexts, double-fetches `/api/servers`, doesn't solve BoardPage sidebar reuse cleanly. Rejected: `Record<string, T>` instead of `Map<string, T>` ‚Äî Maps give clear "server unknown" vs "server known with empty value" semantics. (`260508-dc0t-multiserver-session-provider`; transport swapped to the state socket by `260716-qf3j-state-socket`)
- **Single-view layout (sidebar + terminal/dashboard) replaces three pages** ‚Äî Dashboard and Project page functionality subsumed by the sidebar + Dashboard view. Terminal is the main content on `/:session/:window`; Dashboard renders on `/`. No page transitions.
- **Dashboard as inline component in app.tsx (not separate route layout)** ‚Äî The Dashboard renders in the terminal area via a conditional branch (`sessionName && windowIndex ? <TerminalClient/> : <Dashboard/>`). This reuses the existing chrome skeleton (top bar, sidebar) and avoids duplicating the app shell layout. Rejected: separate route with dedicated layout ‚Äî would require lifting sidebar/chrome into a shared layout component and restructuring the route tree.
- **POST-only API client with path-based intent** ‚Äî Each mutation is a separate function with its own URL (e.g., `killSession(session)` ‚Üí `POST /api/sessions/:session/kill`). No multiplexed `action` field in request bodies. Formalized as constitution ¬ßIX (Uniform HTTP Verb) and brought into full conformance by `260529-jad6` (the last five `.Put(` routes migrated to `POST`; CORS `AllowedMethods` ‚Üí `[GET, POST, OPTIONS]`). Semantics that would conventionally map to `PUT`/`PATCH` (partial update) live in the path + body contract instead of the verb.
- **Shared chained-`set-option` primitive + "validate-all-then-one-atomic-invocation" partial-merge** (`260529-jad6`) ‚Äî `WindowOptionOp{Key; Value *string}` + `appendOptionOps(args, target, ops)` is a single reusable primitive for emitting any sequence of `set-option -w` set/unset ops as one `\;`-chained tmux invocation. Both `SetWindowOptions` (the `POST /options` endpoint) and `CreateWindowWithOptions` (window creation) consume it ‚Äî there is no separate inline option-map construction path. The `POST /options` handler pairs this with a strict ordering contract: **all keys are validated (allowlist + per-key rules) before any tmux subprocess is spawned**, so a single invalid key aborts with `400` and zero tmux calls (no partial application), and the merge that does run is one atomic chained invocation the SSE poll can never observe half-applied. This validate-all-then-atomic pattern is the reusable shape for future multi-key tmux mutations. *Why*: partial-merge (present key sets, `null` unsets, absent untouched) avoids the "client clears a field it didn't echo" bug class that a full-replace PUT re-introduces; the key allowlist (`@color`/`@rk_url`/`@rk_type`) bounds the option-name surface passed to `tmux set-option` (¬ßI). *Rejected*: a generic action-dispatcher for all window verbs (weaker per-action validation, fuzzier ¬ßI audit surface); PATCH/PUT full-replace (violates ¬ßIX / re-introduces the cleared-field bug); passing through arbitrary `@`-prefixed keys (unvalidated surface).
- **Session as server-derived disambiguation context for REST `/select`** (`260529-jad6`) ‚Äî `handleWindowSelect` resolves the owning session server-side (`ResolveWindowSession`) and issues a session-scoped `select-window -t <session>:@N` (`SelectWindowInSession`) rather than a bare `select-window -t @N`. *Why*: a bare window-id target is ambiguous inside a tmux session group (members keep independent active-window state, so tmux may activate the window on the wrong member ‚Äî the wrong-window-highlight symptom, live since #198 made tmux the sidebar's source of truth). The session is derived only where tmux semantics require it; the client never sends it (consistent with dropping `$session` from the URL). *Rejected*: a bare-target select with a client-supplied session (puts the session back in the client-facing identity).
- **Sidebar + drawer pattern on mobile** ‚Äî Desktop sidebar is drag-resizable (default 220px, min 160, max 400, localStorage persist), collapsible. Mobile (< 768px) uses a left-side drawer overlay triggered by `‚ò∞`. Preserves session/window tree layout across breakpoints.
- **Prebuilt binaries over build-from-source Homebrew formula** ‚Äî ship cross-compiled binaries via GitHub Release. Zero build dependencies on user's machine (no Go, Node.js, pnpm). Faster install. Rejected: build-from-source formula (like tu) which requires all build tools. (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **`embed.FS` with copy step over restructuring repo** ‚Äî copy `app/frontend/dist/` into `app/backend/build/frontend/` at build time because Go's `//go:embed` cannot reference files outside the package directory. Simple build-time operation. Rejected: colocating frontend output with Go source (breaks dev workflow). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **VERSION file + ldflags over Go constant** ‚Äî version sourced from `VERSION` file, injected via `-X main.version=...`. Shell scripts can read/write plain text. No code changes for version bumps. Rejected: Go constant (requires code change per release). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **Cobra over custom CLI parsing** ‚Äî industry standard, auto-generates help, 5 subcommands is the sweet spot. Rejected: stdlib `flag` (no subcommand support), custom parsing (unnecessary). (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **SPA handler dual-mode (embedded FS vs filesystem)** ‚Äî `hasEmbeddedAssets()` checks whether `frontend/` contains more than `.gitkeep`. Production uses `embed.FS`, dev uses filesystem (Vite handles frontend). Automatic detection, no build tags or env vars needed. (`260317-ukyz-homebrew-deployment`)
- **Active window sync ‚Äî tmux truth, URL as bookmark** ‚Äî tmux is the sole source of truth for "current window" per server. The URL is a resumable bookmark used only on mount (and reload); after mount it is derived state, rewritten by an SSE-driven `navigate({ replace: true })` whenever the server-reported `isActiveWindow` differs from the URL. Mount-time alignment fires exactly one `selectWindow` to align tmux to a deep-linked URL (gated by `hasAlignedToUrlRef`). All clients on the same server converge ("yank" semantics) ‚Äî cross-server tabs stay independent. Sidebar clicks are pure mutations (`selectWindow` only); no client-side timer or debounce. The previous 3-second `userNavTimestampRef` debounce was deleted entirely ‚Äî it was protecting client-owned selection state that no longer exists. Push channel is tmux control mode (`tmux -CC`) via the new `internal/tmuxctl/` package; primary latency target sub-500ms, with a 12-second safety-net poll as backstop. Boards get a "free win" as a side effect ‚Äî board cleanup now tracks control-mode latency rather than the prior 2.5s poll cadence. Rejected: per-tab current window (reintroduces a second writer, doesn't match the dashboard model). Rejected: hooks + `rk notify` + lockfile (incompatible with PR #197's Constitution ¬ßII Non-Goal). Supersedes the 2026-03-07 `history.replaceState` SSE-polling decision. (`260528-nvlp-active-window-sync`)
  - *Refined by `260530-v6hm-active-window-event-derivation`*: the `isActiveWindow` that drives this writeback is now **event-derived per session group** (two-tier: event-tracked `@wid` authoritative, base `#{window_active}` cold-start/reconnect fallback), not read from the base session pointer alone. The base pointer goes stale when an `rk-relay-*` ephemeral / `rk riff` / external `new-window` moves the active window (group members keep independent pointers), which is why the highlight previously lagged. The fix is purely in the derivation/read path ‚Äî no creator changed, the ephemeral model is untouched, and the frontend writeback needed no edit. See ¬ß Active-Window Event Derivation.
- **Sticky modifier state via useRef + forceUpdate** ‚Äî `useModifierState` uses a ref for the authoritative state and a counter state to trigger re-renders. Ensures `consume()` reads the latest value atomically without stale closure issues.
- **Compose buffer as native textarea (not xterm input)** ‚Äî xterm renders to `<canvas>`, blocking OS-level input features. The compose buffer provides a real `<textarea>` where dictation, autocorrect, paste, and IME all work. Text sent as a single WebSocket message.
- **Armed modifiers bridge to physical keyboard** ‚Äî When bottom-bar modifiers (Ctrl/Alt) are armed, a capture-phase `keydown` listener intercepts physical keypresses, translates them to terminal escape sequences (Ctrl+letter ‚Üí control characters, Alt ‚Üí ESC prefix), and sends via WebSocket. Prevents xterm from receiving the unmodified key. Ignores real Cmd/Ctrl/Alt held by the OS.
- **File upload via server filesystem (not terminal binary injection)** ‚Äî Browser uploads file to `POST /api/sessions/:session/upload`, server writes to `.uploads/` in project root, path auto-inserted into compose buffer. Works because run-kit server and tmux are always co-located; the browser is the remote part. Session identified by URL param (consistent with other session-scoped endpoints, replaces legacy form field approach)
- **Handler files split by resource domain (not monolithic routes.go)** ‚Äî Each handler file owns one resource: `sessions.go`, `windows.go`, `directories.go`, `upload.go`, `sse.go`/`state_ws.go` (session-state), `terminals_ws.go` (pane relay mux, since `260717-803u-relay-mux`), `spa.go`, `health.go`. `router.go` owns middleware, dependency interfaces, and route registration only. (`260312-r4t9-go-backend-api`) *(`relay.go` ‚Äî once the `handleRelay` home ‚Äî now holds only the shared `upgrader` + `forceTERM`, both consumed by `terminals_ws.go`; folding them in and deleting `relay.go` is a noted deletion candidate since its name no longer matches any endpoint.)*
- **Dependency injection via interfaces for handler testability** ‚Äî `Server` struct holds `SessionFetcher` and `TmuxOps` interfaces, plus `hostname` (computed via `os.Hostname()` in `NewRouter()`, empty string on failure) and `*metrics.Collector` (created and started in `NewRouter()` with the server context). `TmuxOps` interface includes `SetWindowOptions(ctx, windowID, server, ops []tmux.WindowOptionOp)` and `CreateWindowWithOptions(session, name, cwd, server, ops []tmux.WindowOptionOp)` for the batched/chained window-option operations (since `260529-jad6` ‚Äî the singular `SetWindowOption`/`UnsetWindowOption` and the dedicated `SetWindowColor`/`UnsetWindowColor` remain on the interface but lost their production callers; window-targeting methods take `windowID string` since `260529-chgz-window-id-routing`; create stays session-scoped). `260529-jad6` also removed `KillPane(paneID)` from the interface (zero call sites) and added `SelectWindowInSession` for the session-scoped REST `/select`. `NewRouter()` wires production implementations; `NewTestRouter()` accepts mocks (including hostname). Enables `httptest.NewRecorder` tests without live tmux. (`260312-r4t9-go-backend-api`)
- **Hostname via health endpoint (not a dedicated endpoint)** ‚Äî hostname is an OS-level value computed once at startup and stored in `Server` struct. Exposed via `/api/health` response (adding a field to an existing endpoint) rather than a new `GET /api/hostname` route. Minimal surface area, consistent with the single-port architecture. (`260320-uq0k-hostname-browser-title`)
- **Per-window fab enrichment via `fab pane map` (replaces per-session file reading)** ‚Äî Single `fab pane map --json --all-sessions` subprocess call per SSE tick replaces per-session `.fab-status.yaml` + `.fab-runtime.yaml` file reads. Provides per-window resolution (each worktree window shows its own change/stage) instead of per-session (all windows inherited session-level state). Decouples from internal file formats. `internal/fab` package deleted entirely. The subprocess invokes the `fab` router on PATH (not a hardcoded kit binary path) with `cmd.Dir = repoRoot` so the router can resolve the project's `fab_version` from `fab/project/config.yaml`. (`260313-3vlx-pane-map-enrichment` introduced pane-map enrichment via the then-in-repo `fab-go` binary; `260417-5nok-fix-sidebar-fab-state` migrated to the router after the binary was removed from the repo. Supersedes `260312-r4t9-go-backend-api` and `260313-txna-rich-sidebar-window-status` decisions)
- **Backend settings file over localStorage-only** ‚Äî `~/.rk/settings.yaml` via `internal/settings/` package + `GET/PUT /api/settings/theme` endpoints. Survives browser cache clears, works across devices accessing the same server. localStorage kept as synchronous cache for instant reads before API responds on page load. Simple `key: value` text parsing (not yaml.v3) ‚Äî one field currently, avoids re-adding a heavyweight dependency. Settings are global (not per-server, no `?server=` param). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **Full ANSI palette over minimal color set** ‚Äî 22 canonical terminal colors per theme enables three consumers from one source: CSS (8 derived colors via `deriveUIColors`), xterm.js (full 22-color theme via `deriveXtermTheme`), and tmux (auto-themed via ANSI colour indices in static tmux.conf). Rejected: 8-color model with separate xterm colors (duplicative, inconsistent). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **Static tmux.conf with ANSI indices over runtime `tmux set -g`** ‚Äî tmux.conf uses `colour0`-`colour15` indices. Changing xterm.js palette auto-themes tmux chrome (status bar, pane borders, pane-border-format). Zero backend involvement for theme switching. Rejected: runtime tmux commands (complex, fragile, requires backend communication). (`260323-7wys-ansi-palette-theme-rework`)
- **`run-kit.yaml` at git root for per-project preferences (not env vars or server config)** ‚Äî `config.FindGitRoot()` walks up from `pane_current_path` to locate the git root, then reads/writes `run-kit.yaml` there. Session color is a per-project user preference, not server configuration (which uses env vars per constitution). Previous `run-kit.yaml` (removed 2026-03-13) stored port/host config ‚Äî this reintroduction serves a different purpose. File is gitignored by convention. Simple line-by-line parsing (no yaml.v3 dependency). (`260416-jn4h-session-window-color-tinting`)
- **Dual storage: `run-kit.yaml` for session color + tmux `@color` for window color** ‚Äî Session colors need persistence across tmux restarts (file-based). Window colors are ephemeral and tmux-native (user options survive session lifetime but not server restart). Rejected: all in `run-kit.yaml` (would require tracking per-window state in a file, complex synchronization with tmux window lifecycle). (`260416-jn4h-session-window-color-tinting`)
- **Separate SSE event type for metrics (`event: metrics`) over embedding in sessions payload** ‚Äî Metrics are server-wide (one payload for all clients), while sessions are per-tmux-server and deduplicated. CPU samples change every tick (dedup logically impossible). Separation avoids inflating session payloads and allows independent evolution. Rejected: embedding in sessions payload (sent N times per server, complicates dedup). (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **Server-side ring buffer with full history per tick over client-side accumulation** ‚Äî New SSE clients immediately get complete 60-sample CPU sparkline history. No reconnection logic needed to rebuild history. At 60 float64s, ~500 bytes per tick is negligible. Rejected: client-side accumulation from deltas (reconnection complexity, frontend state management). (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **Path-based reverse proxy over subdomain routing** ‚Äî `/proxy/{port}/*` keeps all traffic on one origin, avoiding CORS complexity and DNS configuration. Per-port `ReverseProxy` instances cached in `sync.Map` (read-heavy, single-digit entry count). `ModifyResponse` rewrites localhost/127.0.0.1 URLs in HTML `src`/`href`/`action` attributes to proxy paths; handles gzip decompression. JS-constructed URLs are not rewritten (acceptable v1 gap). Rejected: subdomain routing (requires DNS/hosts setup), service worker injection (fragile). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`)
- **Tmux user-defined options for iframe state over database/config file** ‚Äî `@rk_type` and `@rk_url` as tmux window options preserve constitution principles II (no database) and VI (sessions survive restarts). State is co-located with the tmux window lifecycle ‚Äî kill the window, lose the metadata. Reactive via existing SSE polling (no new transport). Rejected: database/config file (violates constitution), window name encoding (fragile). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`) **`@rk_type` demoted from identity to a default-view HINT (`260714-t97o-web-view-lens`)** ‚Äî under the window-view lens model (`docs/specs/window-views.md` R1/R5, `ui-patterns.md` ¬ß Window Views (Lens Model)), "which view am I in" is per-viewer client state (`?view=` + localStorage), NOT the window's identity. `@rk_type=iframe` now only seeds `defaultView` ("default view = web" when `@rk_url` is also set); the frontend no longer reads it as a render gate and no longer mutates it on a view switch. `@rk_url` stays global substrate state (the shared content address, edited via the web lens's URL bar). Both options and the `POST /options` plumbing are otherwise unchanged (no backend/API change).
- **Extend existing create endpoint with optional rkType/rkUrl over new endpoint** ‚Äî Adding optional `rkType`/`rkUrl` to `POST /api/sessions/{session}/windows` reuses the existing creation flow. When `rkType` is present, uses `CreateWindowWithOptions` for atomic `\;`-chained tmux command (prevents SSE seeing window before metadata set). When absent, behavior unchanged (standard terminal window). Rejected: separate `POST .../windows/iframe` endpoint (unnecessary surface area). (`260416-6b0h-iframe-proxy-windows`)
- **procfs direct reading over external monitoring tools** ‚Äî `internal/metrics` reads `/proc/stat`, `/proc/meminfo`, `/proc/loadavg`, `/proc/uptime` directly. No dependency on `top`, `htop`, or monitoring agents. `syscall.Statfs` for disk. All readers return zero values on non-Linux (macOS dev graceful degradation). No new Go dependencies. (`260411-z63r-sidebar-host-window-panels`)
- **In-memory PR-status collector with wholesale-rebuild cleanup + network-isolated three-layer split** ‚Äî `internal/prstatus.Collector` (mirroring `internal/metrics.Collector`) makes ONE batched `gh api graphql viewer.pullRequests(states: [OPEN, MERGED, CLOSED], orderBy: UPDATED_AT DESC, first: 100)` call on a slow 90s background tick, REPLACES its `byNumber` map wholesale each refresh, and serves a deep-copied `Snapshot()`. Three layers on separate cadences keep the 2.5s SSE hot path network-free: (1) `PrURL`/`PrNumber` flow from `fab pane map` (filesystem, cheap) via the existing sessions enrichment join **[superseded by `260705-dmex`: `PrURL`/`PrNumber` are now derived from the pane's branch via the `prstatus` background branch refresher ‚Äî register + snapshot-join, still off the hot path ‚Äî see ¬ß Branch‚ÜíPR Derivation and the next decision]**; (2) the collector fetches live status behind the 90s tick + on-demand POST; (3) the SSE hub joins status onto change-bound windows via a pure `Snapshot()` read **[superseded by `260705-dmex`: the change-bound gate is dropped ‚Äî any window with a derived `PrURL` gets the join; the join key is the canonical URL, not the number]**. *Why include MERGED/CLOSED, not just OPEN*: a just-merged PR is recently updated, so it sits near the top of the `UPDATED_AT DESC` window and shows its `merged` (purple) state instead of dropping to a bare PR number ‚Äî the merged dot is reachable and is the most useful signal on a change-bound window. *Why wholesale rebuild*: the `first: 100` recency cap is the eviction ‚Äî a merged/closed PR shows its terminal state while it stays in the top-100 window, then ages out and drops from the next wholesale rebuild (along with killed windows) ‚Äî cleanup for free, no eviction logic or window-lifecycle hook (the deciding factor when "how does cleanup happen?" was raised in design). *Why GraphQL not `gh search prs`*: the intake's literal `gh search prs --author @me` argv ERRORS ‚Äî that subcommand doesn't expose `statusCheckRollup`/`reviewDecision` JSON fields; `gh api graphql` is the standard cross-repo batched mechanism and serves the identical one-call/O(1)/full-status intent (apply-time correction, plan Assumptions #8). *Why in-memory not tmux-option*: re-derivable in one call (Constitution ¬ßII ‚Äî no DB/disk/tmux-option); restart-survival has little value for a 90s cache and a tmux-option would add a two-writer race + manual pruning. *Why injectable `ghExec`/`available` seams*: matches the codebase's exec-seam test pattern, lets table tests stub `gh` output deterministically. *Rejected*: per-PR `gh pr view` polling (doesn't scale ‚Äî 10 tasks = 10 calls), webhook receiver writing `.status.yaml` (overkill, contradicts fab-kit's poll-free design). gh absent/unauth is a silent no-op (matches `command -v rk`). (`260610-596o-pr-status-sidebar`)
- **Two-tier agent-state + branch-derived PR links (own-your-signals over consuming `fab pane map`)** ‚Äî run-kit stops consuming Claude-only, fab-root-coupled signals through `fab pane map` and derives them itself: agent lifecycle state (Tier 2) reads the `@rk_agent_state` pane user option written by any harness's hooks (Tier 1 ‚Äî change/stage ‚Äî stays fab's), and PR links are derived server-side from the pane's branch. *Why*: the most notification-worthy state (`waiting` ‚Äî blocked on a human) was invisible in the old two-state `active|idle` model, non-Claude agents showed nothing, and PR visibility was limited to fab-change-bound windows; per constitution Principle X (amended here) hooks carry only the underivable, so PR links (derivable from the branch) must NOT ride a push pipeline. *Reconciler at parse-time*: the shell-command reconciler runs in `internal/tmux.parsePanes` (which already has the pane command + option value on one line) ‚Äî colocated + unit-testable, mirroring the pure-parse convention; rollup/duration live in `internal/sessions`. *Branch‚ÜíPR is a NEW per-`(repoDir,branch)` resolver alongside the viewer-wide URL-keyed collector, not a replacement*: the existing `gh api graphql viewer.pullRequests` query has no branch/repo/cwd seam so it cannot express `gh pr list --head`; the two compose (derive URL ‚Üí join live status by URL). *Rework (T007/T008)*: the resolver was moved OFF the FetchSessions/SSE hot path into a background `BranchRefresher` (register + snapshot-join) after review flagged inline `gh` execution breaking the zero-network-call invariant + the 5s API cap ‚Äî a shared process-wide `DefaultBranchRefresher` + package-level `Register`/`SnapshotBranchPR` fa√ßade keeps `FetchSessions`' signature unchanged. *Clean swap, no dual-source fallback*: agent columns read `‚Äî` until `rk agent-setup` runs (single-operator rollout; fallback code contradicts ¬ßIV). *Explicit installer, not silent sync*: `rk agent-setup` shows a diff + confirm before mutating user-global config, idempotent marker-keyed merge, `--uninstall` (plus `--yes`/`-y` non-interactive consent and `--dry-run` preview, and a non-TTY refusal naming `--yes` ‚Äî added by `260717-c424-toolkit-standards-conformance`; full consent flow in [agent-state](agent-state.md) ¬ß `rk agent-setup`). *Rejected*: reconciling in `internal/sessions` (duplicates the shell-name set); extending the single graphql query for branch‚ÜíPR (no scoping seam, misses non-viewer PRs); silent hook sync (surprising for user-config mutation). Full design: [agent-state](agent-state.md), spec [`docs/specs/agent-state.md`](../../specs/agent-state.md). Unblocks fab-kit backlog `[ioku]` (fab pane send/map become convention readers). (`260705-dmex-generic-agent-state-tier`)
- **Web update-notify + one-click upgrade: SSE-cached-slot detection + wrap `rk update`, no new deps/routes/DB** ‚Äî the daemon polls the GitHub Releases API (`internal/updatecheck`, one unauthenticated GET every ~6h) and, on a qualifying minor/major bump, broadcasts a server-global `event: update-available`; the running version rides a set-once `event: version` slot; a `POST /api/update` validates (brew marker + pending update) then spawns a **detached** `rk update`. *Why GitHub Releases API not `brew update`+`brew info` on a schedule*: the brew pair is heavyweight and mutates global brew state every run; a single JSON GET is effectively free and far under the 60/hr/IP unauth limit (user-decided, incl. the rejected alternative). *Why hand-rolled major/minor semver compare*: ~20 lines + a table test, and the repo already hand-parses versions (`parseBrewVersion`) with no semver dep ‚Äî patch-level never notifies (avoids nagging on bugfix churn). *Why SSE cached slots not a `GET /api/version`*: the two events reuse the exact `server-order`/`board-order` fan-out + cached-on-connect machinery (all clients incl. `?metrics=1`), and the SSE connect IS the moment the client needs the version ‚Äî a GET adds surface with nothing to poll (¬ßIV). The `version` slot is replay-on-connect-ONLY (the running version can't change mid-process). *Why wrap `rk update` via a detached spawn*: `rk update` already does brew detection + `brew upgrade` + `daemon.RestartWithBinary` (¬ßIII Wrap, Don't Reinvent); it CANNOT run in-process because the restart kills the serving process mid-request, so `POST /api/update` responds `202` then `exec.Command(self, "update")` with `SysProcAttr{Setsid: true}` (own session/process group, log ‚Üí `~/.rk/update.log`) ‚Äî **deliberately NOT `exec.CommandContext`-bound** because a detached child must outlive the server and ¬ßI's timeout rule only guards against a subprocess *blocking* the server, which a detached spawn cannot. *Why extract `internal/selfpath`*: the brew marker + self-path resolver were duplicated byte-for-byte in `upgrade.go` and `update.go` (unreachable cross-package `package main`/`package api`) ‚Äî the shared package means brew-install detection cannot drift between the CLI and web entry points (cycle-1 review should-fix). *Accepted*: the release-vs-tap-formula CI race (a click in the few-minute window before the formula lands yields "already up to date" ‚Äî no formula pre-verification); no in-flight lock (a second click harmlessly spawns another `rk update`); the write-only `Server.version` field (a review should-fix on new code, not a deletion candidate). *Rejected*: in-process upgrade (impossible ‚Äî restart kills the server); `GET /api/version` (needless surface); a semver dependency; Web Push for update notices (reserved for waiting agents ‚Äî update notices must not buzz phones, user-decided). Frontend: `useUpdateNotification()` hook + top-bar L3 UpdateChip + palette parity ‚Äî see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) ¬ß Update Notification. (`260713-4zap-update-notify-one-click-upgrade`)
- **Terminal relay mux (`/ws/terminals`) with per-stream queues + a fair scheduler ‚Äî one socket per tab, retire `/relay/{windowId}`, keep it SEPARATE from `/ws/state`** ‚Äî Change 2 of the socket-unification plan collapses N per-pane `/relay/{windowId}` sockets onto ONE `/ws/terminals` connection per tab (binary `[u32 BE streamId][payload]` data frames + JSON `open`/`opened`/`resize`/`close`/`closed` control ops; client-allocated u32 stream ids), so a board holds a fixed 2 WebSockets total (state + terminals). *Why per-stream bounded queues + a non-FIFO fair scheduler are a v1 requirement, not an optimization*: on a muxed socket a shared FIFO gives 1.66s interactive echo p50 under a co-stream flood, vs 32ms with per-stream queues + control/short-frame-priority round-robin at identical goodput (spike 2, `docs/findings/relay-mux-hol.md`) ‚Äî head-of-line blocking is the mux's one real risk and this fully mitigates it. *Why a full queue pauses the PTY reader (backpressure) rather than dropping bytes*: dropping mid-stream corrupts VT state;
