the pause pushes the stall into tmux's per-client buffering, the same mechanism a stalled per-pane TCP socket exerted before the mux. *Why stream-level failures become `closed` control events, not socket closes*: one bad window (4004) or attach failure (4001) must not tear down the other panes' streams ‚Äî the socket outlives any single stream. *Why retire `/relay/{windowId}` with no deprecation shim*: the frontend is the sole consumer (personal tool, no API-compat contract; constitution IV ‚Äî minimal surface). *Why keep it separate from `/ws/state` (D6, decided against merging)*: bulk binary terminal output must not share a send buffer/scheduler with state events ‚Äî the terminals scheduler is tuned for interactive-echo fairness under flood, a concern `/ws/state` does not have. *Why the async attach with a placeholder-under-lock (rework S2)*: the per-stream resolve (‚â§5s) + select + attach must not serialize on the socket read loop behind other panes' keystrokes/opens, so it dispatches to a goroutine after registering a placeholder stream synchronously, keeping duplicate-id/racing-resize/close deterministic. *Why `opened` rides the stream's own queue before data (rework M2)*: the client arms its deferred per-stream reset on `opened`, so a data-before-`opened` ordering wiped the reset; enqueuing `opened` on the stream's own bounded queue (channel FIFO + short-frame priority) guarantees opened‚Üídata. *Rejected*: shared FIFO across streams (the 1.66s regression); merging into `/ws/state` (D6); dropping bytes on a full queue (VT corruption); a bespoke window-ID validator (would reintroduce the #205 drift ‚Äî the mux reuses `validate.ValidateWindowID`). Frontend `RelayMux` singleton + `TerminalClient` port ‚Äî see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) ¬ß Terminal Relay (frontend). (`260717-803u-relay-mux`)
- **Chat live stream as a `kind:"chat"` subscription on `/ws/state`, backfill demoted to the GET (D5), chat SSE retired (D2) ‚Äî the socket-unification goal state (2 WS + 0 SSE, D6)** ‚Äî Change 3 of the socket-unification plan moves chat's incremental stream off its dedicated per-view `EventSource` (`GET /api/windows/{id}/chat/stream`) onto the state socket as one more subscription kind, subscribed on chat-lens enter / unsubscribed on leave. Chat was the app's LAST `EventSource` ‚Äî one HTTP/1.1 pool slot on plaintext origins, the exact starvation class socket-unification exists to eliminate; retiring it takes every route to a **fixed 2 WS + 0 SSE**. *Why demote backfill to the existing `GET /api/windows/{id}/chat` (D5), not snapshot-in-ack*: a rotation can target a large resumed session (`claude --resume` re-stamps `@rk_chat`), so pushing a `Conversation` over the shared socket would head-of-line-block session-state events and break bounded-event-size; the GET gains an additive byte `offset` and the subscribe carries `from:<offset>`, so `GET(offset)‚Üísubscribe(from)` composes gap-free/duplicate-free via the byte-offset-tailed JSONL adapter (no client id-dedup overlap window). *Why a per-subscription producer goroutine, not the poll set*: transcript appends generate no tmux events (the recorded reason chat was ever a dedicated stream), so chat cannot ride the tmux poll routing; it owns a `chatProducer` (TAIL/DORMANT machine, ~2s re-resolve) tracked separately from `subs`. *Why rotation goes DORMANT and never re-tails from 0 (rework MUST-FIX)*: re-tailing a rotated-to ref from `from:0` re-streams a whole conversation over the socket and the early `chat-reset` 404-wedges the client's re-compose; going dormant + gating the single `chat-reset` on the rotated-to transcript existing fixes both and preserves lazy-transcript not-yet tolerance. *Why `TailFrom` supersedes the self-priming `Tail`*: `Tail`'s first-`Reset`-with-`Conv` contract existed only for the SSE `chat-backfill`; with backfill on the GET, keeping it is dead code. *Retired*: `handleChatStream`, the `chatStream` struct + `run`/`reresolve`/`subscribe`, `emitChatUpdate`, `writeSSE`/`writeSSEJSON`/`writeSSEError`, `sseHeartbeatPeriod`/`maxLifetime`, and the adapter `Tail` method. *Untouched*: the GET backfill (beyond the offset field), POST chat/send + probe/lock, `POST /keys`, the parser/schema. *Rejected*: snapshot-in-ack / full backfill on `chat-reset` (unbounded event size, D5); merging `/ws/state`+`/ws/terminals` (D6). Frontend `use-chat-subscription.ts` (successor to the deleted `use-chat-stream.ts`) ‚Äî see [ui-patterns](/run-kit/ui-patterns.md) ¬ß Chat View and [chat](/run-kit/chat.md) ¬ß Live stream. *Residuals (recorded at hydrate, non-blocking)*: a swallowed subscribe `error` frame wedges the lens un-acked until a lens toggle / socket reconnect (should-fix, OPEN); byte offsets carry no file identity (a rotation landing on an existing longer transcript at a coincident line boundary can tail a different conversation with no reset ‚Äî record-only); chat frames route by `windowId` alone client-side, so a stale cross-server frame can briefly route into the wrong lens, self-healing on backfill REPLACE (record-only). (`260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`)
- **`currentWindowEverSeen` gate on kill-redirect over unconditional "gone ‚Üí redirect"** ‚Äî The redirect in `app.tsx` that fires when `currentSession` or `currentWindow` is null treats every SSE payload as authoritative by default, but the first payload after a navigation is not: the SSE hub can replay a cached snapshot before delivering fresh data, and tmux window-list enumeration can lag by one poll tick when a session was just created. Unconditionally redirecting on either transient state tears down `TerminalClient` mid-mount. The gate (a ref keyed on `${server}|${session}|${window}`, flipped true the first time `currentWindow` resolves non-null, reset on URL change) defers the redirect until the URL target has been observed as valid at least once. Rejected: inspecting SSE payload identity or delaying `isConnected` (both push complexity into the hub layer and would not distinguish real kills from stale catch-up). Rejected: adding a fixed startup debounce (arbitrary delay, races with fast tests). The gate preserves fast-redirect behavior for genuine kills (seen flag stays true after first valid observation) while eliminating the startup race. (`260417-g9uo-mobile-tap-focus-regression`)
- **CSS Grid topology for the rotated shell over nested flex** ‚Äî The shell rotation makes the sidebar a column that spans all three rows (topbar, content, bottombar). Expressing "sidebar full-height; right column is a 3-row stack" with nested flex requires either a sibling sidebar with explicit height management plus a flex-col right column, or a 2-row layout with sidebar nested inside row 1 ‚Äî neither matches the visual model and both diverge as future cells are added. Grid encodes the topology directly via `grid-template-areas: "sidebar topbar" "sidebar content" "sidebar bottombar"`; collapse becomes a one-line column-width change (`${sidebarWidth}px 1fr` ‚Üî `0 1fr`) animatable as a single `grid-template-columns` transition. Modern browsers (Safari 14+, Chrome 100+) animate `grid-template-columns` reliably. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Sidebar collapses to 0px, not a 48px rail** ‚Äî Maximum content width when collapsed, accepting a small visual layout shift on toggle (the hamburger appears to "move" from sidebar-adjacent to page-adjacent, though structurally it always lives at TopBar.left ‚Äî see next decision). Rejected: a 48px icon rail (VS Code/Linear/Slack convention) ‚Äî avoids the visual relocation but consumes content width for a usability gain that diverges from the user's stated preference for max content width. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Hamburger statically rendered at TopBar.left** ‚Äî Makes the visual relocation on collapse a free side effect of the grid column collapsing ‚Äî no component-level relocation logic, no conditional mount/unmount, no animation orchestration. The hamburger's home is always TopBar.left; the column is what changes. Rejected: state-conditional placement (hamburger inside sidebar when open, inside topbar when closed) ‚Äî adds a state-dependent component-tree mutation that complicates focus management and adds animation responsibility. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Single `sidebarOpen` boolean over `sidebarOpen + drawerOpen`** ‚Äî The pre-rotation distinction between "sidebar open on desktop" and "drawer open on mobile" was a rendering-form difference, not a state difference. The user's intent ("show me the sidebar") is one boolean; the renderer picks the form (grid column vs absolute overlay) by viewport width. Collapsing the two booleans simplifies persistence (one localStorage key, `runkit-sidebar-open`), removes a class of "they're out of sync" bugs, and makes the keyboard chord a single state mutation. Rejected: keep two booleans ‚Äî preserves a historical artifact at the cost of doubled persistence/reset logic and a confusing surface for new contributors. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **`<Shell>` as a shared wrapper over per-route shell components** ‚Äî Both AppShell and BoardPage need the identical 3-row √ó 2-column grid, sidebar collapse, mobile overlay, and visual-viewport handling. A single `<Shell>` (`src/components/shell/shell.tsx`) lets both routes consume a uniform topology by wrapping children in `style={{ gridArea: "sidebar" | "topbar" | "content" | "bottombar" }}` elements; collapse animation, mobile overlay, and the topbar/content/bottombar geometry stay in one place. Rejected: per-route shell components ‚Äî guaranteed to diverge over time (different collapse timings, drift in mobile overlay handling), defeats the rotation's "one topology, many routes" goal. Pattern note: future routes that need the same chrome should adopt `<Shell>` rather than reimplementing the grid. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **`FocusedTerminalContext` as a separate, dedicated context (not a slice of ChromeContext)** ‚Äî When BottomBar moved up to shell-level, it needed a way to target the focused terminal regardless of route. Folding the focused-terminal target into ChromeContext would mix UI state (sidebar open, fixed-width) with terminal-WS state and force every Chrome consumer to re-render whenever focus changes. A small dedicated context with its own provider (`FocusedTerminalProvider` mounted in `RootWrapper`) keeps the dependency narrow: only BottomBar and the ComposeBuffer-rendering TerminalClient subscribe. Compose state (`composeOpen` / `setComposeOpen`) was lifted to the same context so the shell-level BottomBar can open compose for the focused pane on the board route ‚Äî alternative was lifting `<ComposeBuffer>` itself to shell level, which would have required rewiring the file-upload chain (`composeFiles`/`composeInitialText`/`useFileUpload`) across 3-4 components. Frozen-target semantics are preserved because `compose-buffer.tsx` already snapshots `wsRef` on mount; only the focused pane's `TerminalClient` renders ComposeBuffer at any time. Pattern note: future multi-input UIs that need a single shared input target should follow this "lift focused-input target to context" pattern rather than prop-drilling. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Read-only setter pair for in-memory + persisted state (`setSidebarWidth` + `persistSidebarWidth`)** ‚Äî Drag-resize fires per-pointermove (potentially 60+ events per second). Persisting on every event would write localStorage 60 times per second per drag ‚Äî unnecessary I/O and cache thrash. Splitting the dispatch into `setSidebarWidth(width)` (in-memory state) and `persistSidebarWidth(width)` (localStorage write) lets the drag handler call the cheap one in the loop and the expensive one once at drag-end. Convention note: future state with the same shape (live in-memory updates + final commit to persistence) should follow this two-setter pattern rather than debouncing inside the dispatch (which couples state lifecycle to a timing heuristic). (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Mobile sidebar overlay positioned via grid (`gridRow: "2/4"`), not `fixed inset-0`** ‚Äî The spec's literal phrasing was `fixed inset-y-0 left-0 z-50`, but the project convention recorded in `fab/project/context.md` and the existing `mobile-layout.spec.ts` assertion (`sidebarBox.y > 0`) requires the mobile overlay to leave the topbar visible ‚Äî the topbar has the hamburger which closes the overlay, so covering it would be a usability regression. The implementation uses a grid-row-spanning child with `position: absolute` (not `fixed`) so the overlay anchors below the topbar inside the Shell. Pragmatic resolution: spec-wording "fixed-position overlay with backdrop" is satisfied ‚Äî the overlay is fixed-position-style (absolute inside the Shell that itself is full-viewport), it has a backdrop, it carries `role="dialog" aria-modal="true"`. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)
- **Known follow-up ‚Äî `sidebarChildren` prop duplication on `<Shell>`** ‚Äî Both `AppShell` and `BoardPage` build the sidebar JSX once into a local `sidebarElement`, then pass it as `<Shell sidebarChildren={...}>` (used on mobile overlay) AND wrap it in a desktop-branch `<aside style={{gridArea:"sidebar"}}>{sidebarElement}</aside>` (used on desktop). This duplicates a small bit of JSX at every Shell consumer. Considered alternatives: a render-prop or a single named "sidebar" slot owned by Shell. The desktop branch in AppShell also includes the drag-handle aside wrapper, which BoardPage does NOT need ‚Äî collapsing the duplication requires either (a) Shell knowing about the drag handle (small abstraction leak) or (b) exposing a separate "desktopChrome" slot. Captured here as a deferred refactor ‚Äî not in 17m3's scope. (`260509-17m3-rotated-shell-layout`)

## Testing

### Go Unit Tests

Go `testing` package with table-driven tests. Test files co-located with source using `_test.go` suffix. Test scripts: `go test ./...` from `app/backend/`.

Current Go test coverage (`app/backend/`):
- **Internal packages**: `internal/validate` (input validation + tilde expansion + filename sanitization), `internal/config` (env var reading, port validation, defaults), `internal/tmux` (listSessions parsing + byobu filtering, listWindows activity computation), `internal/sessions` (pane-map JSON parsing, per-window fab field join, graceful degradation on pane-map failure, `fab` router not on PATH via `TestFetchPaneMapFabNotOnPath`, end-to-end subprocess invocation via `TestFetchPaneMapIntegration` gated on `exec.LookPath("fab")`)
- **CLI command tests**: `cmd/run-kit/root_test.go` (no-args defaults to serve), `cmd/run-kit/version_test.go` (version output format), `cmd/run-kit/doctor_test.go` (LookPath-based dependency check)
- **Handler integration tests**: `api/health_test.go`, `api/sessions_test.go`, `api/windows_test.go`, `api/directories_test.go`, `api/upload_test.go`, `api/sse_test.go`, `api/spa_test.go` ‚Äî all use `httptest.NewRecorder` with the chi router and mock `SessionFetcher`/`TmuxOps` interfaces for tmux isolation. Cover response shapes, validation errors, URL param parsing, content-type enforcement. `api/terminals_ws.go` (the pane relay mux, `260717-803u-relay-mux`) has `api/terminals_ws_test.go`: the HOL scheduler test (`TestScheduler_EchoNotHeadOfLineBlocked` ‚Äî paced-writer seam, no real network) plus per-stream behavior against a live-tmux `/ws/terminals` dial (`opened` precedes data, initial-size attach + TERM forcing, resize, client-close‚Üí`closed` 1000, bad/missing window‚Üí`closed` 4004 with the socket still open). The 4001 attach-failure path has no dedicated test (forcing `StartWithSize` to fail needs a seam that does not exist ‚Äî accepted). `api/relay_test.go` was ported to these `/ws/terminals` equivalents (its `withRelayTmux`/`relayServerWithProdTmux` helper names outlived the retired endpoint ‚Äî a cosmetic-rename deletion candidate)

### Frontend Unit Tests (app/frontend/)

Vitest with jsdom environment. Config at `app/frontend/vitest.config.ts`. MSW mocks all API endpoints (`app/frontend/tests/msw/handlers.ts`). Test files co-located with source using `.test.{ts,tsx}` suffix. Since `260716-qf3j-state-socket`, `session-context.test.tsx` drives a `MockWebSocket` speaking the state-socket protocol (hello/subscribe/ack/event/gone) ‚Äî the former `MockEventSource` is retired; the behavioral assertions (per-server isolation, server-order re-sort, server-gone teardown, host-metrics dedup, `hostMetricsConnected` debounce, `serversLoaded`, `pendingServer`, `shouldReloadOnVersion`, StrictMode re-subscribe) are preserved.

Test coverage includes: sidebar (expand/collapse, window selection, kill session, activity dots, duration display, info popover), breadcrumb dropdowns (open/close, selection), drawer (open via hamburger, close on selection), command palette (Cmd+K), modifier state, touch targets (44px on `coarse`), API client (correct URL construction for each endpoint).

### Playwright E2E Tests (app/frontend/tests/e2e/)

Thin suite (3-5 tests) for API round-trip validation. Config at `app/frontend/playwright.config.ts`. Self-managed tmux sessions in `beforeAll`/`afterAll` hooks.

E2E test coverage: create/kill session via UI, state-socket delivers real data, sidebar navigation, sidebar window sync (external window creation/rename reflected within 5000ms, kill-then-create at same index does not suppress new window via stale optimistic context). Since `260716-qf3j-state-socket` (guard tightened by `260717-803u-relay-mux`, taken to its final form by `260717-vhvz-chat-on-state-socket`): a `connection-budget.spec.ts` guard asserts each route holds **‚â§ 2 WebSockets total ‚Äî 1 `/ws/state` + (0 or 1) `/ws/terminals`** (Host and bare-server routes hold only state; Terminal and Board routes add exactly one terminals socket) and **zero `text/event-stream` responses** ‚Äî **now including a chat-lens route case (`?view=chat`)** (`260717-vhvz`): the last `EventSource` is gone, so even a chat view is 2 WS + 0 SSE (the chat-lens budget case runs `?view=chat` on a window with no `@rk_chat`, so the lens falls back to tty ‚Äî documented in the `.spec.md`). Sockets are counted as opened ‚àí closed via each ws close event (a duplicate same-URL socket is detectable; Vite HMR WS excluded). `803u` replaced the per-pane `/relay/` classifier with a `/ws/terminals` classifier ‚Äî a board with N panes now shows ONE terminals socket, not N relay sockets. A shared `_state-socket-mock.ts` `routeWebSocket` helper (answering `hello`‚Üíglobal-replay + `subscribe`‚Üí`ack`, extended by `260717-vhvz` to answer a `kind:"chat"` subscribe with an ack carrying `offset` + optional `chat`/`chat-state`/`chat-reset` emits) backs the specs migrated off `page.route(...text/event-stream...)` mocks; `chat-view.spec.ts` dropped its `**/api/windows/*/chat/stream*` `text/event-stream` route mock for the extended state-socket mock + a plain `GET /api/windows/*/chat*` backfill `page.route` (`260717-vhvz`); `multi-server-sidebar:70` (the long-standing UNFIXED attachServer‚ÜíSSE flake) now passes DETERMINISTICALLY ‚Äî the subscribe/ack protocol structurally fixed the race. Acceptance A-014 (two board panes, one flooding, the other stays interactive ‚Äî the HOL scheduler in vivo) was verified via a throwaway e2e probe (echo ~421ms under a sustained ~10MB/s co-pane flood, the flood stream kept flowing, zero `closed`/socket churn), not a committed spec.

## Security

- All subprocess calls use `os/exec.CommandContext` with argument slices (never `sh -c` or shell strings)
- All `exec.CommandContext` calls include timeout via `context.WithTimeout` (10s tmux, 30s build). Terminal relay attach uses `context.WithCancel` (long-lived, cancelled on disconnect)
- User input validated via `internal/validate` before reaching any subprocess
- Directory listing restricted to `$HOME` via `ExpandTilde()` ‚Äî rejects `..` traversal, absolute paths outside home, and `~username` syntax. Symlinks under `$HOME` are not resolved (accepted risk for local dev tool)
- File uploads: filename sanitized via `SanitizeFilename()` (strips path separators, null bytes, leading dots, collapses dot sequences); 50MB size limit enforced server-side via `http.MaxBytesReader`; writes via `os.Create` (not subprocess)
- CORS: permissive by default (`*` origin) for multi-client API flexibility. TLS handled by Tailscale Serve in production
- Web Push: the VAPID private key (`~/.rk/vapid.json`) is written mode `0600` and is **never** returned to any client ‚Äî only the public key is served via `GET /api/push/vapid-public-key`. The subscribe/notify endpoints validate JSON shape and bound the request body (64 KiB); no subprocess execution is introduced by the push path (`260615-xd9r-web-push-notifications`)
